4 min
The Redundancy in the Answer and the Proper Concise Expression
Commentary on the redundancy in the answer phrase

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the commentator considers the wording of the answer to have a redundancy (استدراك) and what the concise expression should be.

Core Idea
The answer can be stated more simply without losing its force.

The commentator begins by noting an unnecessary elaboration in the answer. He points out that the full alternative phrasing is not needed; a briefer statement suffices. This lesson examines that critique and the intended concise form.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on redundancy
Read the opening Arabic sentence and its translation. Identify the comment about 'استدراك' (redundancy).
2
Understand the concise expression
The commentator says it suffices to say 'if you mean by complete cause...'. Understand why that is sufficient.
The rest of the alternative is implied.
3
Reflect on the benefit
Consider why the original answer might have been phrased as it was, and why the commentator sees it as redundant.
The commentator is not rejecting it, just noting a stylistic point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي عبارة الجواب استدراك؛ إذ يكفي أن يقال : إن أردت بالعلة التامة إلى آخره . ثم إن المتبادر مما نقله عن الحكماء وزيفه هو أن الفصل علة لوجود الجنس في الخارج، وذلك

تحققت
متنافيين، كان اللازم فصلاً واحداً، فيلزم الانحصار وإن نظر إلى أنه ليس فصل أولى من فصل كانت الأمور المتنافية لازمة لأمر واحد فلا يرد أن معنى استلزام العلة للمعلول أنه متى تحقق، لا أينما تحققت تحقق، فلا يلزم الانحصار وأن الواجب الواو بدل أو لأن اللازم كلا الأمرين. وأما على تقدير علية الفصل له فاللازم اقتضاء الأمور المتنافية لأمر واحد، ولا استحالة فيه، فتدبر؛ فإنه قد خفي على بعض الناظرين وما قيل : إن ما ذكره إنما يتم في الأجناس المتعددة الأنواع، لا في جنس منحصر في نوع واحد فمدفوع بأنه غير معلوم التحقق، لما عرفت من انحصار طريق معرفة التركب من الجنس والفصل في الاشتراك مع الغير في ذاتي والمخالفة آخر، ومادة النقض يجب أن تكون متحققة .

قوله : ( وأنها غير مستلزمة إلخ) أي من حيث ذاتها، فاستلزامها للمعلول في بعض الصور كالجزء الأخير، والشرط المساوي بواسطة استلزامه للعلة التامة لا ينافي ذلك . قوله : ( ولا يجب إلخ) زاد الوجوب مع أن المناسب للسابق واللاحق أن يقول : وإنها غير مستلزمة لمعلولها ؛ إشارة إلى أن المانع يكفيه الجواز، ودعوى عدم الاستلزام غصب .
قوله : ( وفي عبارة الجواب إلخ ) زاد لفظ العبارة إِشارة إلى أن المقدمتين المذكورتين لا بد من ملاحظتهما في الجواب؛ لأن الشق الأول من الترديد مبني على المقدمة الأولى، والشق الثاني على الثانية، إلا أنه لما كان تخصيص منع العلية على تقدير إرادة التامة والاستلزام على تقدير إرادة الناقصة، مشيراً إليهما ، كان في الجواب كفاية عن ذكرهما، ففي العبارة استدراك .
قوله : (مما نقله عن الحكماء وزيفه لم يعد الموصول في المعطوف؛ إشارة إلى أنه أمر واحد، وكون أحدهما علة وعدم علية الجنس يثبت علية الفصل صفتان يتبادر منه العلية
قوله : ( ولا يجب استلزامها (الخ وإن جاز كما في الجزء الأخير من العلة التامة، والعلة علة تامة للقريبة كالمبدأ الأول بالنسبة إلى العقل الثاني، فقوله : إنما المستلزم البعيدة التي هي معناه إنما المستلزم ،البتة وهي علة الوجوب الكلي، أو إنما المستلزم بلا واسطة .
And in the wording of the answer there is a redundancy; for it suffices to say: if you mean by complete cause... etc. Then what is understood from what he transmitted from the philosophers and refuted is that the specific difference is a cause of the existence of the genus in the external world, and that if [the consideration that the nature does not necessitate two things] is realized, then [if the opposite differences] are mutually exclusive, the necessary would be a single specific difference, so confinement follows; and if he considers that no specific difference is more deserving than another, then the mutually exclusive matters would be necessary for a single thing, so it is not refuted that the meaning of the cause's necessitating the effect is that when it is realized, it does not necessitate realization wherever it is realized, so confinement does not follow; and the required letter 'waw' is a substitute for 'or' because the necessary is both things. And upon the supposition of the specific difference's causality for it, the required is the entailment of mutually exclusive things for a single thing, and there is no impossibility in that; so reflect, for it has been hidden from some observers. And what was said: that what he mentioned is only complete for genera with multiple species, not for a genus confined to a single species, is refuted because its realization is not known, as you have known that the way of knowing composition from genus and specific difference is confined to sharing with another in an essential and differing in another, and the matter of refutation must be realized.

He said: (and that it does not necessitate etc.) i.e., from its own essence, so its necessitating the effect in some forms like the last part and the equal condition through its necessitating the complete cause does not contradict that. He said: (and it is not necessary etc.) he added the necessity although it would be appropriate for the preceding and following to say: and it does not necessitate its effect; indicating that the preventer is satisfied with permissibility, and the claim of lack of necessitation is usurpation.
He said: (and in the wording of the answer etc.) he added the word 'wording' to indicate that the two mentioned premises must be observed in the answer; because the first part of the alternative is based on the first premise, and the second part on the second; however, since specifying the denial of causality on the estimation of intending the complete cause and the necessitation on the estimation of intending the incomplete cause refers to them, the answer suffices without mentioning them, so in the wording there is redundancy.
He said: (from what he transmitted from the philosophers and refuted) he did not repeat the relative pronoun in the conjunction, indicating that it is a single matter; and that one of them being a cause and the genus not being a cause establishes the causality of the specific difference as two attributes from which causality is understood.
He said: (and it does not necessitate its effect etc.) although it is permissible as in the last part of the complete cause, and the cause is a complete cause for the proximate [effect] like the First Principle relative to the Second Intellect, so his statement: 'only the complete cause necessitates' the remote [effect] which means: only the complete cause necessitates absolutely, and it is the cause of universal necessity, or only the necessitator without mediation.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage contains further commentary on the answer given earlier. It begins by noting that the phrasing of the answer is somewhat redundant; a more concise expression would suffice. The commentator then clarifies that the intended meaning of the philosophers is that the specific difference is a cause of the existence of the genus in the external world. He discusses a nuance regarding necessitation: if the cause's necessitation means that whenever the cause exists the effect exists, then the argument that the genus would be confined to one species does not necessarily follow. He also addresses an objection that the argument only works for genera with multiple species, but refutes it by noting that the way to know composition from genus and specific difference is through commonality and difference, and the case of a genus confined to one species is not known to be realized. The remaining glosses further explain the incomplete cause, the wording of the answer, and the meaning of 'necessitation' in different contexts.

Key Terms
استدراك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the answer is incomplete or insufficient.
Correction: The commentator only points to a stylistic redundancy, not a flaw in the reasoning.

Checkpoint
What does the commentator mean by 'استدراك'?
A) The answer has a mistake.
B) The answer has unnecessary repetition.
C) The answer is too short.
D) The answer is unclear.

Key Takeaway
The answer's phrasing is slightly redundant; a shorter form suffices.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you explain your beliefs to others, do you sometimes add extra words that cloud the core message? How can you practice more concise and precise speech about your faith starting today?
?
This lesson shows that even scholars’ expressions can have redundancy. How does this humility about language affect your own attitude when you catch yourself using unnecessary words in discussing serious matters?
?
If you were to remove all 'istidrak' from your daily conversations about deen, what would you have to omit? Commit to one specific change in how you phrase a common Islamic concept this week.

Logic and Technical Terms

5 min
The Nuance of Necessitation: When the Cause is Realized vs. Wherever it is Realized
Clarification of the meaning of necessitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the subtlety in the meaning of a cause's necessitation, specifically that it means 'when the cause exists, the effect exists' not 'wherever the cause exists, the effect exists'.

Core Idea
Necessitation is about existential connection, not spatial or temporal universality.

The commentator clarifies an important nuance in the concept of necessary connection. Some might think that if a cause is necessitating, it must produce its effect in all circumstances. But the commentator explains that the correct understanding is that when the cause is realized, the effect is realized, not that wherever it is realized, the effect follows. This resolves an objection about confinement of the genus.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on necessitation
Read from 'ثم إن المتبادر...' to '...فلا يلزم الانحصار'
Focus on the phrase 'متى تحقق، لا أينما تحققت'.
2
Grasp the distinction
Understand the difference between 'when realized' (متى تحقق) and 'wherever realized' (أينما تحققت).
The first is about existential coincidence, the second about universal conditional.
3
See how it defeats confinement
If necessitation were 'wherever', then a cause that is a specific difference would necessitate all its effects everywhere, leading to confinement. But since it is 'when', it does not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي عبارة الجواب استدراك؛ إذ يكفي أن يقال : إن أردت بالعلة التامة إلى آخره . ثم إن المتبادر مما نقله عن الحكماء وزيفه هو أن الفصل علة لوجود الجنس في الخارج، وذلك

قوله : ( ولا يجب استلزامها (الخ وإن جاز كما في الجزء الأخير من العلة التامة، والعلة علة تامة للقريبة كالمبدأ الأول بالنسبة إلى العقل الثاني، فقوله : إنما المستلزم البعيدة التي هي معناه إنما المستلزم ،البتة وهي علة الوجوب الكلي، أو إنما المستلزم بلا واسطة .

Commentary
This passage contains further commentary on the answer given earlier. It begins by noting that the phrasing of the answer is somewhat redundant; a more concise expression would suffice. The commentator then clarifies that the intended meaning of the philosophers is that the specific difference is a cause of the existence of the genus in the external world. He discusses a nuance regarding necessitation: if the cause's necessitation means that whenever the cause exists the effect exists, then the argument that the genus would be confined to one species does not necessarily follow. He also addresses an objection that the argument only works for genera with multiple species, but refutes it by noting that the way to know composition from genus and specific difference is through commonality and difference, and the case of a genus confined to one species is not known to be realized. The remaining glosses further explain the incomplete cause, the wording of the answer, and the meaning of 'necessitation' in different contexts.

Key Terms
استلزام
علة تامة
علة ناقصة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that if X is a cause of Y, then X always and everywhere produces Y.
Correction: The correct understanding is that when X exists, Y exists, but this may not hold in all contexts due to additional conditions.

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what is the correct meaning of 'استلزام العلة للمعلول'?
A) Whenever the cause exists, the effect exists.
B) Wherever the cause exists, the effect exists.
C) The cause and effect are identical.
D) The effect exists without the cause.

Key Takeaway
The necessitation of a cause means the effect exists when the cause exists, not in every circumstance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you rely on a means (such as wealth, health, or knowledge) to achieve a result, do you assume that because the cause is present, the effect must follow? How does this lesson's clarification of 'when realized' versus 'wherever realized' challenge your assumption? What does it reveal about your trust in Allah versus your trust in means?
?
Think of a specific situation where you felt entitled to a certain outcome because you fulfilled what you thought were its causes (e.g., praying for guidance, studying hard, giving charity). Did you consider that those causes only necessitate the effect when the conditions set by Allah are met? How can you cultivate a deeper sense of tawakkul and humility in that area starting today?
?
This lesson teaches that necessitation is not absolute but conditional. In your own life, where do you tend to absolutize causes—making them into guarantees? Will you now begin to consciously phrase your expectations as 'if Allah wills' not just in words but in your heart? What is the first step you can take to reorient your reliance?

4 min
Refuting the Objection: Genus Confined to a Single Species
Refutation of an objection about genus confinement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that the argument about genus and specific difference only works for genera with multiple species, and how the commentator refutes it.

Core Idea
The objection is not sound because we cannot know if a genus is confined to a single species.

The commentator now addresses a counterargument: some might claim that the entire discussion about genus and specific difference only applies when the genus has multiple species; if the genus is confined to a single species, the logic fails. The commentator refutes this by pointing out that the way to know composition from genus and difference is through sharing and differing, and we cannot be certain that a genus is truly confined to one species.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the part starting from 'وما قيل : إن ما ذكره إنما يتم في الأجناس المتعددة الأنواع...'
2
Understand the refutation
The commentator says this objection is invalid because the realization of a genus confined to one species is not known.
He refers to the method of knowing composition through sharing and differing.
3
Reflect on the method
Consider why the method of genus-difference analysis requires multiple species to be applicable.
If there is only one species, we cannot distinguish genus from difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي عبارة الجواب استدراك؛ إذ يكفي أن يقال : إن أردت بالعلة التامة إلى آخره . ثم إن المتبادر مما نقله عن الحكماء وزيفه هو أن الفصل علة لوجود الجنس في الخارج، وذلك

He said: (and that it does not necessitate etc.) i.e., from its own essence, so its necessitating the effect in some forms like the last part and the equal condition through its necessitating the complete cause does not contradict that. He said: (and it is not necessary etc.) he added the necessity although it would be appropriate for the preceding and following to say: and it does not necessitate its effect; indicating that the preventer is satisfied with permissibility, and the claim of lack of necessitation is usurpation.
He said: (and in the wording of the answer etc.) he added the word 'wording' to indicate that the two mentioned premises must be observed in the answer; because the first part of the alternative is based on the first premise, and the second part on the second; however, since specifying the denial of causality on the estimation of intending the complete cause and the necessitation on the estimation of intending the incomplete cause refers to them, the answer suffices without mentioning them, so in the wording there is redundancy.
He said: (from what he transmitted from the philosophers and refuted) he did not repeat the relative pronoun in the conjunction, indicating that it is a single matter; and that one of them being a cause and the genus not being a cause establishes the causality of the specific difference as two attributes from which causality is understood.
He said: (and it does not necessitate its effect etc.) although it is permissible as in the last part of the complete cause, and the cause is a complete cause for the proximate [effect] like the First Principle relative to the Second Intellect, so his statement: 'only the complete cause necessitates' the remote [effect] which means: only the complete cause necessitates absolutely, and it is the cause of universal necessity, or only the necessitator without mediation.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage contains further commentary on the answer given earlier. It begins by noting that the phrasing of the answer is somewhat redundant; a more concise expression would suffice. The commentator then clarifies that the intended meaning of the philosophers is that the specific difference is a cause of the existence of the genus in the external world. He discusses a nuance regarding necessitation: if the cause's necessitation means that whenever the cause exists the effect exists, then the argument that the genus would be confined to one species does not necessarily follow. He also addresses an objection that the argument only works for genera with multiple species, but refutes it by noting that the way to know composition from genus and specific difference is through commonality and difference, and the case of a genus confined to one species is not known to be realized. The remaining glosses further explain the incomplete cause, the wording of the answer, and the meaning of 'necessitation' in different contexts.

Key Terms
جنس
فصل
نوع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the argument is invalid for genera with only one species.
Correction: The commentator says we cannot be sure such a genus exists; the objection lacks a real counterexample.

Checkpoint
Why does the commentator reject the objection about a genus confined to a single species?
A) Because such a genus is impossible.
B) Because its existence is not known.
C) Because the argument does not apply to it.
D) Because the objection is self-contradictory.

Key Takeaway
The objection that the argument fails for a genus with one species is refuted because such a case is not known to exist.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you object to an argument, do you first verify that the counterexample you have in mind is actually possible? This lesson exposes the danger of assuming something exists without proof. Can you recall a time you dismissed a truth because you thought of a hypothetical exception that you never checked?
?
The refutation turns on the method of knowledge: we cannot know a genus without comparison. In your own life, are there beliefs you hold simply because you never encountered a contrary case, without having a method to test them? How might that be leading you to error?
?
This objection seems plausible at first glance, yet it falls apart upon scrutiny. How many of your own objections to matters of faith or logic are equally based on assumptions you have not verified? Will you commit to examining the basis of your doubts before raising them?

The Objection that Differentia is a Cause for Genus and Its Answer
Al-Jurjani presents an objection and answers it by distinguishing complete and incomplete cause.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Jurjani answers the objection that the differentia is a cause for the genus by distinguishing between complete and incomplete cause.

Core Idea
Causality between genus and differentia is only incomplete, not complete.

In this passage, al-Jurjani presents a common objection: if the differentia is a cause for the genus, then undesirable consequences follow. He then provides a refined answer by clarifying the type of causality involved, distinguishing between a complete cause and an incomplete cause. This distinction preserves the logical relationships without leading to contradictions.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the passage from the beginning through the statement that the differentia is a cause for the genus. Note the two implied consequences that are claimed to be false.
2
Understand the answer's two-part structure
The answer distinguishes two meanings of 'cause': complete and incomplete. Notice that the answer addresses each meaning separately.
The author also notes a shortcut in the phrasing.
3
Identify the consequences of each interpretation
If the cause is complete, the genus-differentia relation would lead to confinement of the genus to one species and contradictory differentiate being necessary for one thing. If the cause is incomplete, these consequences do not follow.
4
Reflect on the author's concluding remark
Al-Jurjani notes that the answer could be simplified by only mentioning the complete cause interpretation. Consider why that might be sufficient.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الثاني - المقصد العاشر : وجوب حاجة بعض الأجزاء إلى بعض المتقابلة لازمة لشيء واحد، وكلاهما باطل . ( فالفصل علة للجنس ) وهو المطلوب . ( وأجيب عنه بأن المحتاج إِليه ) هو ( العلة الناقصة وأنها غير مستلزمة ) لمعلولها، ) فإن أردت بالعلة ( العلة ( التامة منعنا كون أحدهما علة للآخر، ( والحاجة) التي يجب ثبوتها بين الأجزاء ( لا تستلزمه ) أي كون أحدهما علة تامة للآخر، وهو ظاهر. ( وإن أردت ( بالعلة العلة ( الناقصة ؛ فلعل الجنس علة ) ناقصة للفصل، ولا يجب استلزامها المعلولها ، ( إنما المستلزم) للمعلول ( هي العلة التامة)، فلا يلزم انحصار ) الجنس في نوع ،واحد ولا كون الفصول المتقابلة لازمة لشيء واحد. وفي عبارة الجواب استدراك؛ إذ يكفي أن يقال : إن أردت بالعلة التامة إلى آخره .
The Second Observatory - The Tenth Objective: The Necessity of Some Parts Being in Need of Others. "The contradictory things are necessary for one thing, and both are false. (The differentia is a cause for the genus) and that is what is sought. (And it was answered about it that the thing in need) is (the incomplete cause and that it does not necessitate) its effect. So if you mean by the cause the (complete cause, we deny that one of them is a cause for the other. (And the need) that must be established between the parts (does not necessitate it), i.e., that one of them is a complete cause for the other, and that is apparent. (And if you mean) by the cause the (incomplete cause; then perhaps the genus is an incomplete cause for the differentia, and its necessitation of its effect is not necessary. (Only the one that necessitates) the effect (is the complete cause). So neither the confinement of the genus to one species nor the contradictory differentiate being necessary for one thing follows. And in the phrasing of the answer there is a supplemental remark; for it suffices to say: If you mean by the complete cause etc."
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its answer. The objection states that the differentia is a cause for the genus and that this causality is what is required. The answer replies by distinguishing between incomplete and complete cause. If the questioner means the complete cause, then we deny that one part is a complete cause for the other, because the need between parts does not entail complete causality. If the questioner means the incomplete cause, then it is possible that the genus is an incomplete cause for the differentia, and an incomplete cause does not necessitate its effect. Only the complete cause necessitates its effect. Therefore, the two consequences that were feared (confinement of the genus to one species or contradictory differentiate being necessary for one thing) do not follow. The author also notes that the phrasing of the answer contains a supplemental remark; it is sufficient to say 'if you mean the complete cause...'.

Key Terms
فصل (differentia)
جنس (genus)
علة تامة (complete cause)
علة ناقصة (incomplete cause)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any causal relation between genus and differentia implies that the differentia is a complete cause that necessitates the genus.
Correction: The answer shows that only an incomplete cause is needed; a complete cause is denied. Incomplete causality does not entail the feared consequences.

Checkpoint
According to the answer, what is the consequence of considering the differentia as a complete cause for the genus?
A) The genus is confined to one species.
B) The differentia is a complete cause and necessitates the genus.
C) We deny that one is a complete cause for the other.
D) The genus becomes indeterminate.

Key Takeaway
The differentia's causality to the genus is only incomplete, not complete, which avoids logical contradictions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Think of a recent argument—could it have been avoided if you had defined your terms? What step will you take this week to be more precise in your discussions?
?

Are you sometimes tempted to think that your actions are the complete cause of His mercy, rather than recognizing that they are only incomplete causes that need His grace? How will you remind yourself of your complete dependence on Him today?

Differentia: Mental Determinate of the Genus
Al-Jurjani clarifies the philosophers' statement on the differentia as mental determinate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophers' view that the differentia determines the genus in the mind, not externally, and why this distinction is important.

Core Idea
The differentia does not create the genus, it specifies it in the mind.

In this passage, al-Jurjani clarifies the correct position of the philosophers regarding the relationship between genus and differentia. He distinguishes between external causation and mental determination, a crucial distinction in logic and ontology. This lesson will guide you through the philosophers' statement and its proper interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
First, carefully read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Note how al-Jurjani begins by correcting a common misunderstanding.
The passage is dense with logical terminology.
2
Identify the two misconceptions refuted
The author refutes the idea that the differentia is a cause for the external existence of the genus, and also that it is a cause for the genus's existence in the mind. Find where these are mentioned.
These are both stated explicitly in the passage.
3
Understand the positive claim
The correct view is that the differentia makes the genus determinate in the mind (يحصله في العقل). Focus on the phrases 'تحصله بالفصل' and 'علة له يحصله في العقل'.
This is the core philosophical position.

And he said 'it would be better' because it could be said: The meaning of his statement 'And otherwise it would not be conceived etc.' is in the case where the genus is attained by a differentia from the differentiate in the mind without that differentia, while it is possible to ignore the differentia and the generic form remains. And the issue of concurrence does not arise, because the permissibility of concurrence means that each of the two causes is such that if...

Commentary
This passage clarifies the correct view of the philosophers regarding the relationship between genus and differentia. The author first states that what is commonly understood from the transmitted quote (that the differentia is a cause for the external existence of the genus) is contrary to the philosophers' principles. The correct view is what the philosophers actually said: the genus (الجنس) is an indeterminate (مبهم) thing in the mind, apt to be many species, and it is identical to each one in external existence, but it is not determinate as a complete quiddity of any species. Its determination (تحصله) is through the differentia (الفصل). When the differentia is joined, the genus becomes specified and determinate. Thus the differentia is a cause for the genus's determination in the mind (علة له يحصله في العقل), not a cause for its external existence, because the genus does not have a separate existence from the differentia externally. Nor is the differentia a cause for the genus's existence in the mind; otherwise the genus would not be conceived without any differentia. The author then provides comments on each part of the philosophers' statement, explaining that the correspondence between genus and species is between two known objects, not between knowledge and known. He also discusses the objection that if the genus is indeterminate and the species is determinate, then why is the genus considered indeterminate but the species not? He responds that the species is determinate relative to the genus, but it itself is indeterminate relative to its own accidents. Finally, he discusses a textual variant regarding the statement 'otherwise the genus would not be conceived without a differentia', suggesting it might be better to say 'otherwise the differentia would not be conceived without the genus', based on the permissibility of substitution of causes.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some hold that the differentia is an external cause for the genus's existence, like a physical cause bringing about a physical effect.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the differentia is only a mental cause for the determination of the genus in the mind, not an external cause for its existence.

Checkpoint

A) It brings the genus into external existence.
B) It makes the genus determinate in the mind.
C) It is the external cause for the genus's existence.
D) It removes the genus from the mind.

Key Takeaway
The differentia serves as a mental cause that determines the genus to correspond to a specific species, not as an external cause of its existence.

Genus and Differentia: Mental Causality Explained
The author refutes an objection by stating the philosophers' definition of genus and differentia.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the differentia is considered a cause for the genus only in the mind, according to the philosophers.

Core Idea
The differentia determines the genus in the mind, not in external existence.

In this passage, the author corrects a misunderstanding about the relationship between genus and differentia. He presents the philosophers' view that the genus is an ambiguous concept that becomes specific only through the differentia, and that this specification happens solely in the intellect. This distinction is crucial for understanding how logical concepts relate to external reality.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the full Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the key terms: genus (الجنس), differentia (الفصل), ambiguous (مبهم), determination (تحصيل).
The passage is dense with logical terminology.
2
Identify the correction
The author begins by saying a previous view contradicts the philosophers' principles. What is the correct view according to the philosophers?
The correct view is that the differentia determines the genus only in the mind.
3
Understand the definition of genus
The philosophers define genus as an ambiguous concept that can apply to many species. It is identical to each species in existence but not fully determinate.
Ambiguity here means it can apply to multiple species without being specific.
4
Examine causality
The differentia is a cause that makes the genus determinate in the mind. It does not cause the genus to exist externally because they are not distinct in external reality.
If they were distinct externally, there would be two separate things, which is not the case.
5
Reflect on the exception
The text notes that the differentia is not a cause for the genus in the mind in an absolute sense, because otherwise the genus could not be conceived without any differentia. But it can be conceived without a specific differentia.
This nuance prevents a misunderstanding about mental causality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مخالف لقواعدهم، إنما المطابق لها ما ذكره بقوله : (قال الحكماء: الجنس) أمر ( مبهم ) في العقل يصلح أن يكون أنواعاً كثيرةً، هو عين كل واحد منها في الوجود، وليس هو متحصلاً مطابقاً لماهية نوع منها بتمامها ، ( وإنما تحصله بالفصل)، فإنه إذا انضم الفصل إليه صار متعيناً ومتحصلاً . ( فهو ) أي الفصل (علة له يحصله في العقل) أي يجعله مطابقاً لتمام ماهية النوع، ويزيل إبهامه أي يعينه لنوع واحد من الأنواع التي كان صالحاً لكل واحد منها، فهو علة لتحصله وتعينه في الذهن، (لا أنه علة خارجية لوجوده؛ إذ ليس للجنس وجود مغاير لوجود الفصل في الخارج حتى يتصور بينهما علية، وليس الفصل أيضاً علة لوجود الجنس في الذهن، وإلا لم يعقل الجنس بدون فصل من الفصول.
It contradicts their principles; rather, what corresponds to them is what he mentioned by his saying: (The philosophers said: the genus is an ambiguous thing in the intellect that can be many species, it is the very same as each one of them in existence, and it is not determinate corresponding to the complete essence of any species, and its determination is only through the differentia). For when the differentia joins it, it becomes specific and determinate. So it, i.e., the differentia, is a cause for it that determines it in the intellect, i.e., makes it correspond to the complete essence of the species, and removes its ambiguity, i.e., specifies it to one species among the species for each of which it was suitable. So it is a cause for its determination and specification in the mind, not that it is an external cause for its existence; for the genus has no existence distinct from the existence of the differentia in the external such that causality between them can be conceived, nor is the differentia a cause for the existence of the genus in the mind, otherwise the genus would not be conceived without one of the differentiae.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer followed by a definition. The author first states that a certain view (that the differentia is a cause for the genus in the external) contradicts the philosophers' principles. He then says the correct view is what the philosophers themselves said: the genus is an ambiguous concept in the intellect that can apply to many species and is identical to each in external existence, but it is not determinate as a complete essence. Its determination comes only through the differentia. The differentia is a cause for the genus in the mind—it makes the genus correspond to the complete essence of the species and removes its ambiguity. However, it is not an external cause because genus and differentia are not distinct in external existence. Nor is it a cause for the genus in the mind in the sense that the genus cannot be conceived without any differentia; that would be false because the genus can be conceived without a specific differentia (but not without all differentiae—hence the exception).

Key Terms
الجنس
الفصل
العلة
الوجود الذهني
الوجود الخارجي
الإبهام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The differentia is an external cause for the existence of the genus.
Correction: The differentia only determines the genus in the mind; they are not distinct in external existence, so no external causality exists.

Checkpoint
According to the philosophers, what is the role of the differentia (الفصل) with respect to the genus (الجنس)?
A) It causes the genus to exist in the external world.
B) It determines the genus in the mind, making it correspond to a specific species.
C) It is identical to the genus in the mind.
D) It is the material cause of the genus.

Key Takeaway
The differentia determines the genus in the mind, not in external reality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
This lesson shows that the differentia 'determines' the genus only in the mind, not in reality. In your own life, are there mental distinctions you treat as absolute truths without realizing they are merely tools? Will you commit to examining one such distinction today?
?
The philosophers defined genus as 'ambiguous' until determined. Is there an area of your faith where you have settled for ambiguity in your understanding, relying on vague definitions rather than seeking precise knowledge? What step will you take this week to remove that ambiguity?

The Differentia as a Conceptual Determinant: The Example of Magnitude
The author illustrates the philosophers' view using the example of magnitude and its species.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the example of magnitude demonstrates that the differentia does not exist externally as a separate cause but rather determines the genus only in the mind.

Core Idea
The differentia is a mental determinator, not an external additive.

The author now provides a concrete example to illustrate the philosophers' position that the differentia is not an external cause. He uses the concept of magnitude (المقدار) to show that in external reality, a particular magnitude is exactly what it is—line, surface, or body—without any combination. The ambiguity arises only in the mind, where magnitude can potentially be any species, and it becomes determinate only when joined with a differentia. This example anchors the abstract discussion in a familiar geometrical context.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how the author uses the example of magnitude to clarify a logical point.
The passage builds on the earlier claim that the differentia is a cause for determination of the genus in the intellect.
2
Understand the example of magnitude
The author points out that magnitude is not a separate distinct thing in the external world that sometimes becomes a line, sometimes a surface, etc. Instead, each particular magnitude is inherently one of these species. Grasp this key point.
Contrast this with the idea that the differentia could be an external factor added to the genus.
3
Grasp the ambiguity of magnitude in the mind
In the intellect, the concept of magnitude is ambiguous—it can apply to line, surface, or body but matches none completely. It needs a differentia to become determinate. Recognize that this ambiguity exists only in the mind, not in external reality.
The differentia removes the mental ambiguity and makes the concept correspond to a specific external essence.
4
Identify the role of the differentia
The differentia, such as 'line-ness', is what determines magnitude in the mind. Without it, no specific form (linear, surface, or body) is obtained. See that the differentia is thus a cause only in the intellect, not externally.
This illustrates the philosophers' view that the differentia is not an external cause but a conceptual determinant.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا الذي ذكرناه من كون الفصل علة لتحصل الجنس وزوال إبهامه في العقل (بين) لا حاجة به إلى دليل اخترعه المتأخرون لهم، ( فإنه ليس المقدار ) مثلاً ( أمراً معيناً ممتازاً في الخارج ( يقترن به تارة كونه خطاً)، أي فصل الخط المميز إياه عن مشاركاته في المقدارية، (وتارة) كونه (سطحاً)، وتارة كونه جسماً تعليمياً، بل ثمة مقدار) مخصوص (هو) في نفسه (الخط ليس ذلك المقدار ) إلا الخط من غير أن يكون هناك شيئان يجتمعان في الخارج فيتحصل منهما الخط ( ومقدار) آخر ( هو السطح ليس إلا ) السطح ومقدار ثالث هو الجسم التعليمي ليس إلا . ( نعم المقدار ) أمر ( مبهم في العقل يحتمل كل واحد من الأنواع المندرجة تحته ولا يطابق تمام ماهية شيء منها، بل يحتاج في تحصله ومطابقته لتمام الماهية الموجودة في الخارج إلى أن يكون أحدهما ) بل أحدها، أي إلى أن يقترن به فصل واحد منها ليفرزه ويحصله فما لم يقترن به ) في العقل فصل من تلك الفصول (لم تحصل له الصورة الخطية ( المطابقة لماهية الخط الموجود في الخارج ، ( و ) لا الصورة (السطحية)، ولا الصورة الجسمية.
And this that we have mentioned—that the differentia is a cause for the determination of the genus and the removal of its ambiguity in the intellect—is clear, and there is no need for a proof devised by the later scholars for them. For magnitude, for example, is not a particular thing distinct in the external that is sometimes joined by its being a line—i.e., the differentia of the line that distinguishes it from its participants in magnitude—and sometimes by its being a surface, and sometimes by its being a teaching body. Rather, there is a specific magnitude that is in itself the line; that magnitude is nothing but the line, without there being two things that come together in the external and from them the line is produced. And another magnitude that is the surface is nothing but the surface, and a third magnitude that is the teaching body is nothing but it. Yes, magnitude is an ambiguous thing in the intellect that can take each one of the species subsumed under it and does not correspond to the complete essence of any of them. Rather, it needs for its determination and correspondence to the complete essence existing in the external to be one of them—i.e., to be joined with one differentia from among them to separate it and determine it. So as long as it is not joined in the intellect with one of those differentiae, the linear form corresponding to the essence of the line existing in the external is not obtained for it, nor the surface form, nor the body form.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage provides an illustrative example to clarify the philosophers' position. The author asserts that the explanation given—the differentia as a cause for the determination of the genus in the mind—is self-evident and does not require an elaborate proof invented by later scholars. He uses magnitude (المقدار) as an example. In external reality, a particular magnitude is either a line, a surface, or a teaching body (geometrical solid). There is no external thing called 'magnitude' that exists separately and then gets combined with another thing to become a line, etc. Instead, each magnitude is exactly what it is. The concept of magnitude in the intellect is ambiguous—it can apply to any of these species but matches none completely. It becomes determinate only when joined in the mind with a specific differentia, such as 'line-ness'. Without that differentia, no specific form (linear, surface, or body) is obtained in the mind. Thus, the differentia is a cause only in the mind, not in external existence.

Genus and Differentia Are One in External Existence
Demonstrates through quantity that genus is ambiguous and needs differentia in mind only

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand through the example of quantity that genus and differentia are not separate entities in external reality but are distinguished only in the mind.

Core Idea
Genus and differentia are one in reality, distinct only in thought.

This lesson uses a concrete example—the categories of quantity—to clarify a subtle logical point: how genus and differentia relate. The author shows that in the external world, there is no separate 'quantity' apart from specific quantities like line or surface; rather, the specific thing itself is both genus and differentia combined. This passage will help you grasp why the genus needs the differentia only in the mind, not in reality.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage once through, then read the literal translation. Focus on the overall argument before analyzing details.
The passage uses parentheses for inserted commentary; ignore them for now.
2
Understand the example of quantity
Notice that quantity (miqdar) is used as an example. The author says quantity is not a determinate thing externally; rather, specific quantities like line, surface, and solid exist as distinct individuals.
The differentia (e.g., line-ness) distinguishes the species within the genus.
3
Grasp the key claim: no external separation
The passage emphasizes that there are not two things (genus and differentia) that combine externally. Instead, the specific quantity itself is the line, etc. This refutes the idea that genus and differentia are separate in the world.
4
Appreciate the role of the mind
The mind sees quantity as ambiguous (mubham) and needs a differentia to form a specific concept. In reality, no such separation exists. This shows why the proof invented by later scholars is unnecessary.
The differentia 'realizes' (yuhassil) the specific form in the mind.

(For the quantity) for example (is not a determinate thing distinguished in external existence) (with which is conjoined sometimes its being a line), i.e., the differentia of the line distinguishing it from its partners in quantity-ness, (and sometimes) its being (a surface), and sometimes its being a solid body. Commentary
This passage provides a concrete example to illustrate the relationship between genus and differentia, specifically that they are not separate in external existence. It begins by stating the topic: the necessity of parts needing each other, here the genus needing the differentia. The author declares that the genus's ambiguity in the mind is clear and does not require the proof invented by later scholars. Using the example of quantity (miqdar), he explains that quantity is not a determinate thing externally; rather, specific quantities like line, surface, and solid exist as distinct things. In external reality, there is no separate 'quantity' entity apart from these specifics. In the mind, quantity is an ambiguous concept that requires a differentia (such as line-ness) to become determinate and correspond to a real essence. Without that differentia, no specific mental form (linear, surface, or solid) can be attained. Thus, the genus and differentia are one in external existence but distinct in the mind.

The Causal Relationship Between Differentia and Genus
Commentary on the causal relationship between differentia and genus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the differentia is considered the efficient cause of the genus in the mind and why the genus cannot be understood without a differentia.

Core Idea
The differentia is the cause that brings the genus into the mind, not the reverse.

This commentary delves into the causal relationship between differentia and genus, a key topic in logic. The author clarifies that the causality is efficient and that the differentia necessitates the genus in the mind, leading to the impossibility of the genus existing without a differentia. We'll explore the reasoning behind this and the implications for understanding definitions.

Guided Path
1
Read the Passage with Translation
Read the Arabic and literal translation simultaneously, noting technical terms like 'illa (cause), fasl (differentia), and jins (genus).
Pay attention to the commentator's glosses on the original text.
2
Understand the Core Claim
Identify the main claim: the differentia is the cause of the genus in the mind. Notice how the commentator argues that if this causality holds, the genus cannot be understood without a differentia due to the impossibility of two causes succeeding each other.
The commentator uses the principle of 'impossibility of succession' (imtina' al-tawarud) to reinforce the argument.
3
Distinguish Original and Later Proof
Observe the commentator's remark that the original philosophers held the claim of causality, while later scholars invented a proof. The commentator suggests we do not need to apply that proof.
This highlights a methodological point about relying on transmitted knowledge from the philosophers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتقرر قوله : ( بينهما علية أي بالفاعلية؛ إذ مطلق العلة الخارجية لا يقتضي وجود العلة فضلاً عن التغاير. قوله : ( وإلا لم يعقل إلخ ) كان الظاهر أن يقول : وإلا لم يعقل الفصل بدون الجنس؛ لأن العلة يستلزم وجود المعلول دون العكس؛ لجواز أن يكون معللاً بعلة أخرى، فلعله اختار ذلك لأن في عدم استلزام الفصل للجنس خفاء بناء على كونه خاصاً، والخاص يستلزم العام بخلاف العكس، ووجه صحته أنه إذا كان الفصل علة لوجود الجنس في الذهن لا يجوز أن يوجد فيه لعلة أخرى بناء على امتناع التوارد على البدل بعد تحقق إحداهما، فيلزم أن لا يعقل بدون فصل ما . قوله : ( لا حاجة به إلخ) فيه إشارة إلى أن المنقول الحكماء هو أصل المدعى، وهو الفصل علة للجنس، والدليل المذكور اخترعه المتأخرون ، فلا حاجة بنا إلى تطبيقه على هذا المعنى . قوله : ( فإنه ليس إلخ ) تصوير للحكم البين في جزئي للتوضيح . قوله : ( أي فصل لأن الكلام في الجنس والفصل، فالمراد بكونه خطأ ما هو سببه . قوله : (ليس ذلك إلخ) تأكيد لما قبله . قوله : ( شيئان يجتمعان) كما في البيت مثلاً. قوله : أي إلى أن يقترن إلخ) أي الكلام على الحذف بقرينة قوله : فما لم يقترن، والمراد بكونه أحدهما سببه . قوله : (ليفرزه) الإفرار باعتبار كونه مقسماً للجنس، والتحصيل باعتبار كونه مقوماً. وجد ابتداء وجد المعلول الشخصي به وأما إذا وجد المعلول بإحدى العلتين فلا يجوز أن توجد العلة الأخرى حينئذ كما سيجيء. وفيما صورناه إنما يكون من هذا الوجه الثاني الممتنع فتدبر.
And it is established that his statement: (between them is causality) i.e., efficient causality; for absolute external causality does not necessitate the existence of the cause, let alone the difference. His statement: (otherwise it would not be understood, etc.) The apparent would be to say: otherwise the differentia would not be understood without the genus; because the cause necessitates the existence of the effect but not the reverse; because it may be caused by another cause. Perhaps he chose that because in the non-necessitation of the differentia for the genus there is obscurity based on it being a specific, and the specific necessitates the general contrary to the reverse. The soundness of that is that if the differentia is the cause of the existence of the genus in the mind, it is not permissible that the genus exist in the mind due to another cause, based on the impossibility of succession (al-tawarud) of causes after one of them has occurred, so it follows that it cannot be understood without some differentia. His statement: (there is no need for it, etc.) points to the fact that what is transmitted from the philosophers is the original claim, that the differentia is the cause of the genus, and the mentioned proof was invented by later scholars, so we have no need to apply it to this meaning. His statement: (for it is not, etc.) is a depiction of the clear judgment in a particular case for clarification. His statement: (i.e., a differentia because the discussion is about genus and differentia, so what is meant by its being a line is its cause. His statement: (not that, etc.) is an emphasis on what preceded. His statement: (two things that come together) as in the house, for example. His statement: (i.e., to be conjoined, etc.) i.e., the speech is abbreviated with the indication of his statement: 'so as long as it is not conjoined,' and what is meant by its being one of them is its cause. His statement: (to separate it) al-ifrār (separation) in consideration of its being a divider of the genus, and al-tahṣīl (realization) in consideration of its being a constituent. If the beginning existed, the particular effect exists by it; but if the effect exists by one of the two causes, it is not permissible that the other cause exist then, as will come. And in what we have depicted, it is only from this second impossible aspect, so ponder.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage is a commentary explaining the causal relationship between differentia and genus. It begins by clarifying that the causality is efficient causality (bi-l-fi'liyya). The commentator then addresses the objection that if the differentia is the cause of the genus, then the genus cannot be understood without the differentia. He explains that the differentia as a specific necessitates the general, and if the differentia is the cause of the genus in the mind, the genus cannot have another cause because two causes cannot succeed each other for the same effect. Therefore, the genus cannot be understood without some differentia. The commentator also notes that the claim that the differentia is the cause of the genus is the original position of the philosophers, and the proof invented by later scholars is unnecessary. He then glosses various parts of the original text, explaining terms like 'separate it' (yufrizahu) as dividing the genus and 'realize it' (yuhaṣṣiluhu) as constituting it. Finally, he distinguishes between the case where the effect exists from the beginning due to the cause and the impossible case where the effect exists from one cause and then another cause appears.

Key Terms
علة
فصل
جنس
توار على البدل
خاص
عام
إفراز
تحصيل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the genus can exist in the mind without any differentia, or that the genus could be caused by something other than the differentia.
Correction: The passage argues that if the differentia is the efficient cause of the genus in the mind, it is impossible for the genus to exist due to another cause, and thus the genus cannot be understood without a differentia.

Checkpoint
What is the relationship between differentia and genus according to this commentary?
A) The genus is the cause of the differentia.
B) The differentia is the cause of the genus in the mind.
C) They are equal in causality.
D) There is no causal relationship.

Key Takeaway
The differentia is the efficient cause of the genus in the mind, making their conjunction necessary and the genus unintelligible without some differentia.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you learn a new concept, do you strive to identify its essential differentia—what makes it distinct—or are you satisfied with a vague, general understanding? How might this habit affect the depth of your knowledge?
?
This lesson shows that the genus cannot be understood without a differentia. In your own search for truth, are you careful to avoid accepting general ideas without their defining characteristics? Where might you be doing this without realizing it?
?
The passage emphasizes the impossibility of two independent causes for the same effect. Reflect on your beliefs: are you trying to base your faith on multiple conflicting sources, or have you committed to a single, coherent foundation? What would it take to resolve any contradictions?

The Unity of Genus and Differentia in External Existence
Clarifies that genus and differentia are one externally, with argument and example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why genus and differentia are not distinct externally and how this explains the predication of multiple terms on one individual.

Core Idea
Genus and differentia are one in external existence, not two separate things.

This passage from al-Mawaqif clarifies a key logical and metaphysical point: the terms we use to describe an individual, like 'human', 'animal', and 'rational', do not refer to separate external parts. The author argues that genus and differentia are united in external existence, and this unity is necessary for predication to be possible.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and the English translation carefully. Notice the logical flow: conclusion, argument, then clarification with example.
2
Identify the main claim
The passage begins by stating that genus and differentia have no distinction in external existence. They are united in existence and constitution. Identify this claim.
This is the central thesis.
3
Understand the argument
The passage provides an argument: if genus and differentia were externally distinct, they could not be predicated of each other as identical. Consider why this is the case.
Two externally distinct things cannot be said to be the same thing.
4
Analyze the further clarification
The author then explains that while the mental concepts of general and specific differ, their identity in external existence is one. The example of Zayd shows that he is all these things without multiplicity.
This resolves the apparent tension.
5
Reflect on the implication
If there were external multiplicity, predication would be impossible. Reflect on why this matters for logic and ontology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لك من هذا الذي صورناه في المقدار وأنواعه أنه ليس بين الجنس والفصل تمايز في الخارج بأن يكون للجنس وجود فيه والفصل وجود آخر، بل هما متحدان بحسب الخارج وجوداً وجعلاً. كيف والأمران المتمايزان بالوجود في الخارج لا يمكن حمل أحدهما على الآخر بهو هو، وإن كان بينهما أي اتصال فرضت كالملازمة والحلول في الهيولى والصورة. ولنزده زيادة تحقيق فنقول: العام له مفهوم غير مفهوم الخاص، ويتحصل مفهوم العام بالخاص كما تحققته فيكون له أي لكل واحد من العام والخاص صورة عقلية مغايرة لصورة الآخر، ولكن هويتهما في الخارج واحدة فلا تمايز بينهما في الخارج، بل في الذهن فقط فزيد هو الإنسان وهو الحيوان وهو الناطق، ولا تعدد في الخارج بأن يكون الحيوان موجوداً في الخارج، وينضم إليه موجود آخر هو الناطق، فيتحصل منهما ماهية الإنسان، ثم ينضم إلى هذه الماهية موجود آخر هو التشخص المخصوص، فيتحصل منهما زيد؛ إذ لو كان هناك تعدد خارجي لم يتصور حمل هذه الأشياء بعضها على بعض.
Thus from this which we have depicted about quantity and its types, [we conclude] that there is no distinction between genus and differentia in external existence such that the genus has an existence and the differentia another existence; rather, they are united according to external existence in existence and constitution. How? For two things distinguished by existence in external existence cannot be predicated of one another as identical, even if there is any connection assumed between them, like concomitance and inherence in matter and form. And for further clarification we say: the general has a concept other than the concept of the specific, and the concept of the general is realized by the specific, as you have realized. So each of the general and the specific has a mental form different from the form of the other, but their identity in external existence is one; there is no distinction between them in external existence, but only in the mind. Thus Zayd is the human, and he is the animal, and he is the rational. There is no multiplicity in external existence such that the animal exists externally and another existent, the rational, joins it so that the essence of human results from them; then an existent, the specific individuation, joins this essence so that Zayd results from them. For if there were external multiplicity, it would not be conceivable to predicate these things of one another.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage further clarifies the relationship between genus and differentia, emphasizing their unity in external existence. It begins by stating that from the example of quantity, it is clear that genus and differentia are not distinct externally; they are one in existence and constitution. The passage then argues that two things that are distinct in external existence cannot be predicated of each other as identical, even if they have some connection. For further clarification, it explains that the general and specific have different mental concepts, but their identity (huwiyya) in external existence is one. The example of Zayd illustrates this: Zayd is simultaneously human, animal, and rational, but this does not imply multiple external existents. If there were external multiplicity, predication of these terms on one subject would be impossible. Thus, the passage confirms the ontological unity of the genera and differentiae in individuals.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that predicating multiple attributes (e.g., animal, rational, human) on one subject implies that the subject is composed of multiple real external parts corresponding to each attribute.
Correction: The passage shows that these attributes are one in external existence; they are not separate parts. Zayd is one existent, and the predications refer to that same identity, not to distinct ontological components.

Checkpoint

B) Because they are one in external existence.
C) Because Zayd is a composition of these.
D) Because they are mental concepts only.

Key Takeaway
Genus and differentia are one in external existence; predication of multiple terms on one subject is possible only because of this unity.

Genus and Species: One in Existence
Proof that genus and species are one in external existence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why genus and species are considered one entity in external existence according to this kalam argument.

Core Idea
Genus and species are not separate in reality, only in the mind.

This passage from Sharh al-Mawaqif tackles a foundational logical question: Are genus and species distinct entities in the external world? The author argues they are not, and shows why their unity is necessary for predication. Let's follow his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its English translation to get the overall argument. Notice the technical terms like 'jins' (genus) and 'fasl' (specific difference).
2
Identify the main claim
The author states clearly that there is no distinction between genus and species in external existence. They are united in existence and constitution.
Look for the phrase 'لا تمايز بينهما في الخارج'.
3
Examine the proof from predication
The author argues that if genus and species were separate in existence, one could not be predicated of the other as identical. This shows why their unity is necessary.
Think about how we say 'Zayd is an animal' – this would be impossible if animal were a separate existent.
4
Understand the example of Zayd
The author uses Zayd to illustrate: Zayd is human, animal, and rational all at once, without any external multiplicity. This example anchors the abstract argument in a concrete case.
Notice that Zayd's essence is one, not a composite of separate parts.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage concludes that if there were external multiplicity, predication would be inconceivable. This reinforces the unity of genus and species in reality.
This conclusion is a key principle in logic and ontology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لك من هذا الذي صورناه في المقدار وأنواعه أنه ليس بين الجنس والفصل تمايز في الخارج بأن يكون للجنس وجود فيه والفصل وجود آخر، بل هما متحدان بحسب الخارج وجوداً وجعلاً. كيف والأمران المتمايزان بالوجود في الخارج لا يمكن حمل أحدهما على الآخر بهو هو، وإن كان بينهما أي اتصال فرضت كالملازمة والحلول في الهيولى والصورة. ولنزده زيادة تحقيق فنقول: العام له مفهوم غير مفهوم الخاص، ويتحصل مفهوم العام بالخاص كما تحققته فيكون له أي لكل واحد من العام والخاص صورة عقلية مغايرة لصورة الآخر، ولكن هويتهما في الخارج واحدة فلا تمايز بينهما في الخارج، بل في الذهن فقط فزيد هو الإنسان وهو الحيوان وهو الناطق، ولا تعدد في الخارج بأن يكون الحيوان موجوداً في الخارج، وينضم إليه موجود آخر هو الناطق، فيتحصل منهما ماهية الإنسان، ثم ينضم إلى هذه الماهية موجود آخر هو التشخص المخصوص، فيتحصل منهما زيد؛ إذ لو كان هناك تعدد خارجي لم يتصور حمل هذه الأشياء بعضها على بعض
From this which we have depicted concerning quantity and its types, it follows that there is no distinction (tamayyuz) between genus (jins) and specific difference (fasl) in external existence, such that the genus has an existence in it and the difference another existence; rather, they are united according to external existence in existence and constitution. How so, for two things distinct in existence in the external world cannot have one predicated (haml) on the other as identical, even if there is between them any connection assumed, such as concomitance and inherence in matter and form. And to increase [our] investigation further, we say: the universal (al-amm) has a concept other than the concept of the particular (al-khass), and the concept of the universal is determined by the particular, as you have realized, so for each of the universal and particular there is a mental image different from the image of the other, but their identity (huwiyya) in external existence is one, so there is no distinction between them in external existence, rather only in the mind. Thus Zayd is the human, and he is the animal, and he is the rational; and there is no multiplicity in external existence such that the animal exists in external existence and another existent, the rational, is joined to it, and from them the essence of human is constituted, then to this essence another existent, the particular individuation (tashakhs al-makhsūs), is joined, and from them Zayd is constituted; for if there were external multiplicity, the predication of these things on one another would be inconceivable.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is a proof that genus and specific difference are not distinct entities in the external world. The author begins by stating the conclusion: from the earlier discussion of quantity and its types, it is clear that there is no external distinction between genus and difference—they are united in external existence. He then argues: if two things were distinct in external existence, neither could be predicated of the other as identical, even if they were connected (e.g., as accident to substance, or as form to matter in the case of prime matter and form). To further clarify, he explains that the universal (e.g., animal) and the particular (e.g., rational) have different mental concepts, but their identity in external existence is one. Therefore, distinctions exist only in the mind. He gives the example of Zayd: Zayd is human, animal, and rational without any external multiplicity. If animal, rational, and individuation were separate existents, predications like 'Zayd is an animal' would be impossible. Thus, the unity of genus and difference in existence is necessary for predication.

The Three Considerations of the Universal
Objection and resolution via three considerations of the universal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the three considerations (bi-sharṭ al-dukhūl, bi-sharṭ al-khurūj, lā bi-sharṭ) resolve the apparent contradiction of predicating the particular on an individual.

Core Idea
The same universal can be identical, a part, or predicated depending on how it is considered.

In this passage, the commentator anticipates an objection: if predication requires unity, how can the particular (tashakhs), a real particular, be predicated on Zayd? He resolves this by showing that a universal like 'animal' can be considered in three ways relative to the individual. Understanding these three considerations is essential for grasping how predication works in logic and ontology.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
The objection states that the preceding argument seems to imply that the particular (tashakhs), a real particular (juz'ī ḥaqīqī), is predicated on Zayd, which contradicts what the commentator said elsewhere.
Notice the tension: predication usually requires universality.
2
Identify the answer and the three considerations
The commentator responds by saying that the relation of the person (shakhs) to the species is like that of difference to genus, and thus it has three considerations. Find the three considerations in the text.
The three are: bi-sharṭ al-dukhūl, bi-sharṭ al-khurūj, and lā bi-sharṭ.
3
Understand each consideration with the animal example
For each consideration, the text gives the example of 'animal' and 'rational' applied to Zayd. Note how each consideration yields a different logical role: identical, part, or predicated.
The consideration changes the status without changing the essence.
4
Reflect on how this resolves the contradiction
The answer shows that the particular can be predicated only in one consideration (lā bi-sharṭ), while in another it is a real particular not predicated. Thus there is no contradiction.
Predication of the particular is valid only when the universal is taken without conditions.
5
Connect to broader lessons
This passage demonstrates the nuanced handling of predication in Islamic logic, especially the role of considerations (i'tibārāt) in resolving apparent conflicts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (لم يتصور حمل هذه الأشياء بعضها على بعض) قيل : هذه العبارة مشعرة بحمل التشخص الذي هو جزئي حقيقي على زيد وهو ينافي ما صرح به الشارح قدس سره في مواضع عديدة من كتبه . أقول : إذا كان نسبة الشخص إلى النوع نسبة الفصل إلى الجنس كان له اعتبارات ثلاثة : فإذا أخذ
قوله: (لم يتصور حمل هذه الأشياء بعضها على بعض هذا يدل على جواز حمل التشخص المخصوص على الماهية بالمواطأة، ويدل عليه ظاهر كلامه في المقصد الحادي عشر أيضاً، قال بعض الفضلاء ولا بطلان في ذلك إلا بحسب التعبير؛ لأنك إذا قلت: هذا الإنسان، فليس المراد بالتشخص إلا مفهوم هذا، ولا شك أنه يحمل على الإنسان وعن هذا المفهوم يعبر
بالمواطأة، فإذا اعتبرنا الحيوان مثلاً من حيث إنه هو الناطق)، أي من حيث إنه متحصل قد دخل فيه من هذه الحيثية ما من شأنه أن يحصله كالناطق مثلاً، كان هو بشرط دخول النوع فيه وكونه متحصلاً مطابقاً لتمام هوية زيد كان عينه، وإذا أخذ بشرط خروج النوع عنه وكون زيد مركباً منهما كان جزءاً غير محمول عليه، وهو بهذا الاعتبار جزئي حقيقي؛ لأن انضمام الكلي إلى الكلي لا يفيد الهذية، وإذا أخذ من حيث هو مع قطع النظر عن التحصل والإبهام كان ذا جهتين ومحمولاً عليه، ولا ينافي ذلك كونه جزئياً حقيقياً من حيث خروجه عن النوع وانضمامه معه . قوله : ( فإذا اعتبرنا إلخ تفريع على ما قبله، أي إذا حصل بين العام والخاص بعد الانضمام جهتا التغاير والاتحاد، فإذا اعتبر العام من جهة الاتحاد كان نوعاً، وإذا اعتبر من حيث التغاير كان جزءاً، وإذا اعتبر مع قطع النظر عنهما كان محمولاً، فصح الحمل مع الجزئية للتغاير بين الجزء والمحمول بالاعتبار، وإن كانا متحدين بالذات وإطلاق الجزء على الذاتي في قولنا : الأجزاء المحمولة باعتبار كونه جزءاً من حد النوع، أو باعتبار كونه متحداً مع الجزء بالذات. قوله : (أي من حيث أنه متحصل أي ليس المراد من اتحاد الحيوان الناطق اتحاده من حيث المفهوم، فإنه خلاف الواقع، بل اعتباره متحصلاً به ومتعيناً، أي صيرورته ناطقاً لا متحصلاً به أمر ثالث؛ كما في المركبات الخارجية. قوله: (قد دخل فيه إلخ حاصله : أن يؤخذ الحيوان متحصلاً تحصلاً نوعياً، بحيث يدخل الناطق في هذا المتحصل، لا الناطق لا بشرط شيء أي الناطق من حيث هو مع قطع النظر عن الإبهام والتحصل، فإنه لا يدخل في النوع، بل الناطق بشرط ،لا أي باعتبار كونه مغايراً للحيوان خارجاً عنه بأن يعتبر الحيوان المبهم ، ويضم إليه الناطق، فيتحصل كل منهما بالآخر، ويصير نوعاً. وتفصيله ما ذكره الشيخ في الشفاء من أن أي معنى يشكل الحال في جنسيته وماديته، فوجدته قد يجوز انضمام الفصول إليه إن كان على أنها فيه ومنه كان جنساً، وإن أخذته من جهة نقص الفصول وتممت به المعنى وختمته حتى لو أدخل شيء آخر لم يكن من تلك الجملة وكان خارجاً، لم يكن جنساً بل مادة، وإن أوجبت له تمام المعنى حتى دخل فيه ما يمكن أن يدخل صار نوعاً، فإذن باشتراط أن لا يكون زيادة يكون مادة، وباشتراط أن يكون زيادة يكون نوعاً، وبأن لا يتعرض لذلك، بل يجوز أن يكون كل واحد من الزيادات على أنه داخلة في جملة معناه يكون جنساً. قوله : (كان هو الإنسان أي من حيث الحقيقة، إذ لا تغاير بين مجموع الحيوان الناطق بالتعبين، كما يعبر أحياناً عن الناطق بمبدئه. وفيه بحث: إذ قد مر أن الجزء الحقيقي ما يحمل على شيء ما، وسيذكر في بحث التعين أن كل تعين جزئي حقيقي عند الفلاسفة، فكيف يجوز حمله على شيء؟ فالصواب أن المراد بقوله : لم يتصور حمل هذه الأشياء إلخ بالنسبة إلى التشخص صحة اعتباره في جانب الموضوع ليس إلا، فتأمل.
His statement: 'the predication of these things on one another would be inconceivable.' It was said: This expression suggests the predication of the particular individuation (tashakhs), which is a real particular, on Zayd, and that contradicts what the commentator (may his secret be sanctified) stated in many places of his books. I say: If the relation of the person (shakhs) to the species is like the relation of the difference to the genus, then it has three considerations: So if we take... His statement: 'the predication of these things on one another would be inconceivable' this indicates the permissibility of the predication of the particular individuation (al-tashakhs al-makhsūs) on the essence by equivalence (bil-muwāţa'a), and the apparent meaning of his speech in the Eleventh Objective also indicates it. Some virtuous ones said: There is no invalidity in that except in terms of expression; because when you say 'this human', the intended meaning of individuation is only the concept of 'this', and there is no doubt that it is predicated on human, and this concept is expressed by equivalence. Then if we consider the animal, for example, from the aspect that it is the rational, i.e., from the aspect that it is determined (mutahassil) in which has entered by this aspect what is apt to determine it, like the rational for example, then it is with the condition of the entry of the species into it and its being determined matching the complete identity of Zayd, it is identical to him; and if it is taken with the condition of the exit of the species from it and that Zayd is composed of them, then it is a part not predicated on him, and in this consideration it is a real particular; because the joining of the universal to the universal does not yield individuation; and if it is taken in itself disregarding determination and ambiguity, it has two aspects and is predicated on him, and that does not contradict its being a real particular in terms of its exit from the species and its joining with it. His statement: 'Then if we consider... etc.' is a branch on what precedes, i.e., when between the universal and the particular after joining there obtain the two aspects of difference and union, then if the universal is considered from the aspect of union it is a species, if considered in terms of difference it is a part, and if considered disregarding both it is predicated. So predication is valid along with particularity due to the difference between the part and the predicate by consideration, even if they are united in essence. And the application of 'part' to the essential (al-dhātī) in our saying 'the predicated parts' is either considering it a part of the definition of the species, or considering it united with the part in essence. His statement: 'i.e., from the aspect that it is determined' means that the intended meaning of the union of the animal and the rational is not their union in terms of concept, for that would be contrary to reality, rather considering it determined by it and specified, i.e., its becoming rational, not that being determined by it is a third thing, as in external composites. His statement: 'has entered into it etc.' its summary: that the animal is taken as determined by a specific determination, such that the rational enters into this determined entity, not the rational unconditionally (lā bi-sharṭ shay'), i.e., the rational in itself disregarding ambiguity and determination, for it does not enter into the species; rather the rational with the condition of not, i.e., considering it different from the animal outside it, by taking the ambiguous animal and joining the rational to it, then each is determined by the other, and it becomes a species. And its detail is what the Shaykh (Ibn Sina) mentioned in al-Shifā': that any meaning whose situation is problematic in terms of its being a genus or a matter, you find it may allow the joining of differences to it; if it is on the condition that they are in it and from it, it is a genus; if you take it from the aspect of deficiency of the differences and complete the meaning with it and seal it such that if something else enters it would not be from that whole and would be outside, then it is not a genus but matter; and if you necessitate for it the complete meaning such that what can enter enters, it becomes a species. So then, with the condition that there be no increase, it is matter; with the condition that there be increase, it is a species; and with no attention to that, but rather it is permissible that each one of the increases be included in the totality of its meaning, it is a genus. His statement: 'it is the human' means in terms of reality, since there is no difference between the totality of the animal and the rational by specification, as sometimes the rational is expressed by its principle. But there is a discussion: since it has passed that the real part is what is predicated on something, and it will be mentioned in the discussion of specification that every specification is a real particular according to the philosophers, so how can it be predicated on something? So the correct view is that the intended meaning of his statement 'predication of these things would be inconceivable' with respect to individuation is only the validity of its consideration in the side of the subject, not otherwise. So reflect.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer regarding the predication of the particular individuation (tashakhs) on an individual like Zayd. The objection states that the previous argument (that predication requires unity in existence) seems to imply that the particular (which is a real particular) can be predicated on Zayd, contradicting the commentator's earlier statements. The answer, introduced by 'I say' (aqūl), resolves this by noting that the relation of the person (shakhs) to the species is like that of difference to genus, and thus the universal (like animal) can be considered in three ways: (1) with the condition of including the species (bi-sharṭ al-dukhūl) – then it is identical to the individual; (2) with the condition of excluding the species (bi-sharṭ al-khurūj) – then it is a part not predicated; (3) considered in itself without either condition (lā bi-sharṭ) – then it has two aspects and is predicated. The text then elaborates on these three considerations through further commentary, citing Ibn Sina's discussion of genus, matter, and species. It concludes with a remark that the predication of individuation is only valid when considered on the subject side, not as a real part.
