علة مستقلة
علة ناقصة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under what condition can multiple differentiae exist without contradiction?
A) When the effect is one in essence
B) When the causes are independent
C) When the differentiae are proximate
D) When the effect is multiple in essence

Key Takeaway
The impossibility of two proximate differentiae requires that the effect is one in essence and each differentia is part of an independent causal complex.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your understanding of Allah's oneness, do you ever feel that multiple descriptions (like 'All-Knowing' and 'All-Powerful') might somehow divide His essence? How does the condition of unity of essence (وحدة المعلول بالذات) from this lesson help you trust that His attributes are one with His essence?
?
The passage says that incomplete causes can be multiple, but independent causes cannot. In your worship, do you sometimes rely on multiple incomplete efforts (like prayer without sincerity, or charity without taqwa) rather than seeking a single, complete reliance on Allah? How would it change your practice to seek that independent cause?

Logic and Technical Terms
intermediate
5 min
Resolving the Objection: Sensation and Movement as Effects of One Differentia
Sanusi resolves the objection that sensation and movement are two differentiae for animal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why 'sensitive' and 'volitionally moving' are not two differentiae for animal but effects of a single unknown differentia.

Core Idea
When the real differentia is unknown, we describe it by its necessary effects, even if multiple.

A common objection to the principle is that animal seems to have two proximate differentiae: being sensitive and being volitionally moving. Sanusi explains that these are not two differentiae but two effects of one hidden differentia. This lesson walks through the reasoning and the subtle discussion of precedence between sensation and movement.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and Sanusi's response
Identify the claim that 'sensitive' and 'volitionally moving' might be two differentiae for animal, and note the response that they are merely effects.
2
Understand the method of identifying differentiae through effects
The passage explains that when the real differentia is unknown, we refer to its nearest effects, like 'rational' for the differentia of man.
This is a practical epistemological tool.
3
Appreciate the ambiguity of precedence
The passage discusses why both sensation and movement are used: their mutual precedence is unclear, so both are mentioned as indicators.
This shows caution in defining differentiae.

Source Text

الفرع الثاني: الفصل القريب لا يتعدد، فلا يكون لشيء واحد فصلان قريبان في مرتبة واحدة، وإلا اجتمع على المعلول الواحد بالذات علتان مستقلتان. قوله: (والحيوان فصل له إلخ) لعدم وجود النمو في الملك، وإن كان حساساً متحركاً بالإرادة على رأي المتكلمين. قوله: (إن كان هو الجوهر إلخ) اللام للعهد أي ذلك الجوهر الذي هو مبدأ النطق في الإنسان، وهو صورته النوعية أو النفس الناطقة، وحينئذ لا شك في أنه ليس مشتركاً، وبعضهم حمله على الجنس وأول العبارة الدالة على ادعاء الاشتراك بالمنع أي لا نسلم اشتراكه لم يجوز أن يكون مختلفاً فيهما. وهذا القدر كاف في دفع النقض. قوله: (بل هو أثر من آثار فصله) ويجوز اشتراك المتخالفين في عارض واحد كما مر. قوله: (في مرتبة واحدة) قيد بذلك؛ لأنه يجوز تعدده لماهية واحدة إذا كانا مرتبتين بأن يكون أحدهما فصلاً قريباً لجنس، والآخر لجنس آخر فوقه نحو الناطق والحساس. قوله: (وإلا لكان كل منهما علة للآخر) قيل: لم لا يجوز أن تكون ذات كل منهما علة لحصة الآخر بلا استحالة وأجيب بأن التفريع المذكور بناء على ما فهموا من علية الفصل لطبيعة الجنس، فإن الدليل المذكور على تقدير تمامه إنما يدل على هذا. قوله: (فإنه ليس مشتركاً بل مختلفاً) هذا على سبيل المنع أي لا نسلم الاشتراك، فإن الأصل لما كان ثابتاً بالدليل على زعم المستدل، وكان الإيراد نقضاً عليه، كفى في الجواب منع الاشتراك بلا حاجة إلى الاستدلال باختلاف الآثار. قوله: (بل هو أثر من آثار فصله) إذا سلم اشتراك هذا العارض كما هو الظاهر، لم يكن أثراً لفصله القريب، فلا بد أن يقيد بشيء لا يوجد في الملك، فتأمل. ثم قال: الفصل بالقريب؛ لأن الفصل البعيد وكذا المطلق يجوز تعدده، ويكون كل من الفصول المتعددة علة للجنس الذي في مرتبته كالناطق للحيوان والحساس للجسم النامي، والنامي للجسم مطلقاً، وقابل الأبعاد للجوهر. واعتبر وحدة المعلول بالذات؛ لأنه إذا تعدد ذاته جاز توارد العلل عليه كما في أفراد نوع واحد يقع بعضها بعلة وبعضها بعلة أخرى، وأما مع وحدة الذات، فلا مساغ لذلك؛ إذ يستغنى بكل عن كل، سواء كان الواحد بالذات شخصاً، وهو ظاهر، أو لا، كما نحن بصدده، فإن طبيعة الجنس في النوع قبل اعتبار تعدد أفراده ذات واحدة لا تعدد فيها، وقيد العلة بالاستقلال؛ لأن تعدد العلل الناقصة جائز، فإن قلت: ليس الفصل وحده علة تامة للجنس؛ لجواز أن يكون للجنس أجزاء، وأن يكون هناك شرائط معتبرة. قلت: كل واحد من الفصلين مع باقي الأمور المعتبرة علة مستقلة فيلزم توارد العلل المستقلة. لا يقال: الحساس والمتحرك بالإرادة فصلان قريبان للحيوان؛ لأنا نقول: بل كل منهما أثر لفصله، فإن حقيقة الفصل إذا جهلت عبر عنها بأقرب آثارها كالنطق لفصل الإنسان. ولما اشتبه تقدم كل من الحس والحركة الإرادية على الآخر عبر بهما. ولم يتعرض الشارح قدس سره لبيان فائدته؛ لأن بيان فائدة قيد القريب يتضمنه فإن الفصل البعيد قريب في مرتبة الجنس البعيد. قوله: (وأما مع وحدة الذات إلخ) يعني أن الدليل الذي ذكروه في امتناع توارد العلل، وإن صوره في الواحد الشخصي، لكنه جار في الواحد بالذات، سواء Commentary
This passage is a detailed argument for the principle that a single thing cannot have two proximate differentiae. It begins by stating the principle and the proof: if there were two, then two independent causes would converge on one effect. Then it addresses several glosses: first, explaining why animal is a differentia for man relative to angel (due to lack of growth in angels). Then it explains the meaning of 'rational' as substance versus accident. Then it explains the restriction to 'one rank' because differentiae can be multiple in different ranks. Then it addresses an objection that if two differentiae were possible, each would be cause of the other, and answers that the causation relation prevents this. Then it discusses the condition of unity of essence and independence of causes, showing that the proof applies to both specific and personal unity. It also addresses the example of 'sensitive' and 'volitionally moving' as possible proximate differentiae for animal, but explains they are merely effects of a single differentia. Finally, it discusses the ambiguity of precedence between sensation and movement.

Key Terms

فصل
عارض
لازم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking that 'sensitive' and 'volitionally moving' are two separate proximate differentiae for animal.
Correction: They are two effects of a single unknown differentia, not the differentiae themselves.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why are both 'sensitive' and 'volitionally moving' used to describe the differentia of animal?
A) Because they are the two differentiae
B) Because the real differentia is unknown and their precedence is ambiguous
C) Because sensation always precedes movement
D) Because movement always precedes sensation

Key Takeaway
When the real differentia is unknown, we identify it by its necessary effects, and multiple effects do not imply multiple differentiae.

The Proximate Differentia Only Constitutes One Species: The Core Principle
Core statement of the third branch and its immediate proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third branch's core claim: a proximate differentia can only constitute one species, and why violating this leads to a contradiction in the simplicity of the differentia and the distinctness of genera.

Core Idea
A simple differentia cannot produce two genera; otherwise its effect would be absent.

This lesson introduces the third branch of the discussion on the proximate differentia. The author states the principle and then draws out a consequence: if a proximate differentia could constitute two species in one rank, the simple differentia would have two effects (the genera), which is impossible because the genus of one species does not exist in the other. This establishes the logical necessity that a proximate differentia must be simple and species-specific.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the first part of the passage from 'الفَرْعُ الثَّالِثُ' to 'لَا يُوجَدُ فِي الْآخَرِ'. Notice the concise logical flow: statement, condition, consequence, and justification.
The passage uses conditional reasoning: if X, then Y, but Y is false, so X is false.
2
Translate and paraphrase
Read the English translation and restate the reasoning in your own words. Focus on why the differentia cannot constitute two species.
3
Identify the key terms
Find the terms 'فصل قريب' (proximate differentia), 'بسيط' (simple), and 'تخلف' (absence/falling away). Understand their roles in the argument.
'تخلف' here means the effect failing to occur.
4
Reflect on the condition of simplicity
The proof only works if the differentia is simple. Ask yourself: why is simplicity necessary? What would happen if the differentia were composite?
This sets up the next lesson on objections.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفرع الثالث : لا يقوم فصل قريب (إلا) نوعا واحداً، وإلا أي وإن لم يكن كذلك، بل قوم نوعين في مرتبة واحدة فللبسيط أثران) هما جنسا ذينك النوعين، وهذا إنما يتم إذا كان الفصل القريب بسيطاً، فالأولى أن يقال : فيتخلف عنه معلوله، لأن جنس كل من النوعين لا يوجد في الآخر. قوله : ( إذا جعل التمام في قولهم : الفصل القريب هو الجزء المميز التام . قوله : (امتنع تعدده إلخ) قيل : إِذا تركب ماهية من جنس وفصل مركب من أمرين متساويين، كان ذلك الفصل وكل واحد من جزأيه فصلاً قريباً، بمعنى المميز عن جميع ما عداه . ولا يلزم التوارد؛ لعدم كفاية كل واحد منهما في وجود الجنس. والجواب : أن الجزأين ليسا مرتبة الفصل المركب والكلام في تعدد الفصل القريب في مرتبة واحدة بالقياس إلى الجنس. نعم إنهما في مرتبة واحدة بالقياس إلى الفصل لكن لا جنس فيه . الإرادية الحيوانية بكونها لا على نهج واحد، ليتحقق كونها أثراً لفصله القريب، وإلا فمطلق الحركة بالإرادة موجودة في الفلك، لكن حركة كل من الأفلاك على نهج واحد لبساطته عندهم. :قوله لم يكن لها فصل بهذا المعنى لانتفاء التمامية بالقياس إلى كل واحد منهما، والجزئية بالقياس إلى المجموع وفيه نظر؛ إذ يلزم على هذا أن لا ينحصر الكلي في الخمسة ضرورة أن كل واحد من ذينك الأمرين المتساويين ليس شيئاً منها . قوله: (لم يمتنع تعدده في ماهية ليس لها جنس فيه بحث : إذ الظاهر امتناع هذا أيضاً، تفريعاً على العلية ضرورة تخلف المعلول عن العلة المستلزمة. وما ذكره في حواشيه على المطالع من أن بطلانه إنما يظهر إذا كان هناك جنس أو حصة منه ولا يكون الفصل له، وفيما نحن بصدده لم يوجد شيء منهما، محل تأمل؛ لأن وجود العلة بلا معلول، لا وجودهما معاً من غير أن تكون العلة علة له ألا يرى أن ليس المفهوم من قولنا : النار علة موجبة للحرارة أنه لو وجد النار والحرارة كانت الأولى علة للثانية، حتى لو وجد النار بلا حرارة يكن لم من التخلف الممتنع في شيء، ولو كان معنى التخلف ما ذكره لم يستقم الفرع الثالث والرابع إلا بتكلف . قوله : (إذا كان الفصل القريب بسيطاً) أي حقيقياً لا كثرة فيه بوجه من الوجوه، لا بحسب ذاته ولا بحسب جهاته واعتباراته . معنى التخلف
The third branch: A proximate differentia only constitutes one species. Otherwise (i.e., if it were not so) but rather constitutes two species in one rank, then the simple would have two effects which are the genera of those two species. This only holds if the proximate differentia is simple. So it is better to say: then its effect would be absent from it, because the genus of each of the two species does not exist in the other. His saying: (If completeness is taken in their statement: the proximate differentia is the complete distinguishing part). His saying: (Its multiplicity is impossible, etc.) It was said: If a quiddity is composed of a genus and a differentia that is composed of two equal matters, then that differentia and each one of its parts are a proximate differentia in the sense of distinguishing from everything else. And concurrence is not necessary because each one of them is not sufficient for the existence of the genus. The answer: The two parts are not the rank of the composite differentia, and the discussion is about multiplicity of the proximate differentia in one rank relative to the genus. Yes, they are in one rank relative to the differentia, but there is no genus in it. The animal voluntary [movement] by being not in one manner, so that it is realized as an effect of its proximate differentia; otherwise absolute voluntary motion exists in the celestial sphere, but the motion of each of the spheres is in one manner due to their simplicity according to them. His saying: It did not have a differentia in this sense due to the lack of completeness relative to each one of them, and the lack of partiality relative to the whole. And there is a consideration in it; for it follows from this that the universal is not limited to five, necessarily because each one of those two equal matters is not one of them. His saying: (Its multiplicity is not impossible in a quiddity that has no genus) – there is a discussion in it: for the apparent is that this is also impossible, branching from causality due to the necessity of the effect being absent from the necessary cause. And what he mentioned in his glosses on al-Matali' that its falsity only appears if there is a genus or a portion of it and the differentia does not belong to it, and in our case nothing of them exists, is a place for reflection; because the existence of a cause without an effect, not their existence together without the cause being a cause for it – do you not see that the concept of our statement 'fire is a necessitating cause of heat' is not that if fire and heat exist, the first is a cause of the second, so that if fire exists without heat it would be a case of the impossible absence of effect? And if the meaning of absence were what he mentioned, the third and fourth branches would not be sound except with effort. His saying: (If the proximate differentia is simple) i.e., real, having no multiplicity in any respect, neither in its essence nor in its aspects and considerations. The meaning of absence.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage defines and defends the third branch of the discussion on the proximate differentia (الفصل القريب). It begins by stating the branch: a proximate differentia only constitutes one species. If it were to constitute two species in one rank, then the simple (البسيط) would have two effects, namely the genera of those two species. This is only tenable if the proximate differentia is simple; hence the commentator suggests it is better to say that its effect would be absent from it because the genus of each species does not exist in the other. The commentary then examines the definition of 'proximate differentia' as the complete distinguishing part, and addresses objections about multiplicity. It discusses cases where a quiddity is composed of a genus and a composite differentia, and how each part may be a proximate differentia in the sense of distinguishing. The answer given is that the parts are not at the rank of the composite differentia; the discussion concerns multiplicity in one rank relative to the genus. The commentator then delves into the concept of the simple and its effect, using the example of animal voluntary motion versus celestial motion. The discussion further considers the possibility of multiplicity in a quiddity without a genus, ultimately concluding that even that is impossible due to the necessary connection between cause and effect. The passage ends with a clarification that 'simple' means having no multiplicity in any respect.

Key Terms
فصل قريب
بسيط
تخلف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that a proximate differentia could constitute multiple species if it is simple, because the differentia alone defines the species.
Correction: The passage shows that if a simple differentia constituted two species, the simple would have two effects (the genera), but since each genus is unique to its species, the simple would have to produce a genus that is absent from the other species, which is contradictory.

Checkpoint
According to the third branch, what follows if a proximate differentia were to constitute two species in one rank?
A) The simple would have two effects, namely the genera of those two species.
B) The differentia would be composite.
C) The genus would be the same for both species.
D) The differentia would no longer be proximate.

Key Takeaway
A simple proximate differentia cannot constitute more than one species because it would entail an impossible absence of its effect.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Is there any area of your life where you expect a single foundation—like a principle, intention, or relationship—to produce two conflicting outcomes? How does this logical principle expose the inconsistency in that expectation? What will you do to align that foundation with its proper effect?
?
This lesson teaches that a simple cause cannot have two distinct effects of the same rank. In your own faith and actions, are you trying to serve two masters that pull in different directions? How can you ensure your devotion remains undivided and causally unified?

Objections and Resolutions: Composite Differentia and Quiddities Without Genus
Commentary addressing objections: composite differentia, multiple differentiae in quiddity without genus, and the causal argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objections against the third branch regarding composite differentiae and quiddities without genus, and how the commentator resolves them by appealing to completeness, rank, and causality.

Core Idea
A composite differentia does not violate the rule because its parts are not at the same rank relative to the genus.

After establishing the core principle, the commentator addresses potential counterexamples. If a differentia is composite (composed of two equal parts), could each part be considered a proximate differentia? The answer clarifies that the parts are not at the rank of the composite relative to the genus. Furthermore, the possibility of multiple differentiae in a quiddity without a genus is rejected based on the necessary connection between cause and effect. This lesson unpacks these subtle arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer about composite differentia
Read from 'قيل : إِذا تركب ماهية من جنس وفصل مركب...' up to the end of the answer. Note the two objections and the commentator's response.
Key phrase: 'الجزأين ليسا مرتبة الفصل المركب'.
2
Examine the example of voluntary movement
Read the example of animal voluntary motion versus celestial motion. Understand how it illustrates the condition of 'not being in one manner' for the effect of the differentia.
Celestial motion is simple and uniform; animal voluntary motion is not uniform.
3
Analyze the discussion on quiddity without genus
Read from 'قوله: (لم يمتنع تعدده في ماهية ليس لها جنس...' to the end. Understand why even without a genus, multiplicity of differentiae is impossible due to causality.
The commentator critiques an earlier view and reinforces the causal necessity.
4
Reflect on the definition of 'simple' at the end
Read the final clarification: 'إذا كان الفصل القريب بسيطاً أي حقيقياً لا كثرة فيه'. Connect this to the overall argument.
This reinforces why the core principle stands.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A composite differentia can be broken down into multiple proximate differentiae, each capable of constituting a species.
Correction: The parts of a composite differentia are not at the same rank relative to the genus; they only have the same rank relative to the differentia itself, which lacks a genus. Therefore, they do not constitute multiple species in one rank.

The Fourth Branch: Proximate Differentia Only Accompanies One Genus
Sanusi states the fourth branch and gives its proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a proximate differentia can only accompany one genus and the logical consequence of it accompanying two genera.

Core Idea
A proximate differentia cannot serve two genera simultaneously.

This lesson presents the fourth branch of a logical inquiry: the proximate differentia (فصل قريب) can only accompany one genus in one rank. If it accompanied two genera, it would necessitate two species, leading to the unacceptable consequence of the effect being absent from its necessary cause.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the rule and its proof.
2
Identify the key claim
Notice the claim that the proximate differentia only accompanies one genus. What is the proof given?
The proof is based on impossibility of one species having two genera and the consequent absence of effect from cause.
3
Understand the implication
If it accompanied two genera, two species would result, causing the effect to be absent from its necessary cause—this is impossible.
4
Reflect on the simplicity point
The passage mentions that otherwise the 'simple would have two effects'. Consider what this means.
This is tied to the concept of the simple (بسيط) and its effects.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفرع الرابع : وهو فرع الفرع الثالث المتقدم أنه أي الفصل القريب ( لا يقارن) في مرتبة واحدة (إلا جنسا ،واحداً، وإلا فللبسيط أثران ) ; إذ لو قارن جنسين في مرتبة واحدة، لقوم نوعين في مرتبة واحدة لاستحالة أن يكون لنوع واحد جنسان في مرتبة واحدة، وحينئذ يلزم تخلف المعلول عن علته المستلزمة إياه سواء كانت علة تامة أو جزءاً أخيراً منها، وقد يفرع الثالث على الرابع فيقال : لما ثبت أن الفصل القريب لا يقارن جنسين في مرتبة واحدة لاستلزامه التخلف وجب أن لا يقوم نوعين في مرتبة والأظهر أنهما مشتركان في الدليل بلا تفريع بينهما. وكل ذلك) أي جميع ما ذكر من الفروع قوله : ( فالأولى إلخ ) إنما قال ذلك لأنه لم يظهر بطلان البساطة حتى يكون الاستدلال الموقوف عليها باطلاً. قوله : ( لأن جنس كل إلخ مع أن الفصل علة مقارنة للجنس، فلا يرد أن التخلف إنما يلزم إذا وجد الفصل بدون وجود الجنس، لا إذا وجد الفصل في نوع بدون الجنس. (قوله لاستحالة أن يكون الخ لأنه عبارة عن تمام الذاتي المشترك بين النوع وبين ماهية ما ولا تعدد في التمام . (قوله لاستلزامه التخلف لما مر من امتناع أن يكون لنوع واحد جنسان في مرتبة واحدة. (قوله في الدليل) وهو امتناع التخلف. قوله : ( فالأولى أن يقال إلخ ) إنما قال : الأولى لأنه يمكن أن يكون مراد المصنف بالبسيط الإضافي الأمر الواحد فيكون معنى كلامه أن الأمر الواحد المؤثر لا يكون له أثران متخالفان هما جنسان، وإلا يلزم تخلف المعلول عن علته المؤثرة المستلزمة للمعلول وأنه محال . وأنت تعلم أن حمل عبارة المتن على هذا المعنى تكلف بارد ولذا قال فالأولى . (قوله لا يوجد في الآخر فجنسبة الجنسين حينئذ بالنظر إلى نوعين آخرين يشترك كل منهما مع واحد من النوعين الأولين في جنسه بدون أن يوجد معه فصله، وإنما لم يجز أن جنس كل من النوعين المفروضين في الآخر؛ لأنه لو وجد لكانا نوعاً واحداً، ولم يكن بينهما امتياز . وفيه بحث : إذ عدم الامتياز على تقدير جزئية كل من الجنسين في النوع الآخر، وأما على تقدير وجود كل من الجنسين في النوع الآخر مطلقاً فلا؛ لجواز أن يكون الجنسان متساويين، والامتياز بين النوعين بأن يكون كل من الجنسين في أحدهما ذاتياً، وفي الآخر عرضياً ويمكن أن يقال : إذا وجد فصل هذا النوع وجنسه في النوع الآخر، كما هو المفروض . فإن اعتبر ذات الجنس والفصل لم يتميز أحد النوعين عن خر بشيء منهما، وإن اعتبر الجنس من حيث إنه ذاتي في هذا النوع تميزه بهذه الحيثية عن النوع الآخر ضرورة عروضه ،له لكن يرد حينئذ أن هذه الحيثية خارجة عن الماهية، فالذاتي المأخوذ معها لم يكن ذاتياً بل خارجاً منها فليتأمل.
The fourth branch: It is a branch of the preceding third branch, that is, the proximate differentia (does not accompany) in one rank (except one genus), otherwise the simple would have two effects, for if it accompanied two genera in one rank, it would constitute two species in one rank because it is impossible for one species to have two genera in one rank. Then it would necessitate the absence of the effect from its necessary cause, whether it is a complete cause or a last part of it. And the third is sometimes branched on the fourth: it is said: since it is established that the proximate differentia does not accompany two genera in one rank due to its necessitating absence, it must not constitute two species in one rank. But the more apparent is that they share the proof without branching between them. And all that) i.e., all that was mentioned of the branches. His saying: (So it is better, etc.) – he only said that because the falsity of simplicity has not appeared so that the proof dependent on it would be false. His saying: (because the genus of each, etc.) – even though the differentia is a concomitant cause of the genus, so it is not objected that absence only follows if the differentia exists without the existence of the genus, not if the differentia exists in a species without the genus. His saying: (because it is impossible for it to be, etc.) – because it is an expression of the complete essential common between the species and some quiddity, and there is no multiplicity in completeness. His saying: (because it necessitates absence) – due to what has passed about the impossibility of one species having two genera in one rank. His saying: (in the proof) – it is the impossibility of absence. His saying: (So it is better to say, etc.) – he only said 'better' because it is possible that the author meant by 'simple' the additive simple, the one affair. Then the meaning of his statement is that the one effective affair cannot have two different effects that are genera; otherwise it would necessitate the absence of the effect from its effective cause that necessitates the effect, and that is impossible. And you know that loading the text's expression onto this meaning is an awkward effort, so he said 'better'. His saying: (does not exist in the other) – then the genericity of the two genera then is with respect to two other species, each of which shares with one of the first two species in its genus without its differentia existing with it. And it is not permissible that the genus of each of the two assumed species be in the other, because if it existed, they would be one species and there would be no distinction between them. And there is a discussion in it: for the lack of distinction on the assumption of partiality of each of the two genera in the other species, but on the assumption of the absolute existence of each of the two genera in the other species, no; because it is possible that the two genera are equal, and the distinction between the two species is that each of the two genera is essential in one of them and accidental in the other. And it can be said: if the differentia of this species and its genus exist in the other species, as is assumed, then if the essence of the genus and differentia are considered, one of the two species is not distinguished from the other by anything of them. But if the genus is considered in terms of it being essential in this species, it is distinguished by this respect from the other species due to its accidentally in relation to it, but then it is objected that this respect is outside the quiddity, so the essential taken with it is not essential but external to it. So let one reflect.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth branch, which is a corollary of the third: a proximate differentia only accompanies one genus in one rank; if it accompanied two genera, it would constitute two species, which is impossible because a single species cannot have two genera in one rank. This would lead to the effect being absent from its necessary cause. The commentator then discusses the relationship between the third and fourth branches: some derive the third from the fourth, but the more apparent view is that they share the same proof, namely the impossibility of the effect's absence from its cause. The passage also examines nuances: the differentia is a concomitant cause of the genus, so absence does not occur if the differentia exists in a species without the genus (since the genus might be absent accidentally). The commentary further explores the meaning of 'simple' and suggests an alternative interpretation (the additive simple) but deems it an awkward effort. Finally, it delves into a detailed discussion about distinguishing species when genera are equal, considering whether the genus is essential or accidental, and concludes that if the genus is taken as essential in one species and accidental in the other, the essential aspect becomes external, requiring further reflection.

Key Terms
فصل قريب
جنس
علة
تخلف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A single proximate differentia could define multiple genera.
Correction: The differentia would then constitute two species, which is impossible because one species cannot have two genera.

Checkpoint
What is the main reason a proximate differentia cannot accompany two genera?
A) It would make the simple have two effects.
B) It would require one species to have two genera, which is impossible.
C) It would eliminate the need for a genus.
D) It would create a contradiction in the definition of species.

Key Takeaway
The proximate differentia must accompany exactly one genus; otherwise, logical impossibility arises.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In what area of your life have you been trying to serve two opposing masters, expecting a single effort to produce two contradictory outcomes? How does this logical principle expose the impossibility of that, and what must you clarify today?
?
If a differentia cannot accompany two genera without causing absurdity, how much more can your heart not hold sincere devotion to Allah while also chasing the approval of others? Examine your intentions: which 'genus' is your differentia actually serving?

Logic and Technical Terms
intermediate

Relationship Between the Third and Fourth Branches
Commentary on the relationship between the third and fourth branches and an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the relationship between the third and fourth branches and the nuance of the differentia as a concomitant cause.

Core Idea
The third and fourth branches share the same proof and are not derived from each other.

This lesson explores how the third and fourth branches relate. Some derive the third from the fourth, but the more apparent view is that both rest on the same proof: the impossibility of the effect's absence from its cause. The passage also clarifies a nuance: the differentia is a concomitant cause, so absence only follows if the differentia exists without the genus, not if it exists in a species without the genus.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on branching
Read the part where branching is discussed and note the two views.
2
Identify the two positions
One position derives the third from the fourth; the other says they share the same proof.
3
Understand the nuance about absence
The differentia is a concomitant cause; absence only occurs if the differentia exists without the genus, not if it exists in a species without the genus.
This nuance prevents a potential objection.
4
Reflect on the simplicity point
The commentator remarks on 'the first' and the falsity of simplicity.

Commentary

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The third and fourth branches are derived from each other.
Correction: The more apparent view is that they share the same proof, not that one is derived from the other.

Checkpoint
According to the more apparent view, what is the relationship between the third and fourth branches?
A) The third is derived from the fourth.
B) The fourth is derived from the third.
C) They share the same proof without branching.
D) They are unrelated.

Key Takeaway
The third and fourth branches are independent but share the same logical proof.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever accepted a religious ruling or theological conclusion simply because it seemed to follow from another belief, without checking the actual proof? How does this lesson's emphasis on shared proof (not assumed derivation) call you to reexamine the foundations of your own convictions?
?
In your personal journey, have you mistaken a 'concomitant cause' for a separate cause—believing that something must automatically follow from a specific action or belief, when in reality they are inseparably linked? How can you apply the lesson's distinction to avoid false expectations in your worship or character?
?
This passage corrects a subtle error in logical reasoning. What area of your faith or practice might be vulnerable to a similar logical shortcut? Will you commit today to tracing each of your core beliefs back to its actual proof in revelation or sound reasoning, rather than relying on assumed connections?

The Simple Interpretation and Distinguishing Species
Commentary on the alternative meaning of 'simple' and a discussion on distinguishing species.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the alternative interpretation of 'simple' and the complex discussion of how species are distinguished when genera are equal.

Core Idea
Interpreting 'simple' as 'one affair' leads to issues, and distinguishing species when genera are equal requires careful consideration of essential vs. accidental.

This lesson dives into an alternative interpretation of 'simple' as the 'additive simple' (the one effective affair), which the commentator finds awkward. It then delves into a subtle discussion about how to distinguish two species when their genera are equal, considering whether the genus is essential or accidental in each.

Guided Path
1
Read the alternative interpretation
Read the passage where 'simple' is interpreted as 'the one effective affair' and note why the commentator finds it forced.
2
Understand the hypothetical scenario
The passage describes two species with equal genera and discusses how they are distinguished.
3
Explore the distinction based on essential vs accidental
One possibility is that the genus is essential in one species and accidental in the other.
4
Consider the objection
If the genus is taken as essential in one, the essential quality becomes external to the quiddity, leading to further issues.
The passage ends with 'so let one reflect', indicating room for thought.

(قوله لاستحالة أن يكون الخ لأنه عبارة عن تمام الذاتي المشترك بين النوع وبين ماهية ما ولا تعدد في التمام . (قوله لاستلزامه التخلف لما مر من امتناع أن يكون لنوع واحد جنسان في مرتبة واحدة. (قوله في الدليل) وهو امتناع التخلف. قوله : ( فالأولى أن يقال إلخ ) إنما قال : الأولى لأنه يمكن أن يكون مراد المصنف بالبسيط الإضافي الأمر الواحد فيكون معنى كلامه أن الأمر الواحد المؤثر لا يكون له أثران متخالفان هما جنسان، وإلا يلزم تخلف المعلول عن علته المؤثرة المستلزمة للمعلول وأنه محال . وأنت تعلم أن حمل عبارة المتن على هذا المعنى تكلف بارد ولذا قال فالأولى . (قوله لا يوجد في الآخر فجنسبة الجنسين حينئذ بالنظر إلى نوعين آخرين يشترك كل منهما مع واحد من النوعين الأولين في جنسه بدون أن يوجد معه فصله، وإنما لم يجز أن جنس كل من النوعين المفروضين في الآخر؛ لأنه لو وجد لكانا نوعاً واحداً، ولم يكن بينهما امتياز . وفيه بحث : إذ عدم الامتياز على تقدير جزئية كل من الجنسين في النوع الآخر، وأما على تقدير وجود كل من الجنسين في النوع الآخر مطلقاً فلا؛ لجواز أن يكون الجنسان متساويين، والامتياز بين النوعين بأن يكون كل من الجنسين في أحدهما ذاتياً، وفي الآخر عرضياً ويمكن أن يقال : إذا وجد فصل هذا النوع وجنسه في النوع الآخر، كما هو المفروض . فإن اعتبر ذات الجنس والفصل لم يتميز أحد النوعين عن خر بشيء منهما، وإن اعتبر الجنس من حيث إنه ذاتي في هذا النوع تميزه بهذه الحيثية عن النوع الآخر ضرورة عروضه ،له لكن يرد حينئذ أن هذه الحيثية خارجة عن الماهية، فالذاتي المأخوذ معها لم يكن ذاتياً بل خارجاً منها فليتأمل.
The fourth branch: It is a branch of the preceding third branch, that is, the proximate differentia (does not accompany) in one rank (except one genus), otherwise the simple would have two effects, for if it accompanied two genera in one rank, it would constitute two species in one rank because it is impossible for one species to have two genera in one rank. Then it would necessitate the absence of the effect from its necessary cause, whether it is a complete cause or a last part of it. And the third is sometimes branched on the fourth: it is said: since it is established that the proximate differentia does not accompany two genera in one rank due to its necessitating absence, it must not constitute two species in one rank. But the more apparent is that they share the proof without branching between them. And all that) i.e., all that was mentioned of the branches. His saying: (So it is better, etc.) – he only said that because the falsity of simplicity has not appeared so that the proof dependent on it would be false. His saying: (because the genus of each, etc.) – even though the differentia is a concomitant cause of the genus, so it is not objected that absence only follows if the differentia exists without the existence of the genus, not if the differentia exists in a species without the genus. His saying: (because it is impossible for it to be, etc.) – because it is an expression of the complete essential common between the species and some quiddity, and there is no multiplicity in completeness. His saying: (because it necessitates absence) – due to what has passed about the impossibility of one species having two genera in one rank. His saying: (in the proof) – it is the impossibility of absence. His saying: (So it is better to say, etc.) – he only said 'better' because it is possible that the author meant by 'simple' the additive simple, the one affair. Then the meaning of his statement is that the one effective affair cannot have two different effects that are genera; otherwise it would necessitate the absence of the effect from its effective cause that necessitates the effect, and that is impossible. And you know that loading the text's expression onto this meaning is an awkward effort, so he said 'better'. His saying: (does not exist in the other) – then the genericity of the two genera then is with respect to two other species, each of which shares with one of the first two species in its genus without its differentia existing with it. And it is not permissible that the genus of each of the two assumed species be in the other, because if it existed, they would be one species and there would be no distinction between them. And there is a discussion in it: for the lack of distinction on the assumption of partiality of each of the two genera in the other species, but on the assumption of the absolute existence of each of the two genera in the other species, no; because it is possible that the two genera are equal, and the distinction between the two species is that each of the two genera is essential in one of them and accidental in the other. And it can be said: if the differentia of this species and its genus exist in the other species, as is assumed, then if the essence of the genus and differentia are considered, one of the two species is not distinguished from the other by anything of them. But if the genus is considered in terms of it being essential in this species, it is distinguished by this respect from the other species due to its accidentally in relation to it, but then it is objected that this respect is outside the quiddity, so the essential taken with it is not essential but external to it. So let one reflect.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth branch, which is a corollary of the third: a proximate differentia only accompanies one genus in one rank; if it accompanied two genera, it would constitute two species, which is impossible because a single species cannot have two genera in one rank. This would lead to the effect being absent from its necessary cause. The commentator then discusses the relationship between the third and fourth branches: some derive the third from the fourth, but the more apparent view is that they share the same proof, namely the impossibility of the effect's absence from its cause. The passage also examines nuances: the differentia is a concomitant cause of the genus, so absence does not occur if the differentia exists in a species without the genus (since the genus might be absent accidentally). The commentary further explores the meaning of 'simple' and suggests an alternative interpretation (the additive simple) but deems it an awkward effort. Finally, it delves into a detailed discussion about distinguishing species when genera are equal, considering whether the genus is essential or accidental, and concludes that if the genus is taken as essential in one species and accidental in the other, the essential aspect becomes external, requiring further reflection.

أثران
ذاتي
عرضي
تمييز

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The alternative interpretation of 'simple' is the correct one.
Correction: The commentator says it is an awkward effort (تكلف بارد) and that the author said 'first' for a reason.

Checkpoint

B) It forces a loaded meaning onto the text.
C) It makes the simple have two effects.

The discussion shows the depth of kalam reasoning where subtle distinctions in essential vs accidental properties are debated.

The Fourth Branch: Proximate Differentia and One Genus
Explains that a proximate differentia cannot be paired with two genera in one rank, otherwise a simple would have two effects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a proximate differentia can only be paired with one genus in the same rank, and the logical consequences of violating this rule.

Core Idea
A simple thing cannot have two effects, so a differentia cannot pair with two genera.

This lesson tackles a subtle but crucial rule in logical classification: a proximate differentia—the final distinction that defines a species—cannot be associated with two genera simultaneously. The text explores what would happen if it did: it would force two species into one rank and cause the effect to lag behind its cause. We'll walk through the reasoning and see why this matters for logical structure.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Pay attention to the logical flow: the rule, the hypothetical violation, and the consequences.
The passage is dense; take your time to let the argument sink in.
2
Identify the main claim
The passage states that a proximate differentia cannot be paired with more than one genus in the same rank. Find this statement and note the reasoning that follows.
3
Understand the 'simple having two effects' objection
The core argument is that if a differentia accompanied two genera, it would necessitate two species in one rank, leading to a violation of causal principles. Grasp why this is impossible.
Think of a differentia as a cause that produces a specific effect (species).
4
Examine the branching discussion
The passage mentions that some derive the third branch from the fourth, but the more apparent view is that they share the same proof. See how this nuance fits into the overall logic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفرع ( الرابع : وهو فرع الفرع ( الثالث المتقدم أنه أي الفصل القريب ( لا يقارن) في مرتبة واحدة (إلا جنسا ،واحداً، وإلا فللبسيط أثران ) ؛ إذ لو قارن جنسين في مرتبة واحدة، لقوم نوعين في مرتبة واحدة لاستحالة أن يكون لنوع واحد جنسان في مرتبة واحدة، وحينئذ يلزم تخلف المعلول عن علته المستلزمة إياه سواء كانت علة تامة أو جزءاً أخيراً منها، وقد يفرع الثالث على الرابع فيقال : لما ثبت أن الفصل القريب لا يقارن جنسين في مرتبة واحدة لاستلزامه التخلف وجب أن لا يقوم نوعين في مرتبة والأظهر أنهما مشتركان في الدليل بلا تفريع بينهما. وكل ذلك) أي جميع ما ذكر من الفروع قوله : ( فالأولى إلخ ) إنما قال ذلك لأنه لم يظهر بطلان البساطة حتى يكون الاستدلال الموقوف عليها باطلاً.
The fourth branch: It is a branch of the third preceding branch, that the proximate differentia is not accompanied in one rank except by one genus. Otherwise, the simple [thing] would have two effects. For if it accompanied two genera in one rank, it would necessitate two species in one rank, because it is impossible for one species to have two genera in one rank. Then, the effect lagging behind its cause, which necessitates it, would follow, whether it is a complete cause or a final part of it. And the third may be branched from the fourth, so it is said: Since it is established that the proximate differentia does not accompany two genera in one rank because it necessitates lagging, it must not stand for two species in one rank. The more apparent is that they share the proof with no branching between them. And all that—i.e., all the branches mentioned—the statement: 'So the first is...' He only said that because the falsity of simplicity was not clear such that the inference dependent upon it would be false.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage explains the fourth branch (far' rabi') which is itself a branch of the third preceding branch. The key point is that the proximate differentia (al-fasl al-qarib) cannot be paired with more than one genus in the same rank; if it did, it would imply that a simple thing (basa'it) has two effects, which is impossible. The reasoning is: if the differentia accompanied two genera in one rank, it would necessitate two species in one rank, because one species cannot have two genera in one rank. Consequently, the effect would lag behind its cause (takhalluf al-ma'lul 'an 'illatih), which is impossible. The passage also notes that some base the third branch on the fourth, but the more apparent view is that both share the same proof without one being derived from the other. Finally, the comment on 'the first is...' indicates that the author only said that because the falsity of simplicity was not yet apparent.

Key Terms
الفصل القريب
الجنس
البسيط
تخلف المعلول عن العلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A simple thing can have multiple effects without issue.
Correction: If a simple (e.g., a differentia) produced two effects (species), it would imply that one cause has two different effects at the same level, which breaks the causal necessity assumed in logic.

Checkpoint
According to the fourth branch, what would happen if a proximate differentia accompanied two genera in one rank?
A) It would produce two differentiae.
B) It would necessitate two species in one rank.
C) It would prove the simplicity of the thing.
D) It would be permissible in logical analysis.

Key Takeaway
The proximate differentia must be paired with exactly one genus; otherwise, logical and causal contradictions arise.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The passage argues that a cause necessitates its effect immediately. Are there areas of your life where you delay responding to the truth, as if the cause does not demand an immediate effect?
?

The Impossibility of Two Genera in One Species
Refutes the lagging objection and asserts the impossibility of one species having two genera.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why two genera cannot exist in each other and why the lagging objection is invalid.

Core Idea
Two genera cannot coexist in one species without merging into one.

The commentator begins by clarifying a critical logical point: the differentia is a concurrent cause of the genus, so the objection about lagging does not apply. He then states the impossibility of one species having two genera, which is the foundation for the argument that two genera do not exist in each other.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation to grasp the main argument.
2
Identify the key terms
Identify the terms 'جنس' (genus) and 'فصل' (differentia) and understand their relationship. Notice that the differentia is a concurrent cause.
The differentia is inseparable from the genus.
3
Understand the refutation of lagging
The commentator explains that lagging only occurs if the differentia exists without the genus, but here the differentia is a concurrent cause, so lagging cannot happen.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( لأن جنس كل إلخ مع أن الفصل علة مقارنة للجنس، فلا يرد أن التخلف إنما يلزم إذا وجد الفصل بدون وجود الجنس، لا إذا وجد الفصل في نوع بدون الجنس. (قوله لاستحالة أن يكون الخ لأنه عبارة عن تمام الذاتي المشترك بين النوع وبين ماهية ما ولا تعدد في التمام . (قوله لاستلزامه التخلف لما مر من امتناع أن يكون لنوع واحد جنسان في مرتبة واحدة. (قوله في الدليل) وهو امتناع التخلف. قوله : ( فالأولى أن يقال إلخ ) إنما قال : الأولى لأنه يمكن أن يكون مراد المصنف بالبسيط الإضافي الأمر الواحد فيكون معنى كلامه أن الأمر الواحد المؤثر لا يكون له أثران متخالفان هما جنسان، وإلا يلزم تخلف المعلول عن علته المؤثرة المستلزمة للمعلول وأنه محال . وأنت تعلم أن حمل عبارة المتن على هذا المعنى تكلف بارد ولذا قال فالأولى . (قوله لا يوجد في الآخر فجنسبة الجنسين حينئذ بالنظر إلى نوعين آخرين يشترك كل منهما مع واحد من النوعين الأولين في جنسه بدون أن يوجد معه فصله، وإنما لم يجز أن جنس كل من النوعين المفروضين في الآخر؛ لأنه لو وجد لكانا نوعاً واحداً، ولم يكن بينهما امتياز . وفيه بحث : إذ عدم الامتياز على تقدير جزئية كل من الجنسين في النوع الآخر، وأما على تقدير وجود كل من الجنسين في النوع الآخر مطلقاً فلا؛ لجواز أن يكون الجنسان متساويين، والامتياز بين النوعين بأن يكون كل من الجنسين في أحدهما ذاتياً، وفي الآخر عرضياً ويمكن أن يقال : إذا وجد فصل هذا النوع وجنسه في النوع الآخر، كما هو المفروض . فإن اعتبر ذات الجنس والفصل لم يتميز أحد النوعين عن خر بشيء منهما، وإن اعتبر الجنس من حيث إنه ذاتي في هذا النوع تميزه بهذه الحيثية عن النوع الآخر ضرورة عروضه ،له لكن يرد حينئذ أن هذه الحيثية خارجة عن الماهية، فالذاتي المأخوذ معها لم يكن ذاتياً بل خارجاً منها فليتأمل.
His statement: 'because the genus of each, etc.', although the differentia is a concurrent cause of the genus, so it is not objected that lagging only follows if the differentia exists without the existence of the genus, not if the differentia exists in a species without the genus. His statement: 'because it is impossible, etc.,' because it is an expression of the complete shared essential between the species and a certain essence, and there is no multiplicity in the complete. His statement: 'because it necessitates lagging,' due to what has passed of the impossibility of one species having two genera in one rank. His statement: 'in the proof,' and that is the impossibility of lagging. His statement: 'So it is better to say, etc.,' he only said 'better' because it is possible that the author's intent by 'simple' is the additive simple, i.e., a single thing, so the meaning of his words would be that a single effective thing does not have two differing effects that are two genera; otherwise, the effect lagging behind its effective cause that necessitates the effect would follow, and that is impossible. And you know that interpreting the text of the matn in this sense is a forced and insipid interpretation, so he said 'better.' His statement: 'does not exist in the other,' so the relationship of the two genera then is with respect to two other species, each of which shares with one of the two first species in its genus without its differentia existing with it. He only did not allow that the genus of each of the two supposed species exists in the other; because if it existed, they would be one species and there would be no distinction between them. There is discussion: since non-distinction is on the assumption of each of the two genera being partial in the other species; but on the assumption of the absolute existence of each of the two genera in the other species, no; because it is possible that the two genera are coextensive, and the distinction between the two species is that each of the two genera is essential in one and accidental in the other. And it can be said: if the differentia of this species and its genus exist in the other species, as is assumed, then if the essence of the genus and differentia is considered, one species is not distinguished from the other by anything of them; but if the genus is considered insofar as it is essential in this species, it is distinguished by this aspect from the other species necessarily because [the genus] is accidental to it. But then it is objected that this aspect is external to the essence, so the essential taken with it was not essential but external to it, so let it be pondered.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage addresses a complex objection and answer regarding the claim that the two genera do not exist in each other. The commentator first notes that the differentia is a concurrent cause of the genus, so the objection that lagging only occurs if the differentia is without the genus is not valid. He then explains that 'impossible' refers to the impossibility of one species having two genera. He discusses the author's phrase 'So it is better to say...' suggesting that the author's intended meaning of 'simple' might be the additive simple (al-basit al-idafi), but this interpretation is forced. The core of the objection: it is argued that if the genus of each of two species existed in the other, they would be one species with no distinction. But a counterargument is raised: non-distinction only follows if the genera are partial in the other species; if they exist absolutely, they could be coextensive, and distinction could be by essential vs. accidental. Then a further objection: if the differentia and genus of one exist in the other, considering the genus as essential in one species distinguishes it, but then that aspect is external to the essence, so the essential taken with that aspect is not essential. The passage ends with 'so let it be pondered,' indicating this is a subtle point.

جنس
فصل
علة مقارنة
تخلف

Checkpoint
Why does the commentator say the lagging objection is invalid?
A) Because the differentia is a concurrent cause of the genus.
B) Because the genus is prior to the differentia.
C) Because the differentia is accidental.
D) Because the two genera are separate.

Key Takeaway
Two genera cannot coexist in one species because that would require lagging, which is impossible.

?

The 'Better' Interpretation and Distinction by Essential vs. Accidental
Explores an alternative interpretation and responds to the objection about two genera not existing in each other.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the refined argument that two genera can exist in each other if they are coextensive and distinguished by being essential in one species and accidental in the other, and the subtle problem this raises.

Core Idea
Genera can coexist if distinguished by essential versus accidental attribution.

The commentator now presents an alternative interpretation suggested by the author, known as the 'additive simple' understanding. He then addresses the core objection: if the genus of each species existed in the other, they would be one species. But he offers a counter: they could be coextensive and distinguished by one genus being essential and the other accidental. However, this leads to a further subtlety about the nature of essentiality.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and translation carefully. Notice the structure: first the 'better' interpretation, then the objection from the author, then the response, then a further objection.
2
Analyze the distinction
Understand the proposal that two genera can be coextensive and one can be essential in one species and accidental in the other. This would provide distinction without requiring the genera to be absent.
This is the commentator's defense against the objection.
3
Ponder the final subtlety
The commentator raises a further problem: if the genus is essential in one species and accidental in the other, the aspect that makes it essential is external to the essence. So the essential taken with that aspect is not truly essential.
The passage ends with 'so let it be pondered,' indicating this is a deep point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( لأن جنس كل إلخ مع أن الفصل علة مقارنة للجنس، فلا يرد أن التخلف إنما يلزم إذا وجد الفصل بدون وجود الجنس، لا إذا وجد الفصل في نوع بدون الجنس. (قوله لاستحالة أن يكون الخ لأنه عبارة عن تمام الذاتي المشترك بين النوع وبين ماهية ما ولا تعدد في التمام . (قوله لاستلزامه التخلف لما مر من امتناع أن يكون لنوع واحد جنسان في مرتبة واحدة. (قوله في الدليل) وهو امتناع التخلف. قوله : ( فالأولى أن يقال إلخ ) إنما قال : الأولى لأنه يمكن أن يكون مراد المصنف بالبسيط الإضافي الأمر الواحد فيكون معنى كلامه أن الأمر الواحد المؤثر لا يكون له أثران متخالفان هما جنسان، وإلا يلزم تخلف المعلول عن علته المؤثرة المستلزمة للمعلول وأنه محال . وأنت تعلم أن حمل عبارة المتن على هذا المعنى تكلف بارد ولذا قال فالأولى . (قوله لا يوجد في الآخر فجنسبة الجنسين حينئذ بالنظر إلى نوعين آخرين يشترك كل منهما مع واحد من النوعين الأولين في جنسه بدون أن يوجد معه فصله، وإنما لم يجز أن جنس كل من النوعين المفروضين في الآخر؛ لأنه لو وجد لكانا نوعاً واحداً، ولم يكن بينهما امتياز . وفيه بحث : إذ عدم الامتياز على تقدير جزئية كل من الجنسين في النوع الآخر، وأما على تقدير وجود كل من الجنسين في النوع الآخر مطلقاً فلا؛ لجواز أن يكون الجنسان متساويين، والامتياز بين النوعين بأن يكون كل من الجنسين في أحدهما ذاتياً، وفي الآخر عرضياً ويمكن أن يقال : إذا وجد فصل هذا النوع وجنسه في النوع الآخر، كما هو المفروض . فإن اعتبر ذات الجنس والفصل لم يتميز أحد النوعين عن خر بشيء منهما، وإن اعتبر الجنس من حيث إنه ذاتي في هذا النوع تميزه بهذه الحيثية عن النوع الآخر ضرورة عروضه ،له لكن يرد حينئذ أن هذه الحيثية خارجة عن الماهية، فالذاتي المأخوذ معها لم يكن ذاتياً بل خارجاً منها فليتأمل.
His statement: 'because the genus of each, etc.', although the differentia is a concurrent cause of the genus, so it is not objected that lagging only follows if the differentia exists without the existence of the genus, not if the differentia exists in a species without the genus. His statement: 'because it is impossible, etc.,' because it is an expression of the complete shared essential between the species and a certain essence, and there is no multiplicity in the complete. His statement: 'because it necessitates lagging,' due to what has passed of the impossibility of one species having two genera in one rank. His statement: 'in the proof,' and that is the impossibility of lagging. His statement: 'So it is better to say, etc.,' he only said 'better' because it is possible that the author's intent by 'simple' is the additive simple, i.e., a single thing, so the meaning of his words would be that a single effective thing does not have two differing effects that are two genera; otherwise, the effect lagging behind its effective cause that necessitates the effect would follow, and that is impossible. And you know that interpreting the text of the matn in this sense is a forced and insipid interpretation, so he said 'better.' His statement: 'does not exist in the other,' so the relationship of the two genera then is with respect to two other species, each of which shares with one of the two first species in its genus without its differentia existing with it. He only did not allow that the genus of each of the two supposed species exists in the other; because if it existed, they would be one species and there would be no distinction between them. There is discussion: since non-distinction is on the assumption of each of the two genera being partial in the other species; but on the assumption of the absolute existence of each of the two genera in the other species, no; because it is possible that the two genera are coextensive, and the distinction between the two species is that each of the two genera is essential in one and accidental in the other. And it can be said: if the differentia of this species and its genus exist in the other species, as is assumed, then if the essence of the genus and differentia is considered, one species is not distinguished from the other by anything of them; but if the genus is considered insofar as it is essential in this species, it is distinguished by this aspect from the other species necessarily because [the genus] is accidental to it. But then it is objected that this aspect is external to the essence, so the essential taken with it was not essential but external to it, so let it be pondered.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage addresses a complex objection and answer regarding the claim that the two genera do not exist in each other. The commentator first notes that the differentia is a concurrent cause of the genus, so the objection that lagging only occurs if the differentia is without the genus is not valid. He then explains that 'impossible' refers to the impossibility of one species having two genera. He discusses the author's phrase 'So it is better to say...' suggesting that the author's intended meaning of 'simple' might be the additive simple (al-basit al-idafi), but this interpretation is forced. The core of the objection: it is argued that if the genus of each of two species existed in the other, they would be one species with no distinction. But a counterargument is raised: non-distinction only follows if the genera are partial in the other species; if they exist absolutely, they could be coextensive, and distinction could be by essential vs. accidental. Then a further objection: if the differentia and genus of one exist in the other, considering the genus as essential in one species distinguishes it, but then that aspect is external to the essence, so the essential taken with that aspect is not essential. The passage ends with 'so let it be pondered,' indicating this is a subtle point.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that if two genera exist in each other, the species would be identical with no possible distinction.
Correction: The commentator shows that distinction can still be made if the genera are coextensive and one is essential in one species and accidental in the other.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when would two genera in the same species not cause the species to become one?
A) When they are partial in the species.
B) When they are coextensive and one is essential, the other accidental.
C) When they are both essential.
D) When they are both accidental.

Key Takeaway
Two genera can coexist in different species if they are coextensive and distinguished by essential versus accidental attribution, but this raises a subtle point about the externality of the distinguishing aspect.

The Weakness of the Argument and its Clarification
Clarifies the weakness of an argument by explaining the impossibility of reciprocity in real essences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why reciprocity between genus and differentia is impossible in real essences and how this reveals the weakness of the argument.

Core Idea
Reciprocity between genus and differentia is impossible in real essences, but possible in conceptual ones.

This passage exposes the flaw in an earlier argument by showing that its reasoning would require reciprocity between genus and differentia, which is impossible for real essences. The commentator clarifies that the argument's weakness becomes apparent when we understand the nature of essential composition. We will examine the proof that confines essential composition to genus and differentia or coextensive parts, and contrast this with entitative essences.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the dense logical structure.
2
Identify the key claim about reciprocity
Find where the passage states that reciprocity entails generality and specificity from one aspect, and that this is impossible in real essences.
This is the core insight.
3
Understand the proof from confinement of the essential
Trace the proof: if the essential is not completely shared, it must be either not shared or coextensive, else infinite regress. This leads to the conclusion about composition of real essences.
This proof is a standard argument in logic.
4
Contrast real and entitative essences
Notice how the passage explains that entitative essences can have reciprocity because their components are conceptual. Ask how this contrast clarifies the weakness of the argument.
The argument assumed real essences, but reasoning would only work for entitative essences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ضعفه ظاهر) أي على الوجه الذي قرره بقوله : ويظهر حقيقته مما لخصناه، فإن ما علة تلك الفروع في نفس الأمر، وكون بعضها صحيحا وبعضها غير صحيح يظهر مما لخصه، فما أورده الشارح قدس سره من السؤال والجواب بيان لذلك. وكان الأولى إيراده بطريق التفسير بأن يقول بعد قوله : ويظهر حقيقته مما ذكرناه أما تعاكس الحال إلخ، وأن يترك لفظ : وضعفه كما لا يخفى . قوله : ( عليه ) أي على ما لخصناه . قوله : ( فيتحصل) بالآخر كالخاصة المركبة من العرضين العامين كالطائر الولود. قوله : ( إذ لم يجز أن يكون إلخ يعني أن التعاكس يستلزم أن يكون بينهما عموم وخصوص من وجه كما صوره الشرح قدس سره فيما سبق، وذلك ممتنع في الماهيات الحقيقية؛ لأن الدليل الذي أورده على انحصار الذاتي في الجنس والفصل حاصله : أنه إذا لم يكن الذاتي تمام المشترك فإما أن لا يكون مشتركاً أصلاً فيكون مختصاً بالماهية، أو يكون بعضاً من تمام المشترك مساوياً له، وإلا يلزم التسلسل في تمام المشتركات. ولما لم يمكن أن يكون لماهية واحدة جنسان في مرتبة واحدة يكون ذلك البعض المساوي داخلا في تمام المشترك الآخر الذي يكون ذلك البعض أعم منه فلا تركيب للماهية الحقيقية إلا من جنس وفصل مختص به أو من أمرين متساويين، بخلاف الماهية الاعتبارية فإنه يجوز أن يكون بعض تمام المشترك فيها أعم من كل تمام مشترك يفرض للماهية، ولا تنتهي سلسلة تمام المشتركات لكونها أموراً اعتبارية، فتكون الماهية المركبة منهما مركبة من أمرين بينهما عموم من وجه، لاجتماعهما في الماهية التي فرض تركيبها منهما، وتحقق تمام المشترك في النوع الذي هو بإزاء الماهية وتحقق البعض في النوع الذي فرض بإزاء تمام المشترك تحقيقاً للعموم . قوله: (فقد صار به (نوعاً لأن معنى التحصيل زوال إبهامه وصيرورته مطابقاً لتمام الماهية النوعية . قوله : مشتركان في الدليل وهو تخلف المعلول عن علته .
His statement: 'Its weakness is apparent' — i.e., according to the manner he determined by his saying: 'And its reality is shown by what we summarized.' For what is the cause of those branches in reality, and that some are correct and some are incorrect, is shown by what he summarized. So what the commentator (quddisa sirruh) mentioned of question and answer is an explanation of that. It would have been better to present it by way of interpretation by saying after his statement: 'And its reality is shown by what we mentioned' — 'As for reciprocity of the situation, etc.,' and to leave the phrase 'and its weakness' as is not hidden. His statement: 'upon it' — i.e., upon what we summarized. His statement: 'so it is obtained' by the other, like a property composed of two common accidents, like the bird that gives birth. His statement: 'since it is not possible that, etc.' — meaning that reciprocity entails that between them there is generality and specificity from one aspect, as the commentary (quddisa sirruh) depicted previously, and that is impossible in real essences; because the proof he presented for the confinement of the essential to genus and differentia is summarized as: if the essential is not the complete shared, then either it is not shared at all, so it is specific to the essence, or it is a part of the complete shared coextensive with it, otherwise an infinite regress in the complete shared would follow. Since it is not possible for a single essence to have two genera in one rank, that coextensive part would be included in the other complete shared which is more general than that part, so a real essence is composed only of a genus and a differentia specific to it, or of two coextensive things. In contrast to an entitative essence (al-mahiyya al-i'tibariyya), for it is permissible that some part of the complete shared therein is more general than every complete shared supposed for the essence, and the chain of complete shareds does not terminate because they are entitative matters. Thus the essence composed of them is composed of two things between which there is generality and specificity from one aspect, because they meet in the essence which is supposed to be composed of them, and the complete shared is realized in the species which corresponds to the essence, and the part is realized in the species supposed to correspond to the complete shared, realizing the generality. His statement: 'for it has become thereby a species' — because the meaning of 'determination' (tahsil) is the removal of its ambiguity and its becoming corresponding to the complete specific essence. His statement: 'they share in the proof' — and it is the effect lagging behind its cause.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage clarifies the weakness of the argument presented earlier. The commentator says that the strength or weakness of the branches is revealed by the earlier summary (talkhis) of the topics of genus, differentia, and causality. The author's statement 'its weakness is apparent' refers to the face that the commentator determined. He then discusses that it would have been better to present the explanation directly. The passage then delves into an extended discussion on the impossibility of reciprocity (ta'akus) between genus and differentia in real essences, because it would entail generality and specificity from one aspect, which is impossible for real essences. The proof is based on confining the essential to genus and differentia: if the essential is not the complete shared, it must be either not shared or a coextensive part, otherwise infinite regress. For real essences, composition is only from genus and specific differentia or from two coextensive things. In contrast, entitative essences (al-mahiyya al-i'tibariyya) can have such complexity because their components are conceptual. The passage ends by clarifying the meaning of 'determination' (tahsil) and reiterating that the shared proof is the impossibility of the effect lagging behind its cause.

Correction: The passage clarifies that real essences can only be composed from genus and specific differentia or coextensive parts, while entitative essences allow more complex compositions including generality-specificity from one aspect.

Key Takeaway
Reciprocity between genus and differentia is impossible in real essences due to the confinement of essential composition, but possible in entitative essences.

?

Applying Branches to the Summary: Reciprocity and Multiplicity
Answers whether the branches apply to the author's summary, discussing reciprocity and multiplicity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the branches of reciprocity between genus and differentia and multiplicity of proximate differentia apply to the author's logical summary, and the conditions under which they are permissible or not.

Core Idea
Reciprocity between genus and differentia is possible in concepts but not in real essences.

This passage addresses a specific objection: whether the previously discussed branches (like reciprocity and multiplicity) apply to the author's own summary of the subject. The answer distinguishes between two cases: the permissibility of reciprocity in certain conceptual contexts, and the impossibility of multiple proximate differentiae. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying logical rules to definitions and essences.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Notice the objection-and-answer structure.
2
Identify the two cases discussed
The answer treats two separate issues: reciprocity (تعاكس) between genus and differentia, and multiplicity of the proximate differentia (تعدد الفصل القريب). Notice how each is handled.
3
Understand the reasoning for each case
For reciprocity, the reason is that two concepts can mutually determine each other if each has ambiguity. For multiplicity, the reasoning shows why only one proximate differentia can determine a genus.
The commentary explains the key distinctions.
4
Connect to broader logic
Reflect on why this matters for definition and essential predication. The passage clarifies limits of logical composition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( فإن قلت: هل تتأتى هذه الفروع على ما لخصه أولا، قلت : أما تعاكس الحال بين الجنس والفصل فلا منع منه عليه؛ لجواز أن يكونا مفهومين في كل منهما إبهام من وجه، فيتحصل بالآخر. نعم يمتنع ذلك في الماهيات الحقيقية؛ إذ لم يجز أن يكون بين أجزائها عموم من وجه، وأما تعدد الفصل القريب فلا يجوز؛ لأن الواحد منهما إن تحصل به الجنس فقد صار به نوعاً وليس للآخر في حصول هذا النوع مدخل فيكون فصلاً خارجا عنه لا فصلاً مقوماً له. وإن لم يتحصل الجنس بأحدهما بل بهما معاً كانا فصلاً واحداً لا متعدداً. هذا إذا كانت قوله: (عليه) أي على ما لخصناه. قوله: (فيتحصل) بالآخر كالخاصة المركبة من العرضين العامين كالطائر الولود.
His statement: 'For if you say: Are these branches applicable to what he summarized first? I say: As for reciprocity of the situation between genus and differentia, there is no prevention of it upon it; because it is possible that they are two concepts, in each of which there is ambiguity from one aspect, so each is determined by the other. Yes, that is impossible in real essences; since it is not permissible that between their parts there be generality and specificity from one aspect. As for multiplicity of the proximate differentia, it is not permissible; because if the genus is determined by one of them, it has thereby become a species, and the other has no entry in the attainment of this species, so it would be a differentia external to it, not a constitutive differentia. And if the genus is not determined by either one but by both together, they would be one differentia, not multiple. This is when...' His statement: 'upon it' — i.e., upon what we summarized. His statement: 'so it is obtained' by the other, like a property composed of two common accidents, like the bird that gives birth.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific question: whether the branches discussed (like reciprocity and multiplicity of differentia) apply to the author's earlier summary. The answer distinguishes two cases: (1) Reciprocity (ta'akus) between genus and differentia is not prevented in the context of the summary, because it is possible that each concept has some ambiguity and they mutually determine each other. However, this is impossible in real essences (al-mahiyyat al-haqiqiyya), where parts cannot have generality and specificity from one aspect. (2) Multiplicity of the proximate differentia (ta'addud al-fasl al-qarib) is not permissible, because if the genus is determined by one differentia, it becomes a species and the other differentia is irrelevant; if the genus is not determined by either individually but only by both together, then they function as a single differentia, not multiple. The passage ends with an example of a property composed of two common accidents, like a bird that gives birth (a composite property).

تعدد الفصل القريب

خاصة مركبة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that reciprocity between genus and differentia is always impossible in logic.
Correction: The passage clarifies that reciprocity is only impossible in real essences, not in concepts (where mutual determination is possible).

Checkpoint

A) Because if one differentia determines the genus, the other becomes unnecessary and external, not constitutive.
B) Because multiple differentiae cause infinite regress.
C) Because the genus cannot be determined at all.
D) Because it violates the law of non-contradiction.

Key Takeaway
Reciprocity between genus and differentia is possible in conceptual contexts but not in real essences, and multiplicity of proximate differentia is logically impossible.
