A) Because non-existence cannot be predicated of anything.
B) Because if determination were non-existent, it would be absolute non-existence, which lacks distinction and would make the determined thing absolutely non-existent.
C) Because all attributes are existent.
D) Because determination is a property of quiddity, which is existent.

Key Takeaway
Determination (ta'ayyun) must be an existent attribute because it cannot be non-existential without leading to absurdity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

What would change if you fully embraced your determination as an existent attribute that Allah has given you?
?
Al-Razi argues that non-existence cannot ground distinction. In your daily life, do you define yourself more by what you lack or by what you are? How does this lesson challenge you to see your own existence and the existence of others as genuinely real and valuable?

Proof that Determination is Existential
The commentator proves that determination (ta'ayyun) cannot be nonexistential (adami).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why determination (ta'ayyun) must be an existential (wujudi) attribute rather than a nonexistential (adami) one, based on the logical argument from infinite regress.

Core Idea
Determination cannot be non-existence; assuming so leads to infinite regress.

The commentator presents a subtle logical argument proving that determination (ta'ayyun) is an existential attribute, not a mere negation. This is crucial for understanding the nature of entities in kalam. The argument uses the concept of lack-of-determination (la-ta'ayyun) and shows that assuming determination is nonexistential leads to an infinite regress or contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once through, following the translation. Notice how the commentator unpacks each part of the base text's statement.
2
Identify the two possibilities
The passage considers two possibilities for determination if it were a non-existence: either it is the non-existence of lack-of-determination (la-ta'ayyun) or the non-existence of another determination. Trace these in the text.
3
Understand the first branch: infinite regress
If determination were the non-existence of lack-of-determination, then lack-of-determination itself implies a determination (since it is defined as the absence of determination). This leads to an infinite chain of non-existences, which is impossible, so that determination must be existential.
4
Understand the second branch: similar reasoning
If determination were the non-existence of another determination, that other determination would also be a non-existence of something, again leading to an infinite regress or contradiction. Thus, it too must be existential.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Notice how the argument uses the principle that attributing a quality that has existence in the external world requires the existence of that quality. This seals the case that determination is existential.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وإما عدماً مضافاً ) أي إلى شيء مخصوص، ولا شك أنه يكون عدماً لشيء ينافيه وهو إما اللاتعين الذي هو نقيض ذلك التعين المخصوص، أو التعين الاخر إذ ما سواهما من المفهومات يمكن اجتماعه منه فإن اللاتعين المطلق يصدق على كل تعين مخصوص ضرورة سلب تعين آخر عنه وكل مفهوم ما سوى التعين يمكن عروض التعين له . اللاتعين قوله: (فيكون هو وجودياً) أي يكون التعين الذي هو عدم اللاتعين وجودياً لأن التعين الذي اعتبر في مفهوم اللاتعين وجودي؛ لأنه لو كان عدمياً لكان عدماً للاتعين؛ لأنه المفروض، وهذا اللاتعين أيضاً مشتمل على التعين الذي هو عدم اللاتعين، وهكذا فيلزم اشتمال اللاتعين الذي فرض التعين عدما له على أعدام غير متناهية فلا يكون التعين الذي اعتبر في عدمياً، وإذا كان هذا التعين وجودياً كان التعين الذي فرض أنه عدم اللاتعين وجودياً؛ لأنه عينه لما عرفت من أنه لو لم يكن عينه لم يكن اللاتعين منافياً له . قوله : ( فذلك التعين الآخر إن كان عدماً تقدير الكلام فذلك التعين الآخر إن كان عدمياً كان عدماً لشيء. قوله فهو (وجود) فيكون وجودياً بناء على مساواة الوجود الوجودي لمساواة العدمي بالعدم . قوله : ( والتعين الآخر مثله أي في كونه تعيناً سواء كان ذاتياً لهما أو عرضياً . قوله: (فيكون هو أيضاً وجودياً) بناء على ما تقرر من أن اتصاف شيء بصفة من شأنها الوجود في الخارج فرع وجود الصفة، وإلا لجاز اتصاف الجسم بالحركة المعدومة وهو سفسطة
His saying: 'or a non-existence that is added' i.e., to something specific, and there is no doubt that it is a non-existence of something that contradicts it, and it is either the lack-of-determination (la-ta'ayyun) which is the opposite of that specific determination (ta'ayyun), or the other determination, since other than these two concepts can be combined with it. For absolute lack-of-determination applies to every specific determination necessarily because another determination is negated from it, and every concept other than determination can have determination occur to it. Lack-of-determination. His saying: 'so it would be existential (wujudi)' i.e., the determination that is the non-existence of lack-of-determination is existential because the determination that is considered in the concept of lack-of-determination is existential; for if it were nonexistential (adami), it would be a non-existence of lack-of-determination because that is assumed, and this lack-of-determination also includes the determination that is the non-existence of lack-of-determination, and so on, thus necessitating that the lack-of-determination which is assumed to have determination as its non-existence include infinite non-existences, so the determination considered in [lack-of-determination] is not nonexistential. And when this determination is existential, then the determination that is assumed to be the non-existence of lack-of-determination is existential because it is the same as it, as you know that if it were not the same, then lack-of-determination would not contradict it. His saying: 'then that other determination if it is non-existence' the implied phrase is: then that other determination if it is nonexistential, it is a non-existence of something. His saying: 'so it is existence' so it is existential based on the equality of existential existence to the equality of nonexistential with non-existence. His saying: 'and the other determination is like it' i.e., in being a determination, whether it is essential to both or accidental. His saying: 'so it also is existential' based on what has been established that the attribution of something to a quality whose nature is existence in the external world is a branch of the existence of the quality, otherwise it would be permissible to attribute a body with a non-existent motion, which is sophistry.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is a proof that determination (ta'ayyun) must be existential (wujudi). The commentator explains the meaning of a statement from the base text. The argument begins by considering the possibility that determination is a non-existence that is added (i.e., relative). It must be a non-existence of something that contradicts it, which is either the lack-of-determination (la-ta'ayyun) or another determination. First, if it is the non-existence of lack-of-determination, then lack-of-determination itself includes a determination (since it is defined as the negation of determination), leading to an infinite regress of non-existences unless that determination is existential. Second, if it is the non-existence of another determination, that other determination, being nonexistential, would also be a non-existence of something, and by similar reasoning must be existential. The commentator then explains each sub-statement, concluding that determination cannot be nonexistential without contradiction.

Correction: The passage carefully distinguishes between 'adami' (nonexistential) and 'adam' (non-existence). Determination being nonexistential means it is a non-existence of something specific, not pure nothingness.

Checkpoint

C) It would make determination identical to existence.
D) It would cause all things to be indeterminate.

Key Takeaway
Determination (ta'ayyun) must be existential because assuming it is nonexistential leads to an infinite regress or contradiction.

?

What would change today if you grounded your identity in the existential gift of being a believer?

Take a moment to thank Allah for making you specifically you, and commit to seeing yourself as a positive creation, not just a negation of faults.
?
The proof warns that assuming determination as nonexistential leads to absurdity. The Objection Answered: Determination is Not Necessarily Non-existence
The commentator addresses the objection that determination being nonexistential leads to a contradiction, and gives the initial response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the objection that determination could be nonexistential is refuted by clarifying the meaning of 'adami.

Core Idea
'Adami does not mean non-existence; it is a relative predicate.

In this passage, the commentator addresses a key objection to the proof that determination (ta'ayyun) is existential. The objector argues that if determination were nonexistential, it would lead to a contradiction, but the commentator shows that the term 'adami does not imply non-existence in the same way. Instead, 'adami is contrasted with 'wujudi' as a relative notion.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Carefully read the objector's argument that if determination is 'adami, then it would be non-existence, leading to a contradiction.
Notice the objector uses the terms 'adami and wujudi.
2
Identify the core claim
The objector claims that if determination is nonexistential, it must be non-existence, but the commentator denies this implication.
The key is the meaning of 'adami.
3
Examine the response
The commentator responds that 'adami is opposed to 'wujudi, but that does not mean it is non-existence. He explains the intended meaning of 'wujudi in this context.
The response relies on the distinction between concept and referent.

Source Text

( والجواب : لا نسلم أنه لو كان ( التعين ( عدمياً لكان عدماً)، وإنما يلزم ذلك إذا كان العدمي بمعنى العدم أو مستلزماً له، وهو ممنوع؛ لأن العدمي يقابل الوجودي، كما أن العدم يقابل الوجود، فلو كان العدمي عدماً لكان الوجودي وجوداً، وليس كذلك بل المراد بالوجودي ما يكون ثبوته لموصوفه بوجوده له أي الوجودي هذا المقام، سوى ما ذكره المصنف من منع الملازمة من أن العدمي لا يلزم أن يكون عدماً كما لا يخفى على من تأمل وأجاد . قوله : (بمعنى العدم وعلى هذا التقدير تكون الملازمة بينهما بحسب التغاير الاعتباري. قوله : ( أو مستلزماً له) بحيث يصدق عليه. قوله : ( لكان الوجودي وجوداً إذ لو كان غيره لم يصدق الوجود عليه، فيصدق العدم عليه مع عدم صدق العدمي عليه لصدق الوجودي عليه قوله : ( بل المراد إلخ) تقدير الكلام بل أعم منه لأن المراد بالوجودي إلخ . قوله : ( ما يكون ثبوته لموصوفه بوجوده (له) إن كان وجود العرض في نفسه هو وجوده في الموصوف، كما اختاره المحقق التفتازاني وصرح به الشيخ الرئيس فثبوت شيء لشيء أعم من عليه نفس الوجود والعدم فكذلك، وإن كان ما صدق عليه الوجود والعدم بالاشتقاق فنختار أن ذلك التعين معدوم، ولا يلزم أن يكون هذا التعين وجوداً؛ لأن عدم المعدوم ليس بوجود ولا موجود كما أشرنا إليه . مع جواز قوله : ( والتعين الآخر مثله إن أراد بالمثلية المشاركة في التعينية فلا يتوهم من وجودية أحد المثلين بهذا المعنى وجودية الآخر، وإن أراد الاتفاق في الماهية فلا نسلم المثلية، لم لا يجوز أن تكون التعينات متخلفة في الماهية متشاركة في عارض هو مفهوم التعين، وعلى تقدير تسليمها لا يلزم من وجود أحد المتماثلات وجود جميعها، فإن زيداً وعمراً مثلان اتصاف أحدهما بالوجود والآخر بالعدم قوله : ( أو مستلزماً له بحيث يحمل عليه مواطأة، وإلا فلزوم ذلك ممنوع حينئذ. قوله : ( لكان الوجودي وجوداً) قد يمنع ذلك لجواز أن يتصف المتقابلان بشيء واحد، كالامتناع واللا امتناع المتصفين بالعدم وجوابه : أن ليس المراد بقوله : فلو كان العدمي عدماً أنه لو كان متصفاً بالعدم، بل أنه لو كان بمعنى العدم أو مستلزماً لحمله عليه مواطأة، فمنع الملازمة على هذا مكابرة، فتأمل. قوله : (بل المراد بالوجودي إلخ) فسره ليعلم مقابله الذي هو المقصود بالبيان أصالة، أعني العدمي، والمراد أن الوجودي من الصفات ما ذكره بقرينة قوله : الموصوفه، والتخصيص بناء على أن الكلام في وجودية التعين الذي هو من الأمور الغير المستقلة
And know that the exposition of the aforementioned proof according to what we have written repels all the doubts that the investigators have raised in his saying: 'so it is existential' – there is a denial of it, its basis being the issue of impossibility and non-impossibility. His saying: 'or that it is a non-existence of another determination' – if by determination and lack-of-determination their concepts are meant, then there is no exclusive enumeration; because it is possible that determination is a non-existence of another concept. And if what is meant is their referents, then we do not grant that the referent of lack-of-determination is nonexistential, so its opposite would be positive. How can it be, when lack-of-determination applies to realities other than determination? His saying: 'so this is non-existence of non-existence, so it is existence' – in it, the concept of non-existence is other than existence, and likewise its referent. Also, if what is meant by existence and non-existence in his saying 'if it were non-existence' and 'if it were existence' is the concept of non-existence and existence, then the exclusive enumeration is denied, and the author will also bring it up concerning the principle of the implication. And if what is meant is the referent, then this too is existence. So it is established that determination being nonexistential necessitates it being existential. This is a contradiction, so it is existential. (The answer: We do not grant that if determination were nonexistential it would be a non-existence; this follows only if 'nonexistential' is in the sense of non-existence or implies it, and this is denied; because 'nonexistential' is contrasted with 'existential', just as non-existence is contrasted with existence. For if the nonexistential were non-existence, then the existential would be existence, but it is not so. Rather, by 'existential' is meant what has subsistence for its subject by its existence, i.e., the existential in this context – apart from what the author mentioned in denying the implication that the nonexistential does not have to be non-existence, as is not hidden from one who reflects and does well. His saying: 'in the sense of non-existence' – and on this assumption, the implication between them is according to notional difference. His saying: 'or implies it' such that it applies to it. His saying: 'then the existential would be existence' – for if it were otherwise, existence would not apply to it, so non-existence would apply to it while the nonexistential does not apply to it due to the existential applying to it. His saying: 'rather, the meaning is etc.' – the implied phrase is: rather it is more general than that, because by 'existential' etc. His saying: 'what has subsistence for its subject by its existence' – if the existence of the accident in itself is its existence in the subject, as chosen by al-Muhaqqiq al-Taftazani and stated by the Chief (Ibn Sina), then the subsistence of something for something is more general than existence and non-existence themselves, so it is likewise. And if what is meant is what existence and non-existence apply to by derivation, then we choose that that determination is non-existent, and it does not necessitate that this determination is existence; because the non-existence of the non-existent is not existence nor existent, as we have indicated. Along with the permissibility of his saying: 'and the other determination is like it' – if he means by similarity sharing in determination-ness, then one should not imagine from the existentiality of one of the two similars in this sense the existentiality of the other. And if he means agreement in quiddity, then we do not grant the similarity; why is it not permissible that determinations differ in quiddity while sharing in an accident which is the concept of determination? And on the assumption of granting it, the existence of one of the similars does not necessitate the existence of all of them; for Zayd and 'Amr are two similars, one of them being described with existence and the other with non-existence. His saying: 'or implies it such that it applies to it by way of agreement' – otherwise, the necessity of that is denied at that time. His saying: 'then the existential would be existence' – one may deny that because it is possible for two opposites to be described with one thing, like impossibility and non-impossibility being described with non-existence. And its answer: that what is meant by his saying 'if the nonexistential were non-existence' is not that it is described with non-existence, but that it is in the sense of non-existence or implies its application to it by way of agreement, so denying the implication on this is obstinacy, so reflect. His saying: 'rather, the meaning is etc.' – he interpreted it so that its counterpart which is the primary object of explanation is known, namely the nonexistential. And the meaning is that the existential is among the attributes what he mentioned, by the indication of his saying: 'its subject' – and the specification is based on the fact that the discussion is about the existentiality of determination, which is among non-independent matters.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is an objection and response sequence defending the proof that determination is existential. The commentator first notes that his exposition repels doubts. The objection challenges the claim that if determination is nonexistential it leads to contradiction. The objector argues that the term 'nonexistential' (adami) may not imply non-existence (adam) in the same way; it could be a relative notion. The response clarifies that 'adami is opposed to 'wujudi' (existential), and what is meant by 'wujudi' is what subsists by its existence in a subject. The explanation distinguishes between the sense of 'adami as 'adam itself or what implies it. Further objections about similarity (mithliyya) between determinations are addressed: similarity in being determinations does not entail existentiality of all, and even if they are similar in quiddity, the existence of one does not necessitate existence of another. The passage concludes by defining 'wujudi' as an attribute that is dependent on a subject, since the discussion concerns the existentiality of determination which is not an independent entity.

Key Terms
عدمي (adami)
وجودي (wujudi)
عدم (adam)
وجود (wujud)
تعين (ta'ayyun)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The term 'adami always means non-existence (adam).
Correction: In this context, 'adami is opposed to 'wujudi and does not necessarily imply non-existence; it is a relative predicate.

Checkpoint
What is the objector's main argument?
A) Determination is clearly existential.
B) If determination is nonexistential, it must be non-existence, leading to a contradiction.
C) The terms are unclear.
D) The proof is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The key move in the response is to deny that 'adami (nonexistential) is equivalent to 'adam (non-existence); instead, 'adami is a relative term contrasted with 'wujudi.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever mistaken a relative description (like 'adami) for an absolute judgment (like 'adam), leading to a misunderstanding in your own beliefs? How will you guard against that kind of conflation in your study of theology?
?
This lesson reveals that precision in definitions can save one from contradictions. Where in your own understanding of Islamic theology might you be unwittingly confusing terms? What step will you take this week to clarify one such term?
?
The commentator says the response is 'not hidden from one who reflects and does well.' When was the last time you truly reflected on a theological concept until you grasped its nuance? Will you commit to deeper reflection on the next difficult topic you encounter?

Understanding 'Adami and 'Wujudi: The Full Clarification
The commentator provides a precise definition of 'wujudi, addresses the similarity objection, and concludes the discussion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the precise meanings of 'adami and 'wujudi in kalam discourse, and how the issue of similarity between determinations is resolved.

Core Idea
'Wujudi means an attribute that subsists through its existence in a subject; similarity does not entail shared existentiality.

This passage extends the response by clarifying the definitions of 'existential' and 'nonexistential' and addressing an additional objection about similar determinations. The commentator explains that 'wujudi in this context refers to attributes that are not independent but subsist in a subject. He then addresses the worry that if two determinations are similar, the existentiality of one would imply the existentiality of the other, showing why this does not follow.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition
Focus on the commentator's definition of 'wujudi': 'what has subsistence for its subject by its existence'. Understand how this applies to determination.
This definition is key to the entire argument.
2
Analyze the similarity objection
The objector raises the issue of two similar determinations: if one is existential, does the other have to be? The commentator explains that similarity in being determinations does not require agreement in quiddity or existentiality.
The example of Zayd and 'Amr illustrates this.
3
Confirm the definitions
Review how the commentator distinguishes between the concept of 'adami and its referent, and why this resolves the initial objection.

The Circularity Argument on Essence Portion Discrimination
Objection and answer on the dependence of discrimination of an essence portion on individuation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the circularity argument regarding the dependence of the discrimination of a portion of quiddity on individuation, and the proper resolution that avoids it.

Core Idea
Distinguishing portions of the same quiddity requires individuation, but careful analysis avoids circularity.

This passage presents a subtle objection in Islamic metaphysics: if a portion of quiddity can only be distinguished from another portion by individuation, and individuation itself requires prior distinction, then we face circularity. The author presents and refutes a common answer before offering the proper resolution. Let's examine the argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the first sentence of the passage which states the circularity problem. Ask yourself: why does discrimination of a portion depend on conjunction with individuation?
The objection assumes that without prior discrimination, individuation cannot preferentially attach to one portion.
2
Identify the initial answer and its flaw
The passage gives an initial answer: quiddity is distinguished by itself. But the author notes this misses the point—what matters is distinguishing portions of the same quiddity, not quiddity from others.
3
Grasp the proper resolution
The proper answer involves temporal simultaneity between conjunction and discrimination, and the conceptual nature of conjunction. Understand why this avoids circularity.
The key is that the conjunction is mental, not external.
4
Note the final rejection
The passage ends by rejecting the claim that the answer works if individuation is privative. This shows the depth of the discussion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تميزها وتميزها موقوف على انضمامه إليها فيدور وأجيب عنه: بأن الماهية ممتازة عن غيرها بذاتها لا بانضمام التعين إليها. وفيه نظر؛ إذ مرادهم امتياز حصة من الماهية عن حصة أخرى منها؛ إذ لولا امتياز إحداهما عن الأخرى لم يكن اختصاص التعين بإحداهما وانضمامه إليها أولى من العكس. وذلك أي امتياز الحصة عن الحصة إنما يكون بالتعين لا بذات الماهية، بل الجواب أن يقال: الانضمام مع الامتياز زماناً، وإن كان متقدماً عليه ذاتاً، ولا استحالة في ذلك، كما في اختصاص الفصول بحصص الأجناس وتوضيحه أن التعين أو الفصل ينضم انتزاعياً، فلا انضمام في الخارج حتى يتوقف على تميزها والانضمام في الذهن وإن توقف على تميزها وتصورها لكن تميزها الذهني لا يتوقف على انضمامه إليها، بل على انتزاعه منها. فما قيل: إنه جار على تقدير كونه عدمياً أيضاً وهم.
Its discrimination and its discrimination are dependent on its conjunction with it, so there is circularity. And it was answered: That quiddity is distinguished from other than itself by its essence, not by conjunction of individuation with it. But there is consideration in this answer; because what they mean is the distinction of a portion of quiddity from another portion of it; for if there were no distinction of one from the other, the specification of individuation with one of them and its conjunction with it would not be more appropriate than the opposite. And that, i.e., the distinction of the portion from the portion, is only by individuation, not by the quiddity's essence. Rather, the answer is to say: The conjunction [occurs] simultaneously with the distinction temporally, even if it is prior to it in essence, and there is no impossibility in that, as in the specification of differentiae with the portions of genera. And its clarification is that individuation or differentia is conjoined conceptually, so there is no external conjunction such that it is dependent on their distinction; and conjunction in the mind, even if it depends on their distinction and conception, their mental distinction does not depend on its conjunction with them, but on its abstraction from them. So what was said—that it holds on the assumption that it is also privative—is an illusion.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer sequence concerning the dependence of the discrimination of a portion of quiddity on individuation. The objector first argues that if the discrimination of a portion of quiddity is dependent on the conjunction of individuation with it, and individuation's conjunction with that portion is in turn dependent on prior discrimination (otherwise why that portion rather than another?), then circularity results. The answer given is that the quiddity is distinguished from others by itself, not by individuation. But the commentator notes that this misses the point: what is at stake is the distinction of one portion of the same quiddity from another portion, not the quiddity from something else. That intra-species distinction cannot be by the quiddity's essence alone because the essence is common; it requires individuation. So the proper answer is to say that the conjunction of individuation with a portion occurs simultaneously with discrimination, not before it, in a temporal sense, even if in essence the conjunction is prior. This avoids circularity because the conjunction is not external but mental (conceptual); in the mind, the discrimination of the portion does not depend on the conjunction of individuation but on its abstraction. The passage ends by rejecting the claim that this answer also works if individuation is privative, calling it an illusion.

Key Terms
تميز
الماهية
التعين
انضمام
حصة
انتزاع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that saying 'quiddity is distinguished by itself' solves the circularity problem.
Correction: That answer only works for distinguishing quiddity from other quiddities, not for distinguishing portions of the same quiddity, which is the actual issue.

Checkpoint
What is the main point of the objection in this passage?
A) Individuation must be external to avoid circularity.
B) The discrimination of a portion of quiddity cannot be prior to individuation without leading to circularity.
C) Quiddity is distinguished by itself.
D) The conjunction of individuation is simultaneous with discrimination.

Key Takeaway
The proper resolution to the circularity objection lies in recognizing that conjunction and distinction can be simultaneous temporally, and that individuation is a conceptual abstraction, not an external conjunction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you mentally separate one person from another, do you assume the distinction is inherent in them or that you are adding a conceptual label? How does this lesson's claim that discrimination can be simultaneous with conjunction challenge your usual way of categorizing people?
?
Think of a belief you hold about your own identity that you thought was based on your essence alone. Can you identify an aspect of that identity that actually depends on a conceptual addition (like a label or role) which you might have assumed was intrinsic? How does this lesson's resolution of circularity help you see the relationship between your essence and those additions differently?
?
The passage resolves a logical circularity by appealing to temporal simultaneity and conceptual abstraction. Is there a tension in your life where you feel stuck between two dependencies (e.g., 'I need to change my habits to change my character, but I need to change my character to change my habits')? How might the lesson's insight—that two things can be interdependent yet not circular if viewed temporally—open a way forward for you?

Second Argument Against External Individuation: Infinite Regress and Its Critique
Argument, answer, critique, and counter-objection on external individuation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second argument against external individuation, the proposed answer, the author's critique, and the initial counter-objection involving the Necessary Being.

Core Idea
If individuation is external, it needs another individuation, leading to an infinite regress.

This passage presents a key debate in Islamic philosophy: can individuation (ta‘ayyun) be an external entity? The second argument claims that if it were, it would itself require individuation, causing an infinite regress. An answer based on distinguishing essence versus accident is offered, but the author criticizes it by arguing that each individuation has a universal quiddity. The passage ends with an incomplete objection invoking the Necessary Being.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow, then read the translation. Note the different voices: the objector, the answerer, the author (al-Jurjani), and a subsequent objector.
The passage ends abruptly; the last sentence is incomplete.
2
Identify the argument and its structure
The second argument is presented first. Identify the logical steps: if individuation is external → it needs another individuation → infinite regress. Then note the answer given: common concept of individuation is an accident, individuals are distinguished by their own essences.
The answer tries to avoid regress by saying no additional individuation is needed if essence itself distinguishes.
3
Understand the author's critique
The author (al-Jurjani / the commentator) critiques the answer: every individual of individuation has a universal quiddity (mahiyya kulliyya) in the mind, so distinguishing essence alone is not sufficient. This restores the regress argument.
The critique hinges on the idea that universality is inherent in any external existent.
4
Examine the counter-objection (incomplete)
A new objector denies that every individuation has a universal quiddity, citing the Necessary Being as an exception. The passage breaks off before the full objection is given.
Think about why the Necessary Being might be an exception: it has no universal quiddity in the sense of being shared.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه الثاني: لو كان التعين موجوداً خارجياً لكان معيناً، فإن كل موجود خارجي لا بد أن يكون متعيناً في نفسه، فهو أي كل واحد من التعين مشارك للتعينات الأخر في كونها تعيناً ويمتاز عنها بتعين آخر يخصه فيتسلسل، إذ ننقل الكلام إلى ذلك التعين الآخر. وأجيب عنه: بأن كونه تعيناً أي مفهوم التعين المشترك بين التعينات أمر عارض للتعينات، وهي متمايزة بذواتها المخصوصة والمحوج إلى التمايز بتعين زائد هو الاشتراك في الماهية دون الاشتراك في العوارض. قال المصنف: وفيه نظر؛ لأن كل تعين أي كل فرد من أفراد التعين فله ماهية كلية في العقل ضرورة؛ لأن كل موجود في الخارج كذلك، سواء كان له ما يشاركه في نوعه أم لا بل انحصر نوعه في شخصه، وتعينه غير ماهيته؛ لأنه لا يقبل الشركة بخلاف ماهيته ويتم الدليل بلزوم التسلسل، ولقائل أن يقول: لا نسلم أن كل تعين له ماهية كلية ينتزعها العقل من هويته، ودعوى الضرورة هاهنا غير مسموعة كيف والقاعدة القائلة بأن كل موجود خارجي كذلك منقوض عندهم بالواجب تعالى، بل كل فرد من أفراد التعين هو في
The second aspect: If individuation were an external existent, it would be determinate, for every external existent must be determinate in itself; so each one of the individuations shares with the other individuations in being an individuation and is distinguished from them by another individuation specific to it, leading to infinite regress, for we transfer the discussion to that other individuation. And it was answered: That it is an individuation, i.e., the common concept of individuation among individuations, is an accident of the individuations, and they are distinguished by their particular essences, and what necessitates distinction by an additional individuation is commonality in quiddity, not commonality in accidents. The author said: But there is consideration in this; because every individuation, i.e., every individual of the individuals of individuation, has a universal quiddity in the mind necessarily, because every existent in the outside is likewise, whether or not it has something sharing its type, even if its type is confined to its individual; and its individuation is other than its quiddity because it does not accept commonality unlike its quiddity; and the proof is completed by the necessity of infinite regress. And someone may say: We do not accept that every individuation has a universal quiddity abstracted by the mind from its identity, and the claim of necessity here is not heard, for how, when the rule that every external existent is like that is refuted by them in the case of the Necessary Exalted; rather, every individual of the individuals of individuation is in...
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage presents the second argument against the external existence of individuation: if individuation were an external entity, it would itself require individuation, leading to an infinite regress. The answer given is that 'being an individuation' is a common accident, and the individuals of individuation are distinguished by their own particular essences, not by an additional individuation; the need for another individuation arises only when there is commonality in quiddity, not in accidents. The author (al-Jurjani or the commentator) criticizes this answer: every individual of individuation must have a universal quiddity in the mind, because every external existent does, even if it is a unique species; thus the distinction cannot be by essence alone, and the regress argument stands. He concludes that the proof is complete. Then a counter-objection is introduced: one may deny that every individuation has a universal quiddity, rejecting the necessity claimed, since the rule 'every external existent has a universal quiddity' is violated by the Necessary Being (God) in the philosophers' view; thus the critique fails. The passage ends abruptly at the page break, leaving the counter-objection incomplete.

الموجود الخارجي
ماهية كلية
تسلسل
عوارض
الواجب تعالى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many mistakenly think that the answer 'individuals are distinguished by their essences' fully resolves the infinite regress problem.
Correction: The author shows that even if individuals are distinguished by essences, those essences themselves are universal quiddities that require further individuation, thus the regress remains.

Checkpoint

B) The answer fails because each individuation has a universal quiddity, so distinguishing essence is not sufficient.
C) The answer fails because infinite regress is not a problem.
D) The answer fails because the Necessary Being also has a universal quiddity.

Key Takeaway
The argument that external individuation leads to infinite regress is defended against a counter-answer by showing that every individuation has a universal quiddity, thus the regress is not avoided.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Are you living as if your identity is self-grounded, or do you constantly turn to Allah as the One who defines your reality? What would need to change today for you to live with this awareness?

The dialectic about individuation ultimately points to the Necessary Being as the exception. When you engage in deep theological reasoning, do you let it increase your reliance on Allah, or does it remain an intellectual exercise? ?
The counter-objection denies that every external existent has a universal quiddity, citing the Necessary Being. Repent of your mental constructs and commit to knowing Him through His attributes as revealed, not as you imagine.

Second Argument Against External Individuation: Infinite Regress, Response, and Criticism
Al-Jurjani presents the second argument, its answer, and a criticism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the infinite regress argument against external individuation, the response that ta'ayyun is an accident, and the criticism that every ta'ayyun still has a quiddity requiring further individuation.

Core Idea
Every external existent needs individuation, but if individuation itself is an external existent, it generates an infinite regress.

This passage presents the second theological argument against the view that individuation (ta'ayyun) exists as an external entity. Al-Jurjani explains the argument, the standard response, and then a criticism of that response from the author of al-Mawaqif. Following the reasoning carefully reveals deep questions about quiddity, accident, and individuation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Let the overall flow of argument, response, and criticism come through before you interpret.
Notice the three distinct parts: argument, answer, criticism.
2
Identify the infinite regress argument
Find the core logic: if ta'ayyun is an external thing, it itself needs a ta'ayyun, leading to an endless chain.
3
Understand the response
The response says the common concept of ta'ayyun is an accident, not a quiddity, so the regress is avoided because accidents don't require the same kind of individuation.
4
Examine the criticism
The author of al-Mawaqif argues that every instance of ta'ayyun has a universal quiddity distinct from itself, so the regress still applies.
This is the key twist: even if ta'ayyun is an accident, it still has a quiddity that needs individuation.
5
Reflect on the implications
Consider how this debate affects the distinction between essence and existence, and why theologians argued about the nature of individuation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه الثاني : لو كان التعين ( موجوداً) خارجياً (لكان معيناً)، فإن كل موجود خارجي لا بد أن يكون متعيناً في نفسه، (فهو) أي كل واحد من التعين ( مشارك للتعينات ) الأخر ( في كونها تعينا ويمتاز عنها بتعين) آخر يخصه (فيتسلسل)، إذ ننقل الكلام إلى ذلك التعين الآخر. ( وأجيب عنه : بأن كونه تعيناً) أي مفهوم التعين المشترك بين التعينات أمر ( عارض للتعينات)، وهي متمايزة بذواتها المخصوصة ) والمحوج إلى التمايز بتعين زائد هو الاشتراك في الماهية ) دون الاشتراك في العوارض قال المصنف : ( وفيه نظر؛ لأن كل تعين) أي كل فرد من أفراد التعين (فله) ماهية كلية في العقل ضرورة ) ؛ لأن كل موجود في الخارج كذلك، ( سواء كان له ما يشاركه في نوعه أم لا بل انحصر نوعه في شخصه. ) وتعينه غير ماهيته؛ لأنه لا يقبل الشركة بخلاف ماهيته
The second aspect: if individuation were an externally existing thing, it would be individuated, for every externally existing thing must be individuated in itself. (So) each individual of individuation (participates in that it is an individuation and distinguishes itself from others) by another individuation specific to it, thus leading to infinite regress, for we transfer the discussion to that other individuation. And it was answered: that its being an individuation (i.e., the common concept of individuation among individuations) is an accident of the individuations, and they are distinguished by their specific substances, and the need for additional distinction by an extra individuation is due to sharing in quiddity, not sharing in accidents. The author said: 'There is a problem with this; because every individuation (i.e., every individual of individuation) has a universal quiddity in the mind necessarily, because every externally existing thing is like that, whether it has something sharing its species or not, rather its species is confined to its individual. Its individuation is other than its quiddity because it does not admit sharing contrary to its quiddity.'
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is an objection, answer, and criticism structure. First, the second argument against the existence of individuation (ta'ayyun) as an external entity is presented: if ta'ayyun were an externally existing thing, it would itself need to be individuated. This would require another ta'ayyun to distinguish each ta'ayyun from others, leading to an infinite regress (tasalsul). The response (the answer) is then given: the common concept of ta'ayyun is an accident (arid) that attaches to the individuations, which are already distinguished by their specific substances. The need for an additional ta'ayyun arises only when there is sharing in quiddity (mahiyya), not in accidental attributes. The author (al-Mawaqif's author) then criticizes this response, saying that every individual instance of ta'ayyun necessarily has a universal quiddity that the mind abstracts, since every external existent has such a quiddity. This holds whether or not there are other individuals sharing its species. Thus, the ta'ayyun of each instance is not its quiddity, so the regress argument still applies because the ta'ayyun itself requires a distinguishing factor.

Key Terms
تعين (ta'ayyun)
موجود (mawjud)
ماهية (mahiyya)
عارض (arid)
تسلسل (tasalsul)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking that making ta'ayyun an accident (arid) solves the infinite regress.
Correction: The criticism shows that each ta'ayyun still has a quiddity, which requires further individuation, so the regress persists.

Checkpoint
What is the central problem raised in the second argument against the existence of individuation as an external thing?
A) It leads to a circular definition.
B) It leads to an infinite regress.
C) It contradicts divine simplicity.
D) It makes individuation an accident.

Key Takeaway
Individuation cannot be an external existent because it would require endless further individuation, and even the response that it is an accident fails since each individuation has its own quiddity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think about the ways you seek to distinguish yourself from others—through achievements, possessions, or roles. This lesson argues that external individuation leads to infinite regress. If your identity depends on such external markers, how can you ever feel truly secure? What one change in your perspective could anchor your sense of self in something that does not require further justification?
?
The passage shows that even the response of making ta'ayyun an accident fails because every individuation has a quiddity that demands a further distinction. Consider: are there aspects of your life where you rely on 'accidental' labels (like job title or social status) to define who you are, while ignoring your unchanging quiddity before Allah? How would your daily actions change if you prioritized your essential self over external distinctions?
?
The criticism reveals that no external individuation can be self-sufficient—it always points beyond itself. In your own life, what 'external individuators' have you assumed would give you lasting definition? Confess one such attachment and commit to releasing it by focusing on the only thing that truly individuates you: your unique soul created by Allah.

The Verbal Nature of the Dispute on Individuation
Al-Jurjani completes the proof, introduces an objection, and concludes the dispute is verbal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the disagreement between the mutakallimun and philosophers about individuation is essentially verbal, not substantive.

Core Idea
The dispute over individuation is merely verbal; both sides agree it is identical to external identity.

This passage completes the proof of infinite regress and then presents an objection that challenges the universal scope of the rule. The author then resolves the entire debate by showing that the apparent disagreement rests on a misunderstanding of what the philosophers mean by 'existence' of individuation. You will see how careful attention to terms reveals that the two schools are actually saying the same thing.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the full translation. Notice the flow: completion of proof, objection, and resolution.
The objector's speech starts with 'ولقائل أن يقول'.
2
Identify the objection's core
The objector denies that every individuation has a universal quiddity, using the Necessary Existent as a counterexample. Understand why this challenges the mutakallimun's argument.
The Necessary Existent has no quiddity, so the rule fails for Him.
3
Understand the verbal resolution
The author explains that the mutakallimun's arguments assume individuation is added to quiddity, while the philosophers consider it identical. Since both accept that individuation is the external identity, the dispute is merely verbal.
The key phrase is 'فإذن النزاع لفظي'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويتم الدليل بلزوم التسلسل ولقائل أن يقول : لا نسلم أن كل تعين له ماهية كلية ينتزعها العقل من هويته، ودعوى الضرورة هاهنا غير مسموعة كيف والقاعدة القائلة بأن كل موجود خارجي كذلك منقوض عندهم بالواجب تعالى بل كل فرد من أفراد التعين هو في نفسه بحيث إذا لاحظه العقل لم يمكن له فرض اشتراكه ، ولا تفصيله إلى ماهية قابلة للاشتراك، وأمر زائد عليها مانع من الشركة على قياس تفصيله لأفراد الإنسان. والحق : أن هذين الدليلين الخلفيين للمتكلمين على كون التعين عدمياً مبنيان على كون التعين أمراً منضماً إلى الماهية في الخارج ممتازاً فيه عنها، وقد علمت أنه نفس الهوية الخارجية ذاتاً وجعلاً ووجوداً . وهذا أي كون التعين ممتازاً الماهية في الخارج منضماً إليها بحيث يتحصل منهما هوية مركبة فيه، هو الذي حاول المتكلمون نفيه فإن هذا النفي هو اللازم مما استدلوا به من الوجهين. فإذن النزاع لفظي ، فإن الحكماء يدعون أن التعين أمر موجود، على أنه عين الماهية
And the proof is completed by the necessity of infinite regress. And one may say: we do not grant that every individuation has a universal quiddity that the mind abstracts from its identity, and the claim of necessity here is not listened to, for the rule that every externally existing thing is like that is refuted by them with regard to the Necessary Exalted. Rather, every individual of individuation is in itself such that when the mind observes it, it cannot conceive sharing it, nor analyze it into a quiddity capable of sharing, and an additional thing preventing sharing, analogous to its analysis for individuals of man. The truth is that these two arguments of the mutakallimun for the non-existence of individuation are based on considering individuation as something added to quiddity in the external, distinguished from it. And you have known that it is the same as the external identity in essence, making, and existence. And this – i.e., that individuation is distinguished from quiddity in the external and added to it such that a composite identity results from them – is what the mutakallimun sought to deny. For this denial is necessitated by what they argued from the two aspects. Thus, the dispute is verbal, for the philosophers claim that individuation is an existent thing, but as being identical to quiddity.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage completes the second argument and then presents a resolution. First, the author states that the proof of infinite regress is complete. Then an objector speaks: he denies that every ta'ayyun has a universal quiddity, arguing that the rule that every external existent has such a quiddity is refuted by the case of the Necessary Existent (al-wajib) – a reference to God, who has no quiddity. Moreover, each individual of ta'ayyun is such that the mind cannot conceive it as being shared or analyzed into a quiddity that admits sharing; it is a unique individual that cannot be universalized, like an individual human that cannot be divided into a universal quiddity and an additional individuator. The author then gives the truth (al-haqq): the mutakallimun's two arguments for the non-existence of ta'ayyun are based on the assumption that ta'ayyun is something added to quiddity in the external, separate from it. But it has been shown that ta'ayyun is identical to the external identity (huwiyya) in essence, making, and existence. Therefore, the mutakallimun's denial of ta'ayyun as something additional is what follows from their arguments, but the philosophers claim that ta'ayyun is an existent thing, meaning it is identical to quiddity, not an extra component. Hence the dispute is merely verbal (lafzi): both parties essentially agree that ta'ayyun is part of the thing's identity, but they express it differently.

Key Terms
دليل خلفي (dalil khalfi)
نزاع لفظي (niza' lafzi)
هوية (huwiyya)
حكماء (hukama')
متكلمون (mutakallimun)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The mutakallimun and philosophers truly disagree about whether individuation exists outside the mind.
Correction: The passage shows the dispute is verbal: the mutakallimun deny a separate individuator, while the philosophers affirm it as identical to essence, so they are not contradicting each other.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the real nature of the disagreement between the mutakallimun and the philosophers (hukama') regarding individuation?
A) It is a factual disagreement about whether individuation exists.
B) It is a verbal dispute based on a false assumption.
C) It is about the definition of quiddity.
D) It cannot be resolved.

Key Takeaway
The dispute over whether individuation is existent or not is merely verbal; both schools agree that it is identical to the external identity of a thing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a disagreement you have had with another Muslim about a matter of faith. Did it stem from different wording rather than a real difference in belief? Can you now see a path to reconciliation by focusing on shared meaning rather than terms?
?
The mutakallimun and philosophers both sought truth but were trapped by their own formulations. Are there theological phrases you cling to that might be hindering unity with others who hold the same belief in different words? What would it cost you to let go of the exclusive use of that phrase?
?
This lesson shows that clarity on definitions resolved a centuries-old dispute. Where in your own spiritual life are you unclear about what you truly mean by key concepts like 'tawheed' or 'iman'? What one step can you take this week to define your terms more precisely for yourself?

6 min
Essence Accepts Sharing, But Not Determination
Introduces the aim and concludes dispute is verbal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the eleventh aim regarding essence and determination, and why the dispute between mutakallimun and philosophers over determination is merely verbal.

Core Idea
The dispute over determination is verbal because both sides agree on reality.

This lesson introduces a key distinction: essence (mahiyyah) can be shared, but determination (ta'ayyun) cannot. The mutakallimun argue that determination is non-existent, but their proofs assume it is joined to essence externally. The author argues that determination is nothing other than the very identity of the thing, making the dispute merely verbal.

Guided Path
1
Read the aim statement
Read the first sentence: 'al-mahiyyah taqbal al-shirkah duna al-ta'ayyun.' Understand that essence is universal and can be shared, but particular determinations are not part of the essence.
2
Identify the mutakallimun's two proofs
The author refers to two indirect proofs used by the mutakallimun to argue that determination is non-existent. Note that these proofs assume determination is something joined to essence externally.
The proofs are not detailed here; only their assumption is mentioned.
3
Notice the author's correction
The author states that determination is the very identity of the thing in essence, constitution, and existence. It is not an additional element.
4
Grasp the conclusion
Because the mutakallimun assume conjunction and philosophers see identity, the dispute is merely verbal (al-niza' lafzhi). Both sides describe the same external reality.

نفسه بحيث إذا لاحظه العقل لم يمكن له فرض اشتراكه ، ولا تفصيله إلى ماهية قابلة للاشتراك، وأمر زائد عليها مانع من الشركة على قياس تفصيله لأفراد الإنسان. ( والحق : أن هذين (الدليلين) الخلفيين للمتكلمين على كون التعين عدمياً ( مبنيان على كون التعين أمراً منضماً إلى الماهية في الخارج ممتازاً) فيه ( عنها، وقد علمت أنه نفس الهوية ) الخارجية ذاتاً وجعلاً ووجوداً . ( وهذا ) أي كون التعين ممتازاً الماهية في الخارج منضماً إليها بحيث يتحصل منهما هوية مركبة فيه، (هو الذي حاول المتكلمون نفيه فإن هذا النفي هو اللازم مما استدلوا به من الوجهين. فإذن النزاع لفظي ، فإن الحكماء يدعون أن التعين أمر موجود، على أنه عين الماهية
المذكورة إنما هي في الممكنات، فالصواب الاكتفاء على المنع والمنحصر في المقولات العشر أنواع الموجودات لا أشخاصها لتصريحهم بخروج النقطة والوحدة على تقدير وجودهما. قوله : ( على قياس إلخ ) متعلق بالمنفي لا بالنفي.
قوله : ( فإن الحكماء إلخ) كيف يمكن أن يقال ذلك والحال أنهم استدلوا على وجوديته بجزئيته للموجود الخارجي، وأنهم فرعوا على ذلك بيان علة عدم زيادته في الواجب بأنه يستلزم التركيب، فهذا صلح من غير تراضي الخصمين قال الشيخ في الشفاء : الحيوان مأخوذ بعوارضه هو الشيء الطبيعي، والمأخوذ بذاته هو الطبيعة التي يقال : إن وجودها أقدم من وجود الطبيعي تقدم البسيط على المركب، وهو الذي يخص وجوده بأنه الوجود الإلهي ؛ لأن سبب وجوده بما هو حيوان عناية الله تعالى وأما كونه مع مادة وعوارض هذا الشخص فهو إن كان بعناية الله فهو الطبيعة انتهى وقال المحقق الدواني : ولقد كرر في كلامه تقدم الطبيعة من حيث هي على الطبيعة الشخصية فالصواب أن يقال مراد المصنف أن النزاع بين المتكلمين وبين ما هو التحقيق لفظي، يدل على ذلك قوله : وقد علمت أنه نفس الهوية أي كون التعين وجوديا بمعنى كونه موجوداً في الخارج منضماً إلى الماهية في الخارج على ما علمت من تحقيق مذهبهم، لا أنه موجود على أنه عين الماهية في الخارج، كما ذكره الشارح قدس سره فإنه صلح من غير تراضي الخصمين كما مر .

بمعنى
ووجد منها جزئي واحد كانت الجزئيات الباقية ممتنعة فامتناعها إما لنفس تلك الماهية أو لغيرها، فإن كان لنفسها امتنع أن يوجد ذلك الجزئي الواجب أيضاً، فيكون واجب الوجود ممتنع الوجود وهو الأمر الأول، وإن كان امتناعها لغير ذلك الماهية تكون بالنظر إلى نفس تلك الماهية ممكنة، فتكون تلك الجزئيات الممتنعة لذاتها بالاتفاق ممكنة وهو الأمر الثاني. والجواب : أن امتناعها بخصوصياتها، على معنى أن ما سوى هذا التعيين الحاصل في الواجب لا يمكن اجتماعه مع تلك الماهية؛ لاقتضائها تعيناً مخصوصاً اقتضاء تاماً ، ولا محظور فيه والله أعلم . قوله : ( وقد علمت أنه نفس الهوية إذ لو تحقق الانضمام الخارجي لتحقق الكلي الطبيعي
The Second Observation - The Eleventh Aim: The essence accepts sharing but not determination. Itself such that when the intellect observes it, it cannot posit its sharing, nor its division into an essence capable of sharing and an additional thing preventing sharing, analogous to its division into individuals of man. (And the truth: that these two indirect proofs of the mutakallimun for the non-existentiality of determination are based on the assumption that determination is something joined to the essence in the external world, distinct from it, whereas you have known that it is the very identity externally in essence, constitution, and existence. And this—i.e., determination being distinct from essence in the external world, joined to it such that a composite identity results from them—is what the mutakallimun attempted to negate, for this negation is entailed by what they adduced from the two aspects. Therefore the dispute is verbal, for the philosophers claim that determination is an existent thing, as being identical to essence. What was mentioned is only in possibles, so the correct approach is to suffice with prevention, and what is restricted to the ten categories are types of existents, not their individuals, due to their explicit statement that the point and the unit fall outside, assuming their existence. His statement: (on the analogy etc.) pertains to the negated, not to the negation. His statement: (for the philosophers etc.) How can that be said, when the fact is that they argued for its existentiality by its being a part of the external existent, and they branched on that the explanation of the cause of its non-addition in the Necessary because it entails composition; this is a reconciliation without the consent of the two opponents. Al-Shaykh said in al-Shifa': The animal taken with its accidents is the natural thing, and what is taken in its essence is the nature of which it is said: its existence is prior to the existence of the natural, the priority of the simple over the composite, and it is that whose existence is characterized as the divine existence, because the cause of its existence inasmuch as it is animal is the care of God, and as for its being with matter and accidents of this individual, if it is by the care of God, then it is nature. End quote. And al-Muhaqqiq al-Dawani said: He has repeated in his speech the priority of nature qua nature over the individual nature, so the correct view is to say that the author means that the dispute between the mutakallimun and what is the truth is verbal, indicated by his statement: 'and you have known that it is the very identity,' meaning that determination is existential in the sense that it exists in the external world joined to essence, as you have known from the verification of their doctrine, not that it exists as being identical to essence in the external world, as the commentator (may his soul be sanctified) mentioned, for it is a reconciliation without the consent of the two opponents, as has passed. Because if from it one individual existed, the remaining individuals would be impossible; their impossibility is either for that same essence or for other than it. If for itself, it would be impossible for that necessary individual to exist too, so the Necessary of existence would be impossible of existence—this is the first matter. And if their impossibility is for other than that essence, then in relation to that same essence they are possible, so those individuals impossible in themselves would be unanimously possible—this is the second matter. The answer: that their impossibility is due to their specificities, meaning that what is other than this determination existing in the Necessary cannot combine with that essence because of its demanding a particular determination with a complete demand, and there is no objection in it, and God knows best. His statement: (and you have known that it is the very identity, for if external conjunction were realized, the natural universal would be realized.)
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is a complex argument within the discussion of determination (ta'ayyun). The author begins by stating the eleventh aim: essence (mahiyyah) accepts sharing (al-shirkah) but not determination—i.e., essence is universal, but particular determinations are not part of the essence. He then refers to the mutakallimun's indirect proofs that determination is non-existent. The author argues that these proofs are based on assuming determination is something joined to essence externally. However, he says the truth is that determination is the very identity (al-huwiyyah) itself. The mutakallimun try to negate this conjunction, so the dispute becomes verbal: philosophers affirm determination as existent and identical to essence. The passage then includes glosses on specific phrases, addressing objections and defending the view that the dispute is verbal, quoting authorities like Ibn Sina and al-Dawani. It concludes with an objection-and-answer about why other individuals are impossible given one determination, and the answer is that impossibility is due to specificities.

Key Terms
الماهية
التعين
النزاع لفظي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The dispute between mutakallimun and philosophers over determination is substantive, with real ontological disagreement.
Correction: The author argues it is verbal because both sides agree on the external reality; they only differ in how they describe the relationship between determination and essence.

Checkpoint
What does the author conclude about the dispute between the mutakallimun and the philosophers regarding determination?
A) It is a real disagreement about the nature of determination.
B) It is a verbal dispute based on different assumptions about determination's relation to essence.
C) The mutakallimun are correct that determination is non-existent.
D) The philosophers are correct that determination is a separate existent.

Key Takeaway
The dispute over determination is verbal because both parties agree on the external reality; the difference is only in description.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a recent disagreement you had about a religious or philosophical matter. Is it possible that you and the other person actually agreed on the fundamental reality but were using different words to describe it? Are you willing to revisit that conversation and see if your dispute was merely verbal? What would change if you admitted that?
?
The philosophers and mutakallimun argued vigorously over determination, yet the author claims they agreed on reality. Have you ever insisted on a particular wording or definition, only to realize later that you and your opponent meant the same thing? How did that affect your relationship? Will you now be quicker to recognize verbal disputes and seek common ground?
?
If the dispute over determination is merely verbal, what does that say about other theological controversies you hold strong opinions about? Could some of your deepest convictions be merely linguistic preferences? Are you prepared to examine your own positions to see if they are about reality or just words?

Philosophical Clarifications on Determination
Glosses and quotes defending the verbal dispute thesis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the philosophers' view that determination is existent and identical to essence is defended, and why the dispute remains verbal.

Core Idea
Determination is the very identity of the thing, not an addition.

This lesson delves into the philosophers' position that determination is existent as identical to essence. The author addresses glosses on earlier phrases and quotes Ibn Sina and al-Dawani to show that the dispute is merely verbal. The key is that determination is not a separate component but the essence itself in its concrete existence.

Guided Path
1
Read the philosophers' claim
The passage clarifies that the philosophers claim determination is existent and identical to essence. This is in response to the earlier conclusion that the dispute is verbal.
2
Understand the gloss on the analogy
The author explains that the phrase 'on the analogy' (ala qiyas) pertains to the negated, not to the negation. This resolves a potential misunderstanding about the previous argument.
3
Examine the quotes from Ibn Sina and al-Dawani
Ibn Sina's quote from al-Shifa' discusses the priority of nature over the natural thing. Al-Dawani confirms that the author's intent is to show the dispute is verbal.
4
Conclude with the author's verification
The author restates that determination is existential in the sense of being joined to essence externally, but this 'joining' is not a real composition; it is a conceptual distinction. Thus the dispute remains verbal.

Objection and Answer: Impossibility of Other Individuals
Objection and answer about impossibility of other individuals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that if one individual exists others become impossible, and the answer that impossibility is due to specificities, not the essence.

Core Idea
Impossibility of other individuals is due to their specific determinations, not the essence.

This lesson addresses a key objection: if a given determination exists in the Necessary, why are other determinations impossible? The answer is that each determination entails a specific set of attributes, and the impossibility of others stems from their own specificities, not from the essence itself.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the objection: if one individual exists, the remaining individuals would be impossible. This raises the question why.
2
The two alternatives
The passage presents two possibilities: the impossibility is either due to the essence itself or due to something other than the essence. Each leads to a problematic conclusion.
First leads to the Necessary being impossible; second leads to contradiction.
3
The answer
The impossibility is due to their specificities (bikhsusiyyatiha). Other determinations cannot combine with this essence because each determination demands a particular set of attributes.
4
Final remark on natural universal
The passage ends with a reminder that external conjunction would entail the natural universal, which is not the case.
This ties back to the earlier discussion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الثاني - المقصد الحادي عشر : الماهية تقبل الشركة دون التعين
نفسه بحيث إذا لاحظه العقل لم يمكن له فرض اشتراكه ، ولا تفصيله إلى ماهية قابلة للاشتراك، وأمر زائد عليها مانع من الشركة على قياس تفصيله لأفراد الإنسان. ( والحق : أن هذين (الدليلين) الخلفيين للمتكلمين على كون التعين عدمياً ( مبنيان على كون التعين أمراً منضماً إلى الماهية في الخارج ممتازاً) فيه ( عنها، وقد علمت أنه نفس الهوية ) الخارجية ذاتاً وجعلاً ووجوداً . ( وهذا ) أي كون التعين ممتازاً الماهية في الخارج منضماً إليها بحيث يتحصل منهما هوية مركبة فيه، (هو الذي حاول المتكلمون نفيه فإن هذا النفي هو اللازم مما استدلوا به من الوجهين. فإذن النزاع لفظي ، فإن الحكماء يدعون أن التعين أمر موجود، على أنه عين الماهية
المذكورة إنما هي في الممكنات، فالصواب الاكتفاء على المنع والمنحصر في المقولات العشر أنواع الموجودات لا أشخاصها لتصريحهم بخروج النقطة والوحدة على تقدير وجودهما. قوله : ( على قياس إلخ ) متعلق بالمنفي لا بالنفي.
قوله : ( فإن الحكماء إلخ) كيف يمكن أن يقال ذلك والحال أنهم استدلوا على وجوديته بجزئيته للموجود الخارجي، وأنهم فرعوا على ذلك بيان علة عدم زيادته في الواجب بأنه يستلزم التركيب، فهذا صلح من غير تراضي الخصمين قال الشيخ في الشفاء : الحيوان مأخوذ بعوارضه هو الشيء الطبيعي، والمأخوذ بذاته هو الطبيعة التي يقال : إن وجودها أقدم من وجود الطبيعي تقدم البسيط على المركب، وهو الذي يخص وجوده بأنه الوجود الإلهي ؛ لأن سبب وجوده بما هو حيوان عناية الله تعالى وأما كونه مع مادة وعوارض هذا الشخص فهو إن كان بعناية الله فهو الطبيعة انتهى وقال المحقق الدواني : ولقد كرر في كلامه تقدم الطبيعة من حيث هي على الطبيعة الشخصية فالصواب أن يقال مراد المصنف أن النزاع بين المتكلمين وبين ما هو التحقيق لفظي، يدل على ذلك قوله : وقد علمت أنه نفس الهوية أي كون التعين وجوديا بمعنى كونه موجوداً في الخارج منضماً إلى الماهية في الخارج على ما علمت من تحقيق مذهبهم، لا أنه موجود على أنه عين الماهية في الخارج، كما ذكره الشارح قدس سره فإنه صلح من غير تراضي الخصمين كما مر .

بمعنى
ووجد منها جزئي واحد كانت الجزئيات الباقية ممتنعة فامتناعها إما لنفس تلك الماهية أو لغيرها، فإن كان لنفسها امتنع أن يوجد ذلك الجزئي الواجب أيضاً، فيكون واجب الوجود ممتنع الوجود وهو الأمر الأول، وإن كان امتناعها لغير ذلك الماهية تكون بالنظر إلى نفس تلك الماهية ممكنة، فتكون تلك الجزئيات الممتنعة لذاتها بالاتفاق ممكنة وهو الأمر الثاني. والجواب : أن امتناعها بخصوصياتها، على معنى أن ما سوى هذا التعيين الحاصل في الواجب لا يمكن اجتماعه مع تلك الماهية؛ لاقتضائها تعيناً مخصوصاً اقتضاء تاماً ، ولا محظور فيه والله أعلم . قوله : ( وقد علمت أنه نفس الهوية إذ لو تحقق الانضمام الخارجي لتحقق الكلي الطبيعي
The Second Observation - The Eleventh Aim: The essence accepts sharing but not determination. Itself such that when the intellect observes it, it cannot posit its sharing, nor its division into an essence capable of sharing and an additional thing preventing sharing, analogous to its division into individuals of man. (And the truth: that these two indirect proofs of the mutakallimun for the non-existentiality of determination are based on the assumption that determination is something joined to the essence in the external world, distinct from it, whereas you have known that it is the very identity externally in essence, constitution, and existence. And this—i.e., determination being distinct from essence in the external world, joined to it such that a composite identity results from them—is what the mutakallimun attempted to negate, for this negation is entailed by what they adduced from the two aspects. Therefore the dispute is verbal, for the philosophers claim that determination is an existent thing, as being identical to essence. What was mentioned is only in possibles, so the correct approach is to suffice with prevention, and what is restricted to the ten categories are types of existents, not their individuals, due to their explicit statement that the point and the unit fall outside, assuming their existence. His statement: (on the analogy etc.) pertains to the negated, not to the negation. His statement: (for the philosophers etc.) How can that be said, when the fact is that they argued for its existentiality by its being a part of the external existent, and they branched on that the explanation of the cause of its non-addition in the Necessary because it entails composition; this is a reconciliation without the consent of the two opponents. Al-Shaykh said in al-Shifa': The animal taken with its accidents is the natural thing, and what is taken in its essence is the nature of which it is said: its existence is prior to the existence of the natural, the priority of the simple over the composite, and it is that whose existence is characterized as the divine existence, because the cause of its existence inasmuch as it is animal is the care of God, and as for its being with matter and accidents of this individual, if it is by the care of God, then it is nature. End quote. And al-Muhaqqiq al-Dawani said: He has repeated in his speech the priority of nature qua nature over the individual nature, so the correct view is to say that the author means that the dispute between the mutakallimun and what is the truth is verbal, indicated by his statement: 'and you have known that it is the very identity,' meaning that determination is existential in the sense that it exists in the external world joined to essence, as you have known from the verification of their doctrine, not that it exists as being identical to essence in the external world, as the commentator (may his soul be sanctified) mentioned, for it is a reconciliation without the consent of the two opponents, as has passed. Because if from it one individual existed, the remaining individuals would be impossible; their impossibility is either for that same essence or for other than it. If for itself, it would be impossible for that necessary individual to exist too, so the Necessary of existence would be impossible of existence—this is the first matter. And if their impossibility is for other than that essence, then in relation to that same essence they are possible, so those individuals impossible in themselves would be unanimously possible—this is the second matter. The answer: that their impossibility is due to their specificities, meaning that what is other than this determination existing in the Necessary cannot combine with that essence because of its demanding a particular determination with a complete demand, and there is no objection in it, and God knows best. His statement: (and you have known that it is the very identity, for if external conjunction were realized, the natural universal would be realized.)
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is a complex argument within the discussion of determination (ta'ayyun). The author begins by stating the eleventh aim: essence (mahiyyah) accepts sharing (al-shirkah) but not determination—i.e., essence is universal, but particular determinations are not part of the essence. He then refers to the mutakallimun's indirect proofs that determination is non-existent. The author argues that these proofs are based on assuming determination is something joined to essence externally. However, he says the truth is that determination is the very identity (al-huwiyyah) itself. The mutakallimun try to negate this conjunction, so the dispute becomes verbal: philosophers affirm determination as existent and identical to essence. The passage then includes glosses on specific phrases, addressing objections and defending the view that the dispute is verbal, quoting authorities like Ibn Sina and al-Dawani. It concludes with an objection-and-answer about why other individuals are impossible given one determination, and the answer is that impossibility is due to specificities.

الامتناع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The impossibility of other determinations is due to the essence itself being limited.
Correction: The impossibility is due to the specificities of each determination, not the essence. The essence is capable of other determinations, but each determination's specific requirements prevent combination.

Checkpoint
According to the answer, why are other individuals impossible?
A) Because the essence itself prevents them.
B) Because of their specificities (bikhsusiyyatiha).
C) Because they are not possible in themselves.
D) Because the Necessary cannot have multiple determinations.

Key Takeaway
Other determinations are impossible not because the essence excludes them, but because each determination has its own specific requirement that prevents combination.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the essence of Allah is not limited in any way, yet His specific determinations require that only one exists, what does that say about your own expectations of how He should act? Are you willing to accept that His determinations are complete in themselves, even when they conflict with your desires?
?
The objection implies that limitations arise from specificities, not from the essence. Have you ever attributed a perceived limitation in your life to Allah's essence—such as thinking He is not powerful enough for your situation—when the limitation actually comes from the specific way He has determined your path? How can you realign your thinking?
?
The answer teaches that each determination demands a complete set of attributes. Consider your own life: have you ever felt that specific circumstances (your 'determination') are a barrier to receiving Allah's mercy or guidance? How does this lesson challenge that feeling, showing that it is the nature of determination itself, not a lack in Allah's essence?

Can Essence Cause Determination? The Philosophers' View
Philosophers' thesis on determination by essence with clarifications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophers' claim that determination (ta'ayyun) is caused by essence, and why it cannot be interpreted as efficient causation.

Core Idea
Essence necessitates determination, but it does not produce it as an efficient cause.

The twelfth aim of this observation examines whether essence can be the cause of determination. The philosophers affirm this, but careful analysis shows that the causality is one of necessary concomitance, not production. The commentator explains the precise meaning and defends against misunderstandings.

Guided Path
1
Read the philosophers' statement
Start by reading the source passage, which presents the philosophers' view that determination is caused by essence. Notice the immediate qualification that it is not efficient causation.
The example of four and evenness is key.
2
Distinguish efficient cause from necessary concomitant
The commentator stresses that essence is not an efficient cause but a necessitating condition. Efficient causation would require precedence, which is impossible here.
Think of how four necessitates evenness without producing it.
3
Examine the condition of 'type confined'
The phrase 'its type is confined' avoids implying a single individual. Essence is taken with the condition excluding determination, so it is not predicated.
This prevents the natural universal from being realized externally.
4
Understand the reply regarding the natural universal
A potential objection is that the natural universal would then exist externally. The commentator offers a possible answer: determination attaches to the individual, not the universal essence.
This leads to the claim that the dispute may be verbal.

قوله : (انحصر نوعها إلخ) لم يقل انحصرت في الشخص الواحد لأن الماهية المقتضية المأخوذة بشرط لا، أي أن لا يكون التعين مأخوذاً فيه ومنضماً فيه بل خارجاً عنه منضماً إليه، وهي غير محمولة والشخص إنما يقال بالقياس إلى ما يحمل عليه وهي وهي المأخوذة لا بشرط شيء وهو النوع.
في الخارج لا قبلها، فيلزم تحقق الكلي الطبيعي في الخارج. اللهم إلا أن يقال: عروض التعين وما به التعين للمتعين بهذا التعين لا للماهية الكلية، وتقدم المعروض بالوجود ذاتاً لا يقتضي تقدم تعينه أصلاً فلا محذور فيه على أن تقدم التعين على عروض هذه العوارض لا ينافي تأخره عن ذاتها الكافي في كونها ما به التعين، كما ستعرفه .
قوله : ( فإذن النزاع لفظي فإن الحكماء إلخ) هذا صلح من غير تراضي الخصمين كما نقل عن الشارح؛ لأن المتكلمين لا يقولون بوجودية التعين على أنه عين الماهية كما يدل عليه التحرير المذكور قبل. والحق أن النزاع في وجود التعين فرع النزاع في الوجود الذهني، إذ ليس في الخارج أمر متميز عن الماهية منضم إليها في الخارج بل في الخارج، إنما هو الشخص، والعقل يفصله إلى ما به الاشتراك وهو الكلي الطبيعي، وإلى ما به الامتياز وهو التشخص، فإن ثبت الوجود الذهني كان لها ثبوت وإلا فلا وأنت خبير بأن الكلام في وجود التعين في الخارج فلا يكون فرع الوجود الذهني، فليتأمل.
