قوله: (فإن الحكماء إلخ فيه بحث لأنه إن أراد بكون الماهية علة للتعين فيما انحصر نوعه في شخصه كونها علة موجدة له في الخارج فهو فاسد لاتحادهما في الوجود الخارجي عندهم كما صرح به الآن فلا يعقل كون الماهية موجدة لتعين نفسها . وإن أراد به العلية باعتبار الوجود الذهني فلا وجه له أيضاً؛ لامتناع اقتضاء الماهية الذهنية تشخصها الخارجي، وإلا لزم أن يوجد التعين الخارجي في الذهن ولا يمكن تعدد أفراد تلك الماهية في الذهن أيضاً، فإن قلت : هذا جار في وجود الواجب على رأي المتكلمين . قلت لهم أن يتخلصوا بامتناع التعقل بالكنه
The Second Observation - The Twelfth Aim: Determination if caused by essence. According to the external, and it is distinguished from it only in the mind, and the mutakallimun claim that it is not an existent additional to essence externally joined to it, and there is no conflict between them as you see. And the meaning of the Twelfth Aim: Determination if caused by essence. (The philosophers) who hold that determination is existential said: (Determination if caused by essence). His statement: (If caused by essence, in that the essence alone is sufficient for its emanation from the separate principle, its necessitating it such that its existence cannot be without it, like the necessitation of four for evenness—not that it is an efficient cause of it, so as to ward off what might be imagined that the efficient cause must precede in existence and individuation its effect, because the non-existent and vague cannot be a cause for the determinate; thus if essence were a cause for individuation, the precedence of individuation over itself would be necessary.) For individuation it is. His statement: (its type is confined etc.) He did not say that it is confined to a single individual because the necessitating essence taken with the condition of not—i.e., that determination is not taken into it and joined in it but rather outside it and joined to it—and it is not predicated, and the individual is only said in relation to that which is predicated onto it, and it is what is taken without condition, which is the type. In the external, not before it, so the realization of the natural universal in the external would be necessary. However, it could be said: the occurrence of determination and that by which determination is for that which is determined by this determination, not for the universal essence, and the precedence of the subject in existence essentially does not necessitate the precedence of its determination at all, so there is no objection in it, because the precedence of determination over the occurrence of these accidents does not contradict its posteriority to the essence that suffices as that by which determination is, as you will know. His statement: (Therefore the dispute is verbal, for the philosophers etc.) This is a reconciliation without the consent of the two opponents, as transmitted from the commentator, because the mutakallimun do not say that determination is existential as being identical to essence, as indicated by the aforementioned formulation. The truth is that the dispute over the existence of determination is a branch of the dispute over mental existence, because there is nothing in the external distinct from essence joined to it externally, but rather in the external there is only the individual, and the intellect divides it into that by which it shares—which is the natural universal—and into that by which it is distinguished—which is individuation. If mental existence is established, then it has subsistence; otherwise not. And you are aware that the discussion is about the existence of determination in the external, so it is not a branch of mental existence, so let it be considered. • His statement: (for the philosophers etc.) There is discussion in it, because if what is meant by essence being a cause of determination in cases where its type is confined to its individual is that it is an efficient cause bringing it into existence externally, then it is invalid due to their unity in external existence according to them, as he explicitly stated now, so it is inconceivable that the essence be an efficient cause of its own determination. And if what is meant is the causality with respect to mental existence, there is no basis for it either, because of the impossibility of mental essence necessitating its external individuation, otherwise it would follow that external determination exists in the mind and that multiple individuals of that essence cannot exist in the mind. If you say: this applies to the existence of the Necessary according to the mutakallimun. I say: they can extricate themselves by the impossibility of intellection of the true reality.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is a critical examination of the philosophers' claim that essence can be a cause of determination (ta'ayyun). The passage begins by stating the twelfth aim and then presents the philosophers' position: determination is caused by essence in the sense that essence alone suffices for its emanation, similar to the way four necessitates evenness. However, the commentator immediately raises problems. The core difficulty is that if essence were an efficient cause of individuation, it would require precedence of the effect over the cause, which is impossible. The commentator then explains that the philosophers' phrase 'its type is confined' is carefully worded to avoid saying 'confined to a single individual'. They take essence with a condition (bishart la) that excludes determination, so it is not predicated. Then he discusses the consequence that the natural universal would be realized externally, but he offers a possible reply: determination attaches to the determined individual, not to the universal essence. He then returns to the claim that the dispute is verbal, arguing that the mutakallimun do not affirm determination as identical to essence, so the reconciliation is invalid. Instead, he proposes that the dispute over determination is a branch of the dispute over mental existence (al-wujud al-dhihni), because in the external there is only the individual; the intellect divides it into universal and particular. If mental existence is established, then universals have reality; otherwise not. But he notes that the discussion here is about external determination, so this might not apply. Finally, he presents an objection: if essence causes determination externally, it would be self-causation; if mentally, then external individuation would be necessitated by mental essence, which is also problematic. A possible rejoinder for the mutakallimun regarding the Necessary is mentioned.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Determination is efficiently caused by essence.
Correction: The philosophers mean that essence necessitates determination as a necessary concomitant, not that it produces it as an agent.

Key Takeaway
The philosophers affirm that essence necessitates determination, but not as an efficient cause, and this distinction is crucial to avoid absurdities.

The Verbal Dispute and the Connection to Mental Existence
Final objections and the link to mental existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the dispute over determination is connected to the doctrine of mental existence, and the final objection against the philosophers' position.

Core Idea
The dispute over determination reduces to the reality of mental existence.

After presenting the philosophers' view, the commentator argues that the dispute is not merely verbal, but rooted in the question of mental existence. He then raises a powerful objection: if essence causes determination externally, it would be self-causation; if mentally, it leads to paradoxes. The mutakallimun have a possible escape regarding the Necessary.

Guided Path
1
Examine the claim of verbal dispute
The commentator notes that someone might think the dispute is verbal, but he rejects this because the mutakallimun do not accept determination as identical to essence.
The reconciliation is without consent of the opponents.
2
Understand the link to mental existence
The commentator proposes that the dispute over determination is a branch of the dispute over mental existence (al-wujud al-dhihni). In the external, there is only the individual; the intellect divides it into universal and particular.
If mental existence is real, then universals have subsistence.
3
Analyze the objection about self-causation
The commentator presents a strong objection: if essence is an efficient cause of determination externally, then since they are identical in existence, it would be self-causation, which is absurd.
This is a logical contradiction.
4
Consider the mental interpretation and the rejoinder
If causality is interpreted mentally, then mental essence would necessitate external individuation, leading to paradoxes. The mutakallimun can escape regarding the Necessary by invoking the impossibility of intellection of the true reality.
This final point is a possible defense.

قوله: (إن علل بالماهية بأن كانت الماهية فقط كافيةً في فيضانه من المبدأ المفارق اقتضائها له أنه لا يمكن وجودها بدونه كاقتضاء الأربعة للزوجية لا أن تكون فاعلة له حتى يرد ما يتوهم من أن العلة الفاعلية لا بد أن تتقدم بالوجود والتشخص على معلوله؛ لأن المعدوم والمبهم لا يكون علة للمعين فلو كانت الماهية علة للتشخص يلزم تقدم التشخص على
نفسه.
للتشخص هي
قوله : (انحصر نوعها إلخ) لم يقل انحصرت في الشخص الواحد لأن الماهية المقتضية المأخوذة بشرط لا، أي أن لا يكون التعين مأخوذاً فيه ومنضماً فيه بل خارجاً عنه منضماً إليه، وهي غير محمولة والشخص إنما يقال بالقياس إلى ما يحمل عليه وهي وهي المأخوذة لا بشرط شيء وهو النوع.
في الخارج لا قبلها، فيلزم تحقق الكلي الطبيعي في الخارج. اللهم إلا أن يقال: عروض التعين وما به التعين للمتعين بهذا التعين لا للماهية الكلية، وتقدم المعروض بالوجود ذاتاً لا يقتضي تقدم تعينه أصلاً فلا محذور فيه على أن تقدم التعين على عروض هذه العوارض لا ينافي تأخره عن ذاتها الكافي في كونها ما به التعين، كما ستعرفه .
قوله : ( فإذن النزاع لفظي فإن الحكماء إلخ) هذا صلح من غير تراضي الخصمين كما نقل عن الشارح؛ لأن المتكلمين لا يقولون بوجودية التعين على أنه عين الماهية كما يدل عليه التحرير المذكور قبل. والحق أن النزاع في وجود التعين فرع النزاع في الوجود الذهني، إذ ليس في الخارج أمر متميز عن الماهية منضم إليها في الخارج بل في الخارج، إنما هو الشخص، والعقل يفصله إلى ما به الاشتراك وهو الكلي الطبيعي، وإلى ما به الامتياز وهو التشخص، فإن ثبت الوجود الذهني كان لها ثبوت وإلا فلا وأنت خبير بأن الكلام في وجود التعين في الخارج فلا يكون فرع الوجود الذهني، فليتأمل.

قوله: (فإن الحكماء إلخ فيه بحث لأنه إن أراد بكون الماهية علة للتعين فيما انحصر نوعه في شخصه كونها علة موجدة له في الخارج فهو فاسد لاتحادهما في الوجود الخارجي عندهم كما صرح به الآن فلا يعقل كون الماهية موجدة لتعين نفسها . وإن أراد به العلية باعتبار الوجود الذهني فلا وجه له أيضاً؛ لامتناع اقتضاء الماهية الذهنية تشخصها الخارجي، وإلا لزم أن يوجد التعين الخارجي في الذهن ولا يمكن تعدد أفراد تلك الماهية في الذهن أيضاً، فإن قلت : هذا جار في وجود الواجب على رأي المتكلمين . قلت لهم أن يتخلصوا بامتناع التعقل بالكنه
The Second Observation - The Twelfth Aim: Determination if caused by essence. According to the external, and it is distinguished from it only in the mind, and the mutakallimun claim that it is not an existent additional to essence externally joined to it, and there is no conflict between them as you see. And the meaning of the Twelfth Aim: Determination if caused by essence. (The philosophers) who hold that determination is existential said: (Determination if caused by essence). His statement: (If caused by essence, in that the essence alone is sufficient for its emanation from the separate principle, its necessitating it such that its existence cannot be without it, like the necessitation of four for evenness—not that it is an efficient cause of it, so as to ward off what might be imagined that the efficient cause must precede in existence and individuation its effect, because the non-existent and vague cannot be a cause for the determinate; thus if essence were a cause for individuation, the precedence of individuation over itself would be necessary.) For individuation it is. His statement: (its type is confined etc.) He did not say that it is confined to a single individual because the necessitating essence taken with the condition of not—i.e., that determination is not taken into it and joined in it but rather outside it and joined to it—and it is not predicated, and the individual is only said in relation to that which is predicated onto it, and it is what is taken without condition, which is the type. In the external, not before it, so the realization of the natural universal in the external would be necessary. However, it could be said: the occurrence of determination and that by which determination is for that which is determined by this determination, not for the universal essence, and the precedence of the subject in existence essentially does not necessitate the precedence of its determination at all, so there is no objection in it, because the precedence of determination over the occurrence of these accidents does not contradict its posteriority to the essence that suffices as that by which determination is, as you will know. His statement: (Therefore the dispute is verbal, for the philosophers etc.) This is a reconciliation without the consent of the two opponents, as transmitted from the commentator, because the mutakallimun do not say that determination is existential as being identical to essence, as indicated by the aforementioned formulation. The truth is that the dispute over the existence of determination is a branch of the dispute over mental existence, because there is nothing in the external distinct from essence joined to it externally, but rather in the external there is only the individual, and the intellect divides it into that by which it shares—which is the natural universal—and into that by which it is distinguished—which is individuation. If mental existence is established, then it has subsistence; otherwise not. And you are aware that the discussion is about the existence of determination in the external, so it is not a branch of mental existence, so let it be considered. • His statement: (for the philosophers etc.) There is discussion in it, because if what is meant by essence being a cause of determination in cases where its type is confined to its individual is that it is an efficient cause bringing it into existence externally, then it is invalid due to their unity in external existence according to them, as he explicitly stated now, so it is inconceivable that the essence be an efficient cause of its own determination. And if what is meant is the causality with respect to mental existence, there is no basis for it either, because of the impossibility of mental essence necessitating its external individuation, otherwise it would follow that external determination exists in the mind and that multiple individuals of that essence cannot exist in the mind. If you say: this applies to the existence of the Necessary according to the mutakallimun. I say: they can extricate themselves by the impossibility of intellection of the true reality.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is a critical examination of the philosophers' claim that essence can be a cause of determination (ta'ayyun). The passage begins by stating the twelfth aim and then presents the philosophers' position: determination is caused by essence in the sense that essence alone suffices for its emanation, similar to the way four necessitates evenness. However, the commentator immediately raises problems. The core difficulty is that if essence were an efficient cause of individuation, it would require precedence of the effect over the cause, which is impossible. The commentator then explains that the philosophers' phrase 'its type is confined' is carefully worded to avoid saying 'confined to a single individual'. They take essence with a condition (bishart la) that excludes determination, so it is not predicated. Then he discusses the consequence that the natural universal would be realized externally, but he offers a possible reply: determination attaches to the determined individual, not to the universal essence. He then returns to the claim that the dispute is verbal, arguing that the mutakallimun do not affirm determination as identical to essence, so the reconciliation is invalid. Instead, he proposes that the dispute over determination is a branch of the dispute over mental existence (al-wujud al-dhihni), because in the external there is only the individual; the intellect divides it into universal and particular. If mental existence is established, then universals have reality; otherwise not. But he notes that the discussion here is about external determination, so this might not apply. Finally, he presents an objection: if essence causes determination externally, it would be self-causation; if mentally, then external individuation would be necessitated by mental essence, which is also problematic. A possible rejoinder for the mutakallimun regarding the Necessary is mentioned.

التشخص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The philosophers' view is easily refuted by the self-causation argument.
Correction: The self-causation argument only applies if we interpret causality as external efficient causation; the philosophers may intend a different relation.

Checkpoint
What does the commentator say about the interpretation of essence as an efficient cause of determination externally?
A) It is valid if the essence is distinct.
B) It is invalid because it leads to self-causation.
C) It is valid if determination is mental.
D) It is the only interpretation possible.

Key Takeaway
The philosophers' claim fails whether interpreted as external efficient causation or mental causation, but the mutakallimun's position on the Necessary provides an escape from a similar objection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on your own identity, do you ever assume that your essence (who you are) fully determines your actions? How does the argument against self-causation in this lesson expose the error in thinking you can be the sole cause of your own choices?
?
Your mental images of Allah are not His true reality. Do you ever treat your conceptual understanding of Allah as if it were the full truth? How does the distinction between mental and external existence protect you from inadvertently limiting your Lord in your mind?
?
The mutakallimun affirm that Allah's true reality cannot be grasped by the mind. Have you ever felt frustrated by this limitation? Or does it humble you and increase your awe? In your worship, how can you turn this intellectual limit into a deeper reliance on revelation and submission?

Logic and Technical Terms
advanced
10 min
Determination: Definition and the Philosophers' Causal Argument
Definition and proof of determination's causality by essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophers' concept of determination as an extra existent caused by the essence in a non-efficient sense, and its consequence that the species is confined to a single individual.

Core Idea
Determination is necessitated by the essence, not produced by it as an efficient cause.

This lesson introduces the central issue of the Twelfth Aim: whether determination is caused by the essence. The philosophers argue it is an extra existent that the essence necessitates, like four necessitates evenness. This leads to the conclusion that the species of such an essence is confined to one individual. We will examine their reasoning and the key terminology.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note the key terms: تعين (determination), ماهية (essence), علة (cause).
The passage is dense; read slowly.
2
Identify the philosophers' claim
Look for the statement that determination is caused by the essence. Understand that they mean a necessitation, not efficient causality.
The example of four and evenness clarifies this.
3
Understand the confinement argument
The philosophers argue that if the essence necessitates determination, then the species (type) of that essence can only have one individual. Why? Because any other determination would require a separate cause.
This is a key proof for the philosophers.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider how this argument relates to broader issues in theology and philosophy, such as the nature of the Necessary Existent.
This will be developed in later lessons.

اللهم إلا أن هذا التخلص إنما هو لبعض القائلين بهذا الامتناع والحق على ما نقل عنه أن هذا الكلام من الفلاسفة مشعر بأن التعين يمتاز عن الماهية في الخارج لكن في العلية على تقدير الامتياز أيضاً بحث ظاهر ، فإن العلية مشروطة بالوجود والتشخص عندهم، والشرط من تتمة العلة باعتبار تأثيرها ، فلا يكون معلولاً لها، اللهم إلا أن يمنع مشروطة العلية بالتشخص، وإن اشترطت بالوجود، غايته استلزام الوجود للتشخص، أما توقفه عليه فلا ؛ حتى يلزم المحذور عليه. وفيه نظر لأن الشيء ما لم يتشخص لم يصر علة لتشخص معين وبمثله أبطل الشارح في موقف الجوهر كون الصورة المطلقة علة للهيولى، ومع هذا فلا بد من القول بوجود الكلي الطبيعي في الخارج، وإلا فما لم يوجد لا يكون علة لوجود شيء آخر على ما زعم الحكماء
قوله : (اقتضاء تاماً الاقتضاء التام بمعنى أن الماهية لو وجدت لم ينفك عنها بحسب ذاتها، وهذا التعين لا ينافي احتياجها في الوجود الخارجي إلى فاعلها حتى ينافي الإمكان . والحاصل : أن الماهية بشرط الوجود الخارجي تقتضي التعين، وأما وجودها فمن الفاعل. بقي فيه بحث آخر وهو أن العلة للتعين فيما ادعى لزوم انحصار النوع في الشخص إذا كان الماهية بشرط الوجود الخارجي، فلم لا يجوز أن تكون كل ماهية مقتضية باعتبار وجوداتها الخاصة تعينات متعددة، والوجودات تلحقها باعتبار العلل والاستعدادات. اللهم إلا أن يقال : لا تعدد للعلل في نفس الأمر وأما الاستعدادات فإنما تتعاقب على المادة، فثبت الاحتياج إليها. وليس حينئذ في إسناد التعينات إلى الماهية باعتبار الوجودات كثير نفع .
The Second Observatory - The Twelfth Aim: Determination (al-ta‘ayyun) if it is caused by the essence (al-māhiyya) according to the external (al-khārij), and it is distinguished from it only in the mind (al-dhihn), and the mutakallimūn claim that it is not an extra existent (mawjūd zā’id) over the essence in the external, conjoined to it therein, and there is no incompatibility between them as you see. The meaning of the Twelfth Aim: Determination if it is caused by the essence. (The philosophers said) those who hold that determination is existential (wujūdī): (Determination if it is caused by the essence). His statement: (If it is caused by the essence) meaning that the essence alone is sufficient in its emanation from the separate principle, its requiring it such that its existence cannot be without it, like the requirement of four for evenness, not that it is an efficient cause for it, so that what is imagined might be refuted: that the efficient cause must precede in existence and individuation (tashakhkhuṣ) its effect, because the non-existent and the indistinct cannot be a cause for the determinate. For if the essence were a cause for individuation, the individuation would have to precede itself. His statement: (Its species is confined, etc.) He did not say confined to one individual (shakhṣ wāḥid) because the requiring essence taken with the condition of non-condition (bi-sharṭ lā), i.e., that determination is not taken into it and conjoined in it, but rather external to it conjoined to it, and it is not predicated, and an individual is only said in relation to what it is predicated upon, and it is taken without condition (lā bi-sharṭ shay’) which is the species. In the external not before it, so the realization of the natural universal (al-kullī al-ṭabī‘ī) in the external follows. However, it may be said: The occurrence of determination and that by which determination is for the determinate by this determination, not for the universal essence, and the priority of the subject (ma‘rūḍ) in existence essentially does not necessitate the priority of its determination at all, so no problem therein, and the priority of determination over the occurrence of these accidents does not contradict its posteriority to the essence itself, sufficient in its being that by which determination, as you will know. His statement: (So then the dispute is verbal, for the philosophers, etc.) This is a reconciliation without the consent of the two opponents as narrated from the commentator; because the mutakallimūn do not affirm the existence of determination as being identical to the essence as indicated by the earlier formulation. And the truth is that the dispute over the existence of determination is a branch of the dispute over mental existence (al-wujūd al-dhihnī), since in the external there is no distinct thing from the essence conjoined to it in the external, rather in the external it is only the individual, and the intellect analyzes it into that by which sharing (i.e., the natural universal) and that by which distinction (i.e., individuation). If mental existence is established, it has subsistence, otherwise not. And you are aware that the discussion is about the existence of determination in the external, so it is not a branch of mental existence, so let it be considered. • His statement: (For the philosophers, etc. has discussion) because if he means by the essence being a cause for determination in what its species is confined to its individual that it is an efficient cause for it in the external, it is false due to their unity in external existence as he stated now, so it is not conceivable that the essence is an efficient cause for its own determination. And if he means causality (al-‘illiyya) with respect to mental existence, there is no justification for it either; due to the impossibility of the mental essence requiring its external individuation, otherwise it would necessitate that external determination exists in the mind and it would not be possible for multiple individuals of that essence in the mind also. If you say: This applies to the existence of the Necessary (al-wājib) according to the mutakallimūn. I say: They can escape by the impossibility of conceptualizing (al-ta‘aqqul) with full comprehension (bi-l-kunh). That it is a require of its determination with a complete requirement either essentially or through what is necessary for it, its species is confined to the single individual resulting from the essence and the determination caused by it, and it is not possible that another determination exists with it, otherwise the first determination would be separated from it, so the effect would be absent from its cause which necessitates it. This is if the determination of the essence is additional to it and the essence requires that requirement. But if the essence is determinate by itself, impossible in itself from supposing sharing in it, like the Exalted Necessary according to their view, no multiplicity is conceivable at all, rather this is stronger in negating multiplicity. His statement: (Otherwise it would be separated from it, etc.) due to the impossibility of two determinations coexisting. His statement: (From its cause which necessitates it) He indicated by his statement 'which necessitates it' that it is an effect of the kind that does not separate from the cause, so wherever the cause exists, the effect must exist. Thus what was imagined that absence only occurs if the cause exists and the effect does not exist, not that the cause exists and the effect does not exist with it. His statement: (This is if, etc.) A refutation of the commentator of al-Maqāṣid where he gave the example of this category with the Exalted Necessary. His statement: (According to their view they said: His determination, exalted, is identical to His essence, for if it were additional to it, composition of the essence of the Exalted Necessary would follow. However, this escape is only for some of those who hold this impossibility. And the truth, as narrated from him, is that this speech of the philosophers indicates that determination is distinguished from the essence in the external, but regarding causality, on the assumption of distinction, there is also an apparent discussion. For causality is conditioned by existence and individuation according to them, and the condition is part of the complete cause with respect to its effect, so it cannot be an effect for it. However, unless it is denied that causality is conditioned by individuation, and even if conditioned by existence, its utmost is that existence necessitates individuation, but its dependence on it is not, so that the problem would follow for him. And there is consideration in it, because a thing as long as it has not been individuated does not become a cause for a specific individuation, and similarly the commentator invalidated in the Station of Substance the absolute form being a cause for hyle. And with this, one must affirm the existence of the natural universal in the external, otherwise what does not exist cannot be a cause for the existence of something else according to the claim of the philosophers. His statement: (A complete requirement) The complete requirement means that if the essence existed, it would not separate from it by its essence, and this determination does not contradict its need in external existence for its agent, so as to contradict contingency. The result: The essence under the condition of external existence requires determination, but its existence is from the agent. There remains another discussion: that the cause for determination in what he claimed necessitates the confinement of species to individual, if the essence is under the condition of external existence, then why is it not permissible that every essence requires, by virtue of its specific existences, multiple determinations, and existences attach to it by virtue of causes and dispositions? However, it may be said: There is no multiplicity of causes in actual fact, and as for dispositions, they only succeed each other upon matter, so the need for them is established. And then there is not much benefit in attributing determinations to the essence by virtue of existences.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is a continuous commentary on the Twelfth Aim of the Second Observatory, which asks whether determination (al-ta‘ayyun) is caused by the essence (al-māhiyya). The author first defines the issue: the philosophers hold that determination is an extra existent in the external and is caused by the essence, while the mutakallimūn deny it is an extra existent. The author then explains the philosophers' position in detail. The philosophers argue that determination is caused by the essence in the sense that the essence alone suffices for the emanation of determination from the separate principle, much like the quaternity of four necessitates evenness. This is not efficient causality, as that would require the cause to be existent and individuated before its effect, which would lead to circularity. The commentary then addresses the phrase 'its species is confined' — the philosophers do not say 'confined to one individual' because the essence is taken with the condition of not including determination; the individual is what results from the essence and determination. The discussion then considers an objection: the occurrence of determination is for the determinate, not the universal essence, so no problem. The author then notes the claim that the dispute is verbal, but objects that the mutakallimūn do not affirm determination as identical to the essence. Instead, the dispute hinges on mental existence. The commentary critiques the philosophers' causality: if the essence causes determination in the external, they would be united, so the essence cannot cause its own determination; if in the mind, it cannot cause external individuation. A potential problem with the Necessary Existent is addressed by noting the impossibility of full conceptualization. The explanation of the complete requirement states that if the essence exists externally, it necessitates a single determination, else the effect would be absent from its necessary cause. The commentary notes this applies when determination is additional; for the Necessary Existent, determination is identical to essence, so no multiplicity. Further comments discuss the condition of causality requiring existence and individuation, and the need to affirm the natural universal in the external to avoid circularity. Finally, the author discusses the complete requirement: the essence under the condition of external existence necessitates determination, but existence comes from an agent. A remaining objection about multiple determinations for the same essence is answered by noting that causes do not multiply in actual fact.

ماهية
علة
النوع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the philosophers' claim 'determination is caused by the essence' means the essence efficiently produces determination as a separate effect.
Correction: The philosophers clarify it is a necessitation, like four necessitates evenness, not efficient causality. Efficient causality would require the cause to pre-exist in existence and individuation, leading to circularity.

Checkpoint
According to the philosophers in this passage, what is the relationship between determination and the essence?
A) The essence is an efficient cause that creates determination as a separate existent.
B) The essence necessitates determination such that without it the essence cannot exist, like four necessitates evenness.
C) The essence is identical to determination in the external.
D) The essence receives determination from an external agent.

Key Takeaway
The philosophers argue that determination is necessitated by the essence, not efficiently caused, and this leads to the confinement of the species to a single individual.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider your own existence, do you see it as entirely contingent upon God's will, or as a necessary result of some essence? How does the philosophers' view of determination challenge your understanding of God's absolute sovereignty?
?
This passage distinguishes between efficient cause and requirement. In your daily life, do you sometimes attribute outcomes to secondary causes as if they were independent of God? What is one area where you need to reorient your thinking to see God as the sole creator?
?
The author insists the dispute is not merely verbal. Are there theological or existential questions you have dismissed as 'just semantics'? What might it cost you to take such disputes seriously and examine their real implications for your faith?

The First Case: Determination Caused by the Quiddity
Sanusi presents the first case: if the determination of a quiddity is caused by the quiddity itself, it necessitates a single individual.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first case of determination (ta'ayyun) being caused by the quiddity and why it necessitates a single individual, as well as the distinctions made for self-determined quiddities.

Core Idea
If a quiddity fully necessitates its determination, only one individual can exist.

This lesson introduces the first case in the discussion of determination (ta'ayyun). Sanusi argues that when a quiddity necessitates its own determination completely, the species is limited to one individual. This sets the stage for understanding how multiplicity is impossible in certain cases, including a parallel with the divine essence. The passage also clarifies causal necessitation and addresses potential objections.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the key terms and the overall argument structure.
Focus on the phrase 'انحصر نوعها في الشخص الواحد'.
2
Identify the condition and conclusion
Find the condition: the quiddity necessitates its determination with a complete necessitation. Then see the conclusion: the species is restricted to a single individual.
3
Consider the exception for self-determined quiddities
Note that this applies only when determination is additional to the quiddity. For self-determined quiddities like the Necessary, multiplicity is even more impossible.
This connects to the divine attributes debate.
4
Examine the commentary on causality
The commentary clarifies that the cause necessitates the effect such that wherever the cause exists, the effect must exist, refuting a potential misunderstanding.
Also note the refutation of the commentator of al-Maqasid.
5
Reflect on the deeper objections
The text addresses an objection about multiple determinations from the same quiddity via different existences, and responds that causes are not multiple in actual fact.
This shows the sophistication of the argument.

بأن تكون مقتضية لتعينها اقتضاء تاماً إما بالذات، أو بواسطة ما يلزمها، انحصر نوعها في الشخص الواحد الحاصل من الماهية والتعين الذي علل بها، ولم يمكن أن يوجد معها تعين آخر وإلا انفك عنها التعين الأول فيتخلف المعلول عن علته المستلزمة إياه، هذا إذا كان تعين الماهية زائداً عليها واقتضت الماهية ذلك الاقتضاء، وأما إذا كانت الماهية متعينة بذاتها ممتنعة في نفسها عن فرض الاشتراك فيها، كالواجب تعالى على رأيهم، فلا يتصور هناك تعدد أصلاً، بل هذا أقوى في نفي التعدد

اللهم إلا أن هذا التخلص إنما هو لبعض القائلين بهذا الامتناع والحق على ما نقل عنه أن هذا الكلام من الفلاسفة مشعر بأن التعين يمتاز عن الماهية في الخارج لكن في العلية على تقدير الامتياز أيضاً بحث ظاهر ، فإن العلية مشروطة بالوجود والتشخص عندهم، والشرط من تتمة العلة باعتبار تأثيرها ، فلا يكون معلولاً لها، اللهم إلا أن يمنع مشروطة العلية بالتشخص، وإن اشترطت بالوجود، غايته استلزام الوجود للتشخص، أما توقفه عليه فلا ؛ حتى يلزم المحذور عليه. وفيه نظر لأن الشيء ما لم يتشخص لم يصر علة لتشخص معين وبمثله أبطل الشارح في موقف الجوهر كون الصورة المطلقة علة للهيولى، ومع هذا فلا بد من القول بوجود الكلي الطبيعي في الخارج، وإلا فما لم يوجد لا يكون علة لوجود شيء آخر على ما زعم الحكماء

The second observation - the twelfth objective: Determination if it is caused by the quiddity. That it (the quiddity) be necessitating its determination with a complete necessitation, either essentially or through what accompanies it, its type is restricted to the single individual resulting from the quiddity and the determination which is caused by it, and it is impossible that another determination exist with it, otherwise the first determination would be separated from it and the effect would be absent from its cause that necessitates it. This is if the determination of the quiddity is additional to it and the quiddity necessitates that necessitation. But if the quiddity is self-determined, impossible in itself to suppose sharing in it, like the Necessary Exalted according to their view, then no multiplicity is conceivable at all; rather this is stronger in negating multiplicity. His saying: (Otherwise it would be separated from it, etc.) due to the impossibility of two determinations coexisting. His saying: (from its cause that necessitates it) he indicated by his saying 'that necessitates it' that it is an effect of the kind that is inseparable from the cause; wherever the cause exists, the effect must exist. So the misconception that absence of the effect only follows when the cause exists without the effect, not that the cause exists without the effect coexisting with it, is refuted. His saying: (This is if, etc.) is a refutation of the commentator of al-Maqasid who gave the Necessary Exalted as an example for this division. His saying: (according to their view) they said: His determination, Exalted, is identical to His essence, for if it were additional to Him, composition of the essence of the Necessary Exalted would follow. However, this escape is only for some of those who hold this impossibility. The truth, as reported from him, is that this statement of the philosophers indicates that determination is distinct from the quiddity in external existence, but regarding causation, given the distinction, there is also an apparent investigation. For causality is conditioned by existence and individuation (tashakhkhus) according to them, and the condition is part of the cause in terms of its effect; so it is not an effect of it. However, unless one denies that causality is conditioned by individuation, though it is conditioned by existence; at most existence entails individuation, but it is not dependent on it, so that the problem arises. There is a consideration in this, because a thing, as long as it is not individuated, does not become a cause for a particular individuation. Similarly, the commentator (al-Sharif) in the section on substance invalidated the claim that the absolute form is a cause for hyle. Despite this, one must affirm the existence of the natural universal in the external world; otherwise, what does not exist cannot be a cause for the existence of something else, as the philosophers claim. Determination from existence? His saying: (a complete necessitation) the complete necessitation means that if the quiddity existed, it would not be separated from it by its essence. This determination does not contradict its need in external existence for its agent, so as to contradict possibility. The summary: the quiddity, conditioned by external existence, necessitates determination; as for its existence, it is from the agent. There remains another investigation: the cause for determination, in what is claimed as the necessity of restricting the species to the individual if the quiddity is conditioned by external existence; so why is it not possible that every quiddity, by virtue of its specific existences, necessitates multiple determinations, and the existences attach to it by virtue of causes and dispositions? However, one might say: there is no multiplicity of causes in actual fact; as for dispositions, they only succeed one another upon matter, so the need for them is established. And then there is not much benefit in attributing determinations to the quiddity by virtue of existences.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage presents and examines the first case of the determination (ta'ayyun) of a quiddity (mahiyah): that the determination is caused by the quiddity itself. It begins by stating the condition: the quiddity necessitates its determination with a complete necessitation (iqtida' tamm), either essentially or through a concomitant. The consequence is that the species is restricted to a single individual—the one arising from that quiddity and its determination. No other determination can coexist with it, for that would entail the first determination separating from the quiddity, and the effect would then be absent from its necessitating cause. This applies when the determination is additional to the quiddity. However, if the quiddity is self-determined (like the Necessary Exalted in their view), multiplicity is impossible a fortiori. The commentary then clarifies the points: the impossibility of two determinations coexisting; the meaning of 'necessitating cause' as one that entails the effect wherever it exists, refuting the misunderstanding that the effect only follows after the cause's existence, not with it. The commentator also notes that the example of the Necessary Being here is a refutation of the commentator of al-Maqasid. Further discussion addresses objections about the distinction between determination and quiddity in external reality, the conditions of causality (existence and individuation), and the need for the natural universal to exist externally. Finally, the commentator elaborates on 'complete necessitation' and responds to a potential objection: why could multiple determinations not arise from the same quiddity through different existences? The reply is that causes are not multiple in actual fact, and dispositions only succeed each other in matter.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the argument applies to all quiddities without exception.
Correction: The text distinguishes between quiddities whose determination is additional to them and those that are self-determined (like God), for which multiplicity is even more impossible.

Key Takeaway
When a quiddity fully necessitates its determination, only one individual can exist, and this argument reinforces the impossibility of multiplicity in the divine essence.

Why Determination Cannot Come from Inherence or a Separate Entity
Sanusi eliminates inherence and separateness, then posits the locus as the cause.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why determination must be caused by the locus rather than by an inherent accident or a separate entity, and the logical reasoning behind each elimination.

Core Idea
Determination cannot arise from inherence or separateness; only the locus can specify.

Sanusi continues his analysis of determination by considering the scenario where determination is not caused by the quiddity itself. He systematically eliminates two other possibilities—inherence and separateness—before concluding that the only viable cause is the locus (mahal). This passage is dense with logical reasoning about circularity and equal relation, key tools in kalam.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the three alternatives
Read the Arabic and translation. Note that Sanusi considers three possible causes: (1) something inhering in the quiddity, (2) something separate from it, and (3) its locus. He rejects the first two and accepts the third.
2
Understand the argument against inherence
Focus on why an inherent accident cannot cause determination: because inherence presupposes determination—without determination, inherence is impossible. That would create a circular dependency.
The key phrase is 'حلول شيء في الماهية فرع تعينها' (inherence is a branch of determination).
3
Understand the argument against a separate entity
A separate entity (mubayin) has an equal relation to all individuals and quiddities, so it cannot specify one over another. It lacks the required particularity.
The phrase 'نسبته إلى الكل سواء' (its relation to all is equal) is central.
4
Grasp the conclusion: the locus as the cause
The only remaining option is the locus—the substrate that carries the quiddity. This is what allows for specification without circularity or equal relation.
5
Consider the objection and its resolution
Read the later dialogue: if the locus itself is individuated by the inherent form, that could create a new circularity. The text argues that the inherent's individuation depends on the locus, not the other way around, thus avoiding circularity.
This is a subtle but important refinement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الثاني - المقصد الثاني عشر : التعين إن علل بالماهية
من انحصار الماهية في شخص واحد ; ( وإلا ) أي وإن لم يعلل التعين بالماهية ( فلا يعلل بما يحل فيها ) أي في الماهية؛ لأنه ) أي حلول شيء في الماهية (فرع تعينها)؛ لأنها ما لم تتعين في نفسها لم يتصور حلول شيء فيها، فلا يجوز أن يعلل تعينها بما حل فيها، وإلا دار ، ( ولا ) يعلل أيضاً بما ليس حالاً في الماهية ( ولا محلاً لها؛ إذ ) هو مباين عنها ( نسبته إلى الكل سواء ، فلا يمكن أن يكون علة لتعين شخص دون آخر، ولا لتعيين ماهية دون أخرى (بل) يعلل (بمحلها) أي بمحل الماهية ) فيجوز
قوله : (بل هذا أقوى لأن فرض التعدد فيه محال ، كالمفروض بخلاف صورة الانحصار فإن الفرض فيه ممكن ، وإن كان المفروض محالاً.
قوله : ( وإن لم يعلل التعين إلخ ) أي لا يكفي الفاعل مع الماهية في اقتضاء التعين، بل يكون نسبتهما إلى جميع التعينات على السواء، فلا بد من أمر آخر مخصص.
قوله : (بما يحل فيها أي من حيث حلوله فيها بأن يكون ذلك الأمر باعتبار حلوله في الماهية مخصصاً لفيضان التعين المخصوص، وإنما قيدنا بالحيثية لأنه بدون اعتبار الحلول داخل في المباين.
قوله : (لم يتصور إلخ على صيغة المعلوم أي لا يصير ذا صورة حلول شيء فيها إذ الحلول في الأمر المبهم محال بالبديهة، فيكون حلول شيء في الماهية موقوفاً على تعينها، وتعينها لكونه معلولاً لذلك الشيء باعتبار الحلول موقوفاً على الحلول فيدور، وبهذا التحرير اندفع أنه يجوز أن يكون شيء علةً من حيث ذاته ويكون حلوله موقوفاً على تشخصه، على أنا لا نسلم أن الحلول موقوف على تشخصها بل على وجودها، ولا يلزم من توقفه على الوجود ترقفه على التشخص الذي هو مع الوجود أو متأخر عنه بالذات، نعم يتم ذلك إذا كان التشخص متقدماً على الوجود أو عينه ثم اعلم أن الأمر الحال غير لوازم الماهية لأنه من العوارض الخارجية، فلا يرد أنه مناف لما تقدم من جواز كون علة التشخص من لوازم الماهية على ما وهم .
قوله : (إذ هو مباين عنها سواء كان مجرداً أو مادياً، فلا يمكن أن يكون علة مخصصة لفيضان شخص مخصوص من الفاعل على ماهية دون أخرى .
قوله : ( بل يعلل بمحلها أي بل تكون العلة المخصصة محلها إما بنفسه أو بواسطة ما
قوله : ( فرع تعينها إلخ) أي يتوقف عليه متأخراً عنه ذاتاً، ولا يكفي المقارنة الزمانية حتى يدفع الدور بها، وقد يجاب بأن حلول شيء في الماهية وإن توقف على تشخصها لكن تشخصها لا يتوقف على حلول ما حل فيه حتى يدور بل على ذاته وهذا بعينه وجه تجويزهم تشخص الهيولى بالصورة الحالة فيها . فإن قلت : تشخص المحل حينئذ يتوقف على تشخص الحال إذ لا معنى لجعل الذات المبهمة علة للتشخص، وتشخص الحال إنما هو من المحل فيدور، قلت : كون تشخص الحال من المحل مبني على عدم جواز كونه مما حل فيه للزوم الدور، وهو أول
The second observation - the twelfth objective: Determination if it is caused by the quiddity. From the restriction of the quiddity to one individual; (Otherwise) meaning if determination is not caused by the quiddity (then it is not caused by what inheres in it) i.e. in the quiddity; because (i.e. the inherence of something in the quiddity is a branch of its determination); because as long as it is not determined in itself, the inherence of anything in it is inconceivable. So it is not permissible that its determination be caused by what inheres in it, otherwise a circularity. (Nor) is it caused by what is not inherent in the quiddity (nor a locus for it; since) it is separate from it (its relation to all is equal), so it cannot be a cause for the determination of one individual rather than another, nor for the determination of one quiddity rather than another. (Rather) it is caused (by its locus) i.e. the locus of the quiddity, so it is permissible. His saying: (Rather this is stronger because the supposition of multiplicity therein is impossible, like the supposed; contrary to the form of restriction, for the supposition therein is possible, even if the supposed is impossible.) His saying: (And if determination is not caused, etc.) i.e. the agent along with the quiddity is insufficient for necessitating determination; rather their relation to all determinations is equal, so there must be another specifying factor. His saying: (by what inheres in it means in terms of its inherence in it, such that that thing, by virtue of its inherence in the quiddity, specifies the emanation of the particular determination. We qualified by 'in terms of' because without considering inherence it falls under the separate.) His saying: (is not conceived, etc.) in the active voice, i.e. it does not become capable of having something inhere in it, for inherence in an indeterminate thing is obviously impossible. So the inherence of something in the quiddity is dependent on its determination, and its determination, since it is an effect of that thing in terms of inherence, is dependent on the inherence; thus a circularity. With this exposition it is refuted that it is possible for something to be a cause by its essence while its inherence is dependent on its individuation, though we do not concede that inherence depends on its individuation, but rather on its existence, and its dependence on existence does not entail its dependence on individuation, which is concomitant with existence or posterior to it in essence. Yes, that would hold if individuation were prior to existence or identical to it. Then know that the inherent thing is not among the necessary concomitants of the quiddity, for it is among the external accidents, so it is not open to the objection that it is incompatible with what preceded regarding the permissibility of the cause of individuation being among the necessary concomitants of the quiddity, as some might imagine. His saying: (since it is separate from it, whether it be abstract or material, so it cannot be a specifying cause for the emanation of a particular individual from the agent upon one quiddity rather than another.) His saying: (Rather it is caused by its locus i.e. rather the specifying cause is its locus, either itself or through something) His saying: (is a branch of its determination, etc.) i.e. it depends on it, being posterior to it in essence; temporal simultaneity is not sufficient to avoid circularity. It may be answered that though the inherence of something in the quiddity depends on its individuation, its individuation does not depend on the inherence of what inheres in it so as to cause circularity, but rather on its essence. This is precisely the justification for their allowing the individuation of hyle by the form inherent in it. If you say: The individuation of the locus then depends on the individuation of the inherent, since it is meaningless to make an indeterminate essence a cause for individuation, and the individuation of the inherent is only from the locus, so there is circularity. I say: The fact that the individuation of the inherent is from the locus is based on the impossibility of its being from what inheres in it, due to circularity, and that is more plausible.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage presents the second case: when determination is not caused by the quiddity itself, the commentator systematically eliminates other possibilities. First, determination cannot be caused by something that inheres in the quiddity (say, an accident), because inherence presupposes the quiddity's determination—otherwise inherence in an indeterminate thing is impossible. That would lead to a circularity (dawr): the determination would depend on inherence, and inherence depends on determination. Second, determination cannot be caused by something separate (mubayin) from the quiddity, whether abstract or material, because such a thing's relation to all individuals and quiddities is equal, so it cannot specify one over another. Therefore, the only remaining option is that the cause is the locus (mahal) of the quiddity—i.e., the subject or substrate that carries the quiddity. The commentary then addresses several points: a gloss on 'rather this is stronger' refers back to the first case, clarifying that the impossibility of multiplicity in the Necessary Being is absolute, while in the first case (restriction) multiplicity is only impossible by supposition but not inconceivable in itself. Another gloss explains the phrase 'if determination is not caused' emphasizing that the agent and quiddity together are insufficient without a specifying factor. The commentator further clarifies how to understand the notion of 'inherence'—it is only in terms of inherence that the cause would be considered; otherwise, it falls under the separate. He then refutes a potential objection that something could be a cause by its essence while its inherence depends on individuation, by arguing that inherence does not depend on individuation but on existence; thus no circularity arises. Finally, he distinguishes the inherent accident from necessary concomitants (lawazim) of the quiddity, so that the earlier permissibility of the cause being a necessary concomitant does not conflict with the current argument. The passage ends with a dialogue: if it is objected that the individuation of the locus depends on the individuation of the inherent (leading to circularity), the reply is that the inherent's individuation coming from the locus is itself based on avoiding circularity, which is the more plausible position.

Key Terms
تعين (ta'ayyun)
حلول (hulul)
مباين (mubayin)
محل (mahal)
دور (dawr)
تشخص (tashakhkhus)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that an inherent accident can cause determination because it is attached to the quiddity.
Correction: But inherence itself requires the quiddity to be already determined; otherwise, inherence in an indeterminate thing is impossible. So determination cannot come from an inherent accident without circularity.

Checkpoint
Why cannot determination be caused by something separate (mubayin) from the quiddity?
A) Because it causes circularity.
B) Because it would require inherence first.
C) Because its relation to all individuals is equal, so it cannot specify one.
D) Because it is always a necessary concomitant.

Key Takeaway
When determination is not caused by the quiddity, it must be caused by the locus, because inherence leads to circularity and a separate entity lacks specification power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever assumed that your unique identity (ta'ayyun) comes from something that 'inheres' in you, like your personality or habits? Sanusi argues that inherence depends on prior determination. Can you trace your own sense of self back to something more fundamental? What would that be, and how does this passage challenge your usual thinking?
?
Consider a major decision you face. Are you prone to think that a distant, abstract principle (like fate or divine will considered in isolation) determines the specific outcome? Sanusi says such a separate entity relates equally to all possibilities. Does that challenge your view of how specific events in your life are caused? How do you respond to that challenge?
?
The locus is the bearer of determination. In your spiritual life, what is the locus that carries your faith? Is it something inherent in you, or something external? How does this argument push you to examine the basis of your deen more honestly?

Individuation by Receptacles: Essential and Accidental
Al-Jurjani explains how multiplicity of individuals arises from receptacle multiplicity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the multiplicity of individuals of a single essence arises from the multiplicity of receptacles, both essentially and accidentally.

Core Idea
Multiplicity of individuals comes from the receptacle, not the essence itself.

Al-Jurjani explains a key principle of individuation: that the same essence can have multiple individuals only if the receptacles (loci) are multiple. He distinguishes two ways: essential multiplicity of receptacles and accidental multiplicity due to varying dispositions. This passage sets the foundation for understanding how material substances are individuated.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation. Let the author's own phrasing guide your initial understanding.
Notice the terms 'qābil' and 'isti‘dād'.
2
Identify the two types of receptacle multiplicity
The passage presents two ways: essential (bi al-dhāt) and accidental (bi sabab a‘rāḍ). Find the examples for each and understand how they differ.
Essential: receptacles themselves are multiple by nature. Accidental: a common receptacle acquires different dispositions.
3
Understand the converse case
When the receptacle does not multiply essentially and no differing dispositions occur, the essence is confined to one individual. Relate this to the example of the celestial sphere's hylē.
This shows the principle applies in both directions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تعددها أي تعدد أفرادها بتعدد القوابل أي المحال إما بالذات كهيولات الأفلاك القابلة لصورها الجسمية وكالنطف القابلة للصورة الإنسانية. وإما بسبب أعراض تكتنفها كهيولى العناصر الأربعة، فإنها واحدة مشتركة بينها، وقد عرض لها استعدادات مختلفة بحسب القرب والبعد من الفلك، فلذلك تعدد أشخاصها. وإذا لم يتعدد القابل بالذات ولم يتصور فيها استعدادات متفاوتة انحصرت الماهية الحالة في شخص واحد أيضا كهيولى كل فلك بالقياس إلى صورته النوعية.
Its multiplicity, meaning the multiplicity of its individuals, is by the multiplicity of receptacles, i.e., loci, either essentially, like the hylē of the celestial spheres receptive to their corporeal forms, and like the sperm receptive to the human form; or by means of accidents that surround it, like the hylē of the four elements, for it is one, common to them, and different dispositions have occurred to it according to proximity and distance from the celestial sphere, so their individuals multiply. And when the receptacle does not multiply essentially and no differing dispositions are conceived in it, the essence that inheres in it is confined to one individual as well, like the hylē of each celestial sphere in relation to its specific form.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage defines the principle of individuation (al-ta'ayyun) for essences that have multiple individuals. Al-Jurjani explains that the multiplicity of individuals of a single species arises from the multiplicity of the receptacles (qawābil, singular qābil) in which the essence inheres. This multiplicity occurs in two ways: first, essentially (bi-al-dhāt) — the receptacles themselves are multiple by their own natures, such as the hylē of different celestial spheres receiving their respective corporeal forms, or the sperm (nuṭaf) receiving the human form; second, by means of accidents (a‘rāḍ) that surround the receptacle — for example, the common hylē of the four elements, which is one but acquires different dispositions (isti‘dādāt) due to varying proximity to the celestial sphere, thus causing multiplicity of individuals of each element. The passage then states the converse: if the receptacle does not multiply essentially and does not admit varying dispositions, then the essence that inheres in it is confined to a single individual, as in the case of the hylē of each celestial sphere relative to its specific form. This sets the foundation for the discussion of immaterial substances.

Key Terms
qābil
qabīl
mahiyyah
isti‘dād
hylē
ta‘ayyun

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Multiplicity always comes from the essence itself.
Correction: According to this passage, multiplicity of individuals arises entirely from the multiplicity of receptacles, not from the essence.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what are the two ways that the multiplicity of individuals of a single essence arises from the multiplicity of receptacles?
A) Essentially and accidentally
B) By nature and by divine will
C) By substance and by accident
D) By form and by matter

Key Takeaway
The multiplicity of individuals of an essence is determined by the multiplicity of its receptacles, either essentially or accidentally.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your very individuality as a human being comes not from your essence but from the receptacle (your body) and the accidents that have surrounded it, then what part of 'you' is truly your own? How will this reshape your understanding of your worth and your treatment of others whose receptacles differ?
?
The passage explains that differing dispositions arise from external factors like proximity to the celestial sphere. Consider the dispositions—your talents, health, circumstances—that make you who you are. How many of these did you choose? If they are given, not earned, what attitude toward God should this cultivate? What will you do today to practice this attitude?

The Argument for Confinement of Immaterial Substances
Al-Jurjani states the confinement argument for immaterial substances.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why immaterial substances (mujarradāt) are said to have their species confined to a single individual.

Core Idea
Immaterial substances have no receptacle, so their individuation is by essence itself.

Al-Jurjani applies the earlier principle of individuation to immaterial substances. Since multiplicity comes from matter as receptacle, what lacks matter must lack multiplicity within its species. Let's examine this argument closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the argument builds on the previous discussion about material substances.
The argument relies on the principle that multiplicity arises from receptacles (matter).
2
Understand the key premise
Identify the premise: multiplicity of individuals of a single essence is due to multiplicity of receptacles (matter). For immaterial substances, there is no matter, so no receptacle.
3
Grasp the conclusion
The consequence is that each species of immaterial substance has only one individual. Al-Jurjani states that the cause of individuation is not a locus, so it must be the essence itself or its concomitants, leading to confinement.
This conclusion is deduced from the absence of a receptacle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبنوا على هذا الذي ذكروه من أن تعدد أفراد الماهية الواحد إنما يكون بتعدد قابلها، أعني مادتها على أحد الوجهين أن ما ليس بمادي ويسمي مجرداً ومفارقاً، فنوعه منحصر في الشخص الواحد؛ لأن علة تعينه ليست المحل، إذ لا محل لغير المادي، فهي إما الماهية نفسها أو ما يلزمها فيلزم الانحصار كما مر. وقد يقال: لم لا يجوز أن يكون للمجرد محل غير المادة الجسمية فيتعدد بتعدد ذلك المحل، إما ذاتاً أو استعداداً يحل فيه، كما يدل عليه قوله: وأما بسبب أعراض إلخ، فلا يرد أن هاهنا قسماً آخر وهو أن يعلل بما يحل في محلها. قوله: (لم لا يجوز أن يكون إلخ) ولم يقم دليل على امتناع حلول الجوهر المجرد في الجوهر المجرد.
And they built upon this which they mentioned, that the multiplicity of individuals of a single essence is only by the multiplicity of its receptacle, i.e., its matter, in one of two ways: that what is not material, and is called immaterial and separate, its species is confined to the single individual, because the cause of its individuation is not the locus, since there is no locus for the immaterial; so it is either the essence itself or what accompanies it, so confinement follows as has passed. And it may be said: Why is it not permissible for the immaterial to have a locus other than corporeal matter, and thus become multiple by the multiplicity of that locus, either essentially or by disposition inherent in it, as is indicated by his statement: 'And by means of accidents, etc.'? So it is not refuted that there is another division, namely that it is caused by what inheres in its locus. His statement: 'Why is it not permissible, etc.' And no proof has been established for the impossibility of the immaterial substance inhering in an immaterial substance.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage applies the principle of individuation to immaterial substances (mujarradāt). Al-Jurjani states that the philosophers (or the text's authors) have built on the previous principle: since the multiplicity of individuals of a single essence is due to the multiplicity of receptacles (matter), then anything that is not material — called immaterial (mujarrad) and separate (mufāriq) — will have its species confined to a single individual. The reason is that the cause of its individuation is not a locus (maḥall), because there is no locus for the immaterial; therefore, its individuation must be by the essence itself or its necessary concomitants, which necessarily results in confinement to one individual. An objection is then raised: why cannot the immaterial have a non-corporeal locus, so that it becomes multiple by the multiplicity of that locus, either essentially or by disposition? The objector claims that this possibility is implied by the earlier mention of accidents. The commentator responds in the gloss: the author's statement 'Why is it not permissible...' is merely raising the objection, and no proof has been given for the impossibility of an immaterial substance inhering in another immaterial substance, leaving the question open. Thus the passage presents the standard position and a critical challenge.

Key Terms
mujarrad
mufāriq
ta‘ayyun
maḥall
mahiyyah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that immaterial substances can have multiple individuals just like material ones, because they are still existents.
Correction: The passage clarifies that without matter as a principle of individuation, there is no basis for multiple individuals within the same species. Each immaterial essence is self-individuated.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the cause of individuation for immaterial substances?
A) Their matter and form
B) A non-corporeal locus
C) The essence itself or its accompaniments
D) Their location in the celestial spheres

Key Takeaway
Immaterial substances are self-individuated by their essence, leading to one individual per species.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider something you believe defines your identity: your family, your career, your body. According to this passage, true individuation for immaterial beings comes from the essence itself, not from an external receptacle. If your soul is immaterial, what does this say about where you should look to find your true self? Are you investing more in external receptacles than in discovering your essence?
?
The argument states that if the cause of individuation is the essence itself, then the species is confined to one individual. How does this deepen your appreciation for the Islamic declaration that God is One (Aḥad)? Does this make the uniqueness of God more intellectually compelling or more personally demanding?
?
The passage builds on the principle that multiplicity comes from receptacles. Think of an area in your life where you feel scattered or divided. Could it be that you are seeking identity in too many 'receptacles' rather than seeking unity in your essence? What one change could you make today to move toward internal coherence?

The Objection: Could an Immaterial Substance Have a Non-Corporeal Locus?
Al-Jurjani raises an objection against the confinement argument and notes the lack of a proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that immaterial substances might have a non-corporeal locus, and the response that no proof prohibits this.

Core Idea
The possibility of an immaterial substance inhering in another immaterial substance is not proven impossible.

After presenting the confinement argument, Al-Jurjani raises a critical objection: why cannot an immaterial substance have a non-corporeal locus? This challenges the assumption that only matter can serve as a receptacle. The gloss then notes that no proof has been established against such inherence.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection passage
Read the Arabic and translation of the objection. The objector questions the impossibility of a non-corporeal locus for immaterial substances.
The objection references an earlier statement about accidents as possible principles.
2
Analyze the objector's reasoning
The objector suggests that an immaterial could inhere in another immaterial, either in essence or by disposition, thereby allowing multiplicity through the multiplicity of that locus.
3
Examine the gloss response
The commentator (or author in gloss) notes that the objector's statement is merely raising a question, and that no proof has been given to show that such inherence is impossible.
This leaves the objection unanswered, highlighting a potential gap in the argument.

Source Text

Human Souls: Multiplicity Through Attachment, Not Materiality
Al-Jurjani explains souls' multiplicity via attachment to bodies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why human souls are multiple despite being immaterial, and how this distinguishes them from intellects.

Core Idea
Human souls multiply by governing bodies, not by being material.

This passage addresses a key objection: if souls are immaterial, how can they be many? Al-Jurjani explains that multiplicity comes from attachment—their role as governors of bodies—not from inherence in matter. Understanding this distinction is crucial for grasping the Islamic philosophical view of the soul.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice the objection-and-answer structure.
The passage begins with a hypothetical objection and then provides the answer.
2
Identify key terms
Focus on 'nafs nāṭiqah', 'mujarrad', 'ta‘alluq', 'tadbīr', 'taṣarruf'. These are essential to the argument.
Look up their meanings if needed.
3
Understand the core argument
Why does attachment cause multiplicity? Why are intellects different? Follow the contrast between souls and intellects.
The key point: souls are attached to matter as governors, intellects are free from any attachment.
4
Reflect on the gloss
Consider the additional comment about individuation by receptacle. It reinforces why attachment causes multiplicity.
This is a deeper philosophical point about individuation.
5
Test your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to verify comprehension.
The answer is based solely on this passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولما كان لقائل أن يقول: النفوس الناطقة متعددة مع كونها مجردة عندهم أجاب بقوله: ( والنفوس الإنسانية إنما تعددت وإن لم تكن (مادية) أي حالة في المادة ( لتعلقها بالمادة تعلق التدبير والتصرف، فهي في حكم الماديات، فتتعدد بحسب تعدد المادة التي تتعلق بها، بخلاف العقول المجردة عن المادة بحسب الذات والتعلق فإن أنواعها منحصرة في أشخاصها. ( قال بعض الفضلاء: إذا كان تعين الماهية المتعددة الأفراد معللا بالقابل فالقابل إن كان تشخصه بماهيته أو لوازمها انحصر نوعه في شخصه، ولم يقولوا به أي بكون تعينه معللاً بماهيته وانحصاره في شخص واحد.
And since it could be said: The rational souls are multiple while being immaterial according to them, he answered with his statement: 'And human souls are only multiple, even though they are not material, i.e., not inherent in matter, because of their attachment to matter as attachment of governance and disposal; so they are in the same ruling as material things, so they become multiple according to the multiplicity of the matter to which they are attached, contrary to intellects which are free from matter both in essence and attachment, for their species are confined to their individuals.' Some virtuous ones said: If the individuation of an essence having multiple individuals is caused by the receptacle, then if the receptacle's individuation is by its essence or its concomitants, its species is confined to its individual, and they did not hold it, i.e., that its individuation is caused by its essence and its confinement to one individual.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage addresses an objection concerning human souls: they are multiple even though they are considered immaterial (mujarrad) by the philosophers. Al-Jurjani presents the answer: human souls (al-nufūs al-nāṭiqah) are multiple not because they inhere in matter (they are not material in that sense), but because of their attachment to matter (ta‘alluq) as a relation of governance (tadbīr) and disposal (taṣarruf). This attachment makes them like material things in the sense that their multiplicity follows the multiplicity of the bodies (the matter) they govern. In contrast, the intellects (‘uqūl) are completely free from matter both in essence and in attachment, so each species of intellect is confined to a single individual. The passage then adds a comment from 'some virtuous ones' (ba‘ḍ al-fuḍalā'), likely the commentator, clarifying that if individuation is by the receptacle, and the receptacle's own individuation is by its essence or its concomitants, then that receptacle's species would be confined to one individual—but the philosophers do not hold that view for all receptacles. This reinforces the distinction: human souls individuate via their attachment to multiple bodies, while intellects, lacking any attachment, have species confined to single individuals.

Key Terms
nafs nāṭiqah
mujarrad
ta‘alluq
tadbīr
taṣarruf
‘aql

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think souls are material because they are multiple.
Correction: The passage clarifies that multiplicity arises from attachment to matter, not from being material themselves.

Checkpoint
Why are human souls multiple according to the passage, despite being immaterial?
A) Because they inhere in different bodies
B) Because of their attachment to matter in terms of governance and disposal
C) Because they have different essences
D) Because they are created from different elements

Key Takeaway
Human souls are multiple because they govern bodies, not because they are material; each soul is distinct by its association with a particular body.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your soul governs your body—but have you ever felt that your identity is more than just your body? How does knowing that your soul is distinct because of this particular body change how you see your own uniqueness before God?
?
If souls multiply through attachment to bodies, then your soul is not merely a generic entity. How does this accountability affect the way you treat your body and use it to obey God?
?
The intellects are each alone in their species—no two are alike. Your soul, however, shares its species with others. How does that humbling reality remind you that you are not self-sufficient and must seek guidance from the One who created all souls?
