Unity of the Matter of the Elements
Two interpretations of the unity of the matter of the elements.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the debate about whether the matter of the elements is numerically one or only generically one.

Core Idea
The matter of the elements is one in essence, becoming multiple only externally.

This passage opens a key debate in Islamic cosmology: Are the four elements (fire, air, water, earth) composed of a single underlying matter or distinct matters? Some philosophers argued for a single matter that becomes multiple individuals due to external factors like proximity to the sphere.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once. Note the two interpretations presented.
2
Identify the two interpretations
The passage offers two views: (1) numerical unity of the matter, and (2) generic unity. Find where each is mentioned.
3
Understand the evidence
Notice the evidence cited for the second view: their explicit statement that individuals multiply due to proximity to the sphere.
This supports generic unity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العناصر شخصاً، وقد يقال مرادهم باتحاد هيولى العناصر شخصاً أنه شخص واحد لا انفصال في ذاته وإنما هو من خارج وبسببه يصير أشخاصاً متعددة. وربما يدعى أن مرادهم بالاتحاد الاتحاد النوعي وزيادة التشخص تصرف من الناقل بمقتضى فهمه، يدل عليه تصريحهم بتعدد أشخاصها بسبب القرب والبعد من الفلك، كما مر آنفاً. قوله: (بل تعينه عندهم بصورته فيه بحث؛ لأن هذا مخالف للمشهور، وسيأتي أيضاً في موقف الجوهر وهو أن الهيولى محتاجة إلى الصورة في بقائها، والصورة محتاجة إليها في تعينها. وقد يجاب: بأن لا تنافي بين الاحتياجين فيجوز أن يكون احتياج الهيولى إلى الصورة في البقاء والتشخص معاً، ولا محذور في احتياج كل منهما إلى ذات الأخرى في التشخص، كما صرح الإمام في شرح الإشارات. قيل: والتحقيق أن تشخص الصورة بكون الهيولي المعينة من حيث قابلة لتشخصها، وتشخص الهيولى بالصورة المطلقة من حيث هي فاعلة لتشخصها، ونحن نقول: سيشير الشارح إلى بطلان هذا التحقيق في موقف الجوهر حيث قال: قلنا: الواحد
The elements as individuals, and it is said: Their intention by the unity of the matter of the elements as one individual is that it is one individual with no division in its essence, and it is only from outside that it becomes multiple individuals. Perhaps it is claimed that their meaning by unity is generic unity, and the addition of individuation is a misrepresentation by the transmitter according to his understanding, indicated by their explicit statement that its individuals multiply due to nearness and distance from the sphere, as passed earlier. His statement: (Rather its determination according to them is through its form) contains a discussion; because this contradicts what is well-known, and it will also come in the position of substance that matter is in need of form for its subsistence, and form is in need of it for its determination. It may be answered: There is no incompatibility between the two needs, so it is permissible that matter's need for form be for subsistence and individuation together, and there is no problem in each needing the essence of the other for individuation, as the Imam stated in his commentary on al-Isharat. It was said: The verification is that the individuation of form is through the individuated matter being a receptacle for its individuation, and the individuation of matter is through the absolute form insofar as it is an agent for its individuation. And we say: The commentator will indicate the invalidity of this verification in the position of substance where he said: We said: The one
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage contains two points. First, regarding the elements: some say that the unity of the matter of elements as a single individual means it is one in essence without internal division, becoming multiple only through external factors. Others claim that their intended unity is generic unity, and the addition of specific individuation is a misunderstanding by the transmitter. This is supported by their explicit statement that individuals multiply due to proximity to the sphere. Second, there is an objection: the statement that determination is through form is contradictory to the well-known position that matter needs form for subsistence and form needs matter for determination. The answer is that these mutual needs are not incompatible; matter needs form for both subsistence and individuation together, and there is no circularity. An alternative verification is proposed: form is individuated by matter being receptive, and matter is individuated by absolute form as agent. But the commentator dismisses this verification as invalid in the position of substance (mawqif al-jawhar).

Key Terms
عناصر
اتحاد
هيولى
تشخص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All Islamic philosophers agree that the four elements have distinct and separate matters from the beginning.
Correction: Some philosophers, as reported here, held that the matter of the elements is one, either numerically or generically, and that individuation occurs later.

Checkpoint
What is the evidence cited for the claim that the unity of elemental matter is generic rather than numerical?
A) The matter is indivisible in essence.
B) Individuals multiply due to nearness and distance from the sphere.
C) The transmitter said so.
D) The philosophers explicitly state generic unity.

Key Takeaway
The unity of elemental matter is debated: either numerically one or generically one, with evidence from celestial proximity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage shows that a transmitter might add his own interpretation to a text. Have you ever conveyed something you were not fully sure of, adding your own spin? How can you ensure you transmit knowledge accurately, even when you disagree?
?
The philosophers used the proximity to the celestial sphere as evidence for their view. In your own life, do you often rely on external factors (like status or environment) to define your identity? How does this relate to the Islamic understanding that true identity is based on your relationship with Allah, not physical circumstances?
?
If the matter of the elements is one in essence, what does that imply about the interconnectedness of creation? How should this affect the way you treat the natural world and the resources you use?

Objection to Determination by Form and Its Resolution
Objection to the view that determination is through form, with answer and alternative verification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that determination through form leads to circularity and how it is resolved.

Core Idea
Matter needs form for subsistence and individuation without logical circularity.

A common objection in Islamic philosophy states that if an entity's determination (ta'ayyun) is through its form, then form also needs matter for its own determination, leading to mutual dependency. This lesson examines that objection and the response that the two needs are not incompatible.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage. Note the objection, the answer, and the alternative verification.
2
Identify the objection
Find the statement that determination by form contradicts the well-known position. Understand why it is a problem.
3
Understand the answer and verification
The answer says there is no incompatibility; matter can need form for both subsistence and individuation. The alternative verification specifies how each needs the other in different respects.
The commentator later rejects this verification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Mutual need between matter and form leads to circular causation and is impossible.
Correction: The answer clarifies that the needs are in different respects (subsistence vs. individuation) and thus no circularity occurs.

Checkpoint
According to the answer in the passage, why is there no incompatibility between the needs of matter and form?
A) Because they are separate substances.
B) Because the needs are in different respects.
C) Because the objection is invalid.
D) Because matter does not really need form.

Key Takeaway
The objection that determination by form leads to circularity is resolved by recognizing that matter and form have mutual needs in different respects.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think about a relationship in your life where you depend on someone and they depend on you. Does that create a vicious circle or a healthy interdependence? How does the lesson's distinction between different respects help you evaluate this?
?
The commentator rejects a seemingly plausible verification. Have you ever been too confident in your own reasoning? How can this lesson instill intellectual humility in your approach to theological questions?
?
Matter and form are both created. How does their mutual dependence point to the absolute independence of Allah? How should this affect the way you rely on created things versus relying on Allah?

The Dilemma of Determination: Essence or Infinite Chain?
Enumeration of three possibilities for the cause of determination and their consequences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the cause of determination cannot be the essence itself or an infinite chain of recipients without leading to absurdity.

Core Idea
Determination must have a cause, but neither essence nor an infinite chain of recipients is tenable.

In this passage, the author presents a foundational dilemma: what causes an individual to be this particular individual? He considers three possible causes: the essence itself, what inheres in it, or another recipient. Each leads to unacceptable consequences, including circularity and infinite regress.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three options
Read the passage and list the three possibilities for the cause of determination mentioned by the author.
2
Trace the consequences
For each option, note the consequence that follows: limitation, circularity, or infinite regress.
The passage explicitly states each consequence.
3
Understand the conclusion
The author concludes that the third option (infinite chain) leads to absurdity: a single body composed of infinite recipients.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدور الذي ادعيتموه ، ( وإن كان تشخصه ) بقابل آخر لزم التسلسل ) ؛ لأننا ننقل الكلام إلى تشخص ذلك القابل الآخر. والحاصل أنه لو صح دليلكم على أن تعدد أفراد الماهية النوعية إنما يكون لقابلها للزم تسلسل القوابل إلى غير النهاية، وتركب الجسم الواحد منها هذا خلف . ( والجواب ) عن اعتراض بعض الفضلاء (بأن تعينه) أي تعين القابل معللاً ) بأعراض تلحقه لاستعدادات متعاقبة إلى غير النهاية ) بحيث يكون كل استعداد سابق معداً للاحق، وهذه الاستعدادات ليست مجتمعة معاً بل متعاقبة، ومثل هذا التسلسل جائز عندهم ( لا يجدي ) خبر لقوله : والجواب، وإنما قلنا أنه لا يجدي نفعاً لأنهم لما جوزوا تعينه ) أي تعين القابل ( بما حل فيه ) لأن مرجع ما ذكروه هو أن علة تشخص القابل أمور حالة فيه سابقة على ذلك التشخص، ومقارنة لتشخص آخر معلل بأمور أخرى متقدمة على التشخص الآخر، وهكذا إلى ما لا نهاية له، ثم قال: قوله : ( لأننا ننقل الكلام إلخ بأن نقول : إن كان تشخصه بماهيته لزم انحصاره، وذلك يستلزم انحصار القابل الأول وهو يستلزم انحصار الماهية في فرد واحد وإن كان بما حل فيه لزم الدور وإن كان لقابل آخر ننقل الكلام، وهكذا. قوله : ( بأن تعينه إلخ) تفصيل الجواب : أنه إن كان الترديد المذكور في تشخصه الفردي فنختار أن علة تشخصه نفس ماهيته وأنه منحصر في شخص واحد كما عرفت تفصيله، وإن كان في تشخصه التخصصي الحاصل في ضمن أشخاص الأجسام العنصرية وأشخاص الأفلاك الجزئية، فنقول : إن مخصص ذلك التشخص عوارض تلحق ذلك القابل، إما من جانب الفاعل فقط كما في أشخاص الأفلاك الجزئية، كما سيجيء في الفلكيات وإما باعتبار عوارض سابقة عليها تكون معدة للحوق هذه العوارض مقتضية لتخصص القابل وتشخص حصصه، وتلك العوارض ليست مشخصة لذات القابل بل هو متشخص بذاته كما علمت . وحينئذ اندفع جواب المصنف بأنه لما جوزتم تشخص الهيولى بالعوارض الحالة فيها فليجز ذلك في الماهية؛ لأنه ليس هاهنا تشخص القابل بما حل فيه بل تشخص أبعاضه بما حل في نفسه، فتدبر فإن هذا المقام من الغوامض .
The circularity you claimed, (and if its individuation) is by another recipient, an infinite regress follows); because we transfer the discussion to the individuation of that other recipient. The conclusion: if your proof were valid that the multiplicity of individuals of the specific essence is only due to its recipient, then an infinite regress of recipients would follow, and a single body would be composed of them, which is absurd. (The answer) to the objection of some virtuous ones (that its determination) i.e., the determination of the recipient is caused by accidents that attach to it due to successive preparednesses ad infinitum) such that each prior preparedness is a preparation for the subsequent, and these preparednesses are not simultaneous but successive, and such a regress is permissible for them (is not beneficial) – predicate of His statement: 'and the answer'. And we only said it is not beneficial because when they allowed its determination) i.e., the determination of the recipient (by what inheres in it) because the purport of what they mentioned is that the cause of the individuation of the recipient is matters inhering in it prior to that individuation, and concurrent with another individuation caused by other matters preceding that other individuation, and so on ad infinitum. Then he said: His statement: (For we transfer the discourse etc. by saying: if its individuation is by its essence, then its limitation follows, and that entails the limitation of the first recipient, which entails the limitation of the essence to one individual; and if by what inheres in it, then circularity follows; and if by another recipient, we transfer the discourse, and so on.) His statement: (That its determination etc.) a detailed answer: if the aforementioned disjunction concerns its individual individuation, then we choose that the cause of its individuation is its very essence and that it is confined to one individual as you know its detail; and if it concerns its specific individuation occurring within the individuals of elemental bodies and the particular celestial orbs, then we say: the particularizer of that individuation is accidents that attach to that recipient, either from the side of the agent only, as in the particular celestial orbs, as will come in the celestial matters; or by consideration of prior accidents that serve as preparations for the attachment of these accidents, necessitating the specification of the recipient and the individuation of its portions; and those accidents do not individuate the essence of the recipient, but it is individuated by itself as you have learned. And then the author's answer is refuted: because you allowed the individuation of hyle by accidents inhering in it, so let that be allowed in the essence; because here there is no individuation of the recipient by what inheres in it, but rather the individuation of its parts by what inheres in itself. So reflect, for this station is among the subtleties.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical exchange on the cause of determination (al-ta'ayyun). It begins by presenting an objection: if determination were caused by the essence, it would limit the essence to one individual; if by a recipient, then either the recipient's determination is by its essence (again limitation) or by another recipient (infinite regress). A respondent (some virtuous one) offers an answer: the recipient's determination is caused by successive accidents (preparednesses) that are not simultaneous, and such a regress is permissible. The author retorts that this answer is not beneficial because it concedes that the recipient's determination is by accidents inhering in it. Since they already allowed this for the recipient, why not allow the same for the essence? The author then provides a detailed counter by distinguishing two types of individuation: individual (al-tashakhkhus al-fardi) and specific (al-tashakhkhus al-takhassusi). For individual individuation, the cause is the essence itself, and it is confined to one individual. For specific individuation (e.g., within elemental bodies or celestial orbs), the cause is accidents that attach to the recipient, either purely from the agent or through a chain of preparatory accidents. Importantly, these accidents do not individuate the essence of the recipient; the recipient is individuated by itself. The author concludes that the initial response is untenable because it treats the individuation of the recipient as by inhering accidents, whereas in reality it is the individuation of its parts. The passage ends with a call for deep reflection.

Key Terms
التعين
القابل
التسلسل
الدور

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what follows if determination is caused by another recipient?
A) Circularity
B) Limitation of essence
C) Infinite regress
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
The cause of determination cannot be an infinite chain of recipients because it would require a single body to be composed of infinite recipients, which is absurd.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a flaw in your character, do you defer its correction by pointing to another cause—'I am this way because of my upbringing, my circumstances, my environment'—creating an infinite chain of excuses? What would it mean to accept that determination ultimately comes from your own essence—your choices—and to take responsibility now?
?
If the absurdity of an infinite regress of recipients applies to physical bodies, does it not also apply to your spiritual state? Are you waiting for one more experience, one more teacher, one more moment of clarity to change, when the change must begin within you? What is preventing you from being determined in your devotion today?
?
The third possibility is rejected as absurd—that determination comes from an endless chain. Yet, do you live as though your own determination is endlessly postponed? What is the one concrete step you can take right now to break the chain and act on what you know to be true?

The Successive Accident Response and Its Refutation
Objection and answer regarding successive accidents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the response using successive accidents and why the author considers it not beneficial.

Core Idea
A regress of successive accidents is permissible, but it fails to escape the dilemma.

A critic objects that the regress can be avoided by positing a series of successive preparednesses (isti'dadat) that are not simultaneous. The author retorts that this answer is not beneficial because it concedes that determination is by inhering accidents, which leads back to the same problem.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the respondent's answer: the recipient's determination is caused by a sequence of accidents (preparednesses) that are successive, not simultaneous.
Such a regress is considered permissible by some.
2
Identify the author's rebuttal
The author says 'la yajdi' (is not beneficial). Find why: because it admits that determination is by accidents inhering in the recipient.
3
Trace the implication
If determination is by inhering accidents, then those accidents themselves need determination, leading to an infinite regress of accidents, which is not permissible.
This is the core of the refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The circularity you claimed, (and if its individuation) is by another recipient, an infinite regress follows); because we transfer the discussion to the individuation of that other recipient. The conclusion: if your proof were valid that the multiplicity of individuals of the specific essence is only due to its recipient, then an infinite regress of recipients would follow, and a single body would be composed of them, which is absurd. (The answer) to the objection of some virtuous ones (that its determination) i.e., the determination of the recipient is caused by accidents that attach to it due to successive preparednesses ad infinitum) such that each prior preparedness is a preparation for the subsequent, and these preparednesses are not simultaneous but successive, and such a regress is permissible for them (is not beneficial) – predicate of His statement: 'and the answer'. And we only said it is not beneficial because when they allowed its determination) i.e., the determination of the recipient (by what inheres in it) because the purport of what they mentioned is that the cause of the individuation of the recipient is matters inhering in it prior to that individuation, and concurrent with another individuation caused by other matters preceding that other individuation, and so on ad infinitum. Then he said: His statement: (For we transfer the discourse etc. by saying: if its individuation is by its essence, then its limitation follows, and that entails the limitation of the first recipient, which entails the limitation of the essence to one individual; and if by what inheres in it, then circularity follows; and if by another recipient, we transfer the discourse, and so on.) His statement: (That its determination etc.) a detailed answer: if the aforementioned disjunction concerns its individual individuation, then we choose that the cause of its individuation is its very essence and that it is confined to one individual as you know its detail; and if it concerns its specific individuation occurring within the individuals of elemental bodies and the particular celestial orbs, then we say: the particularizer of that individuation is accidents that attach to that recipient, either from the side of the agent only, as in the particular celestial orbs, as will come in the celestial matters; or by consideration of prior accidents that serve as preparations for the attachment of these accidents, necessitating the specification of the recipient and the individuation of its portions; and those accidents do not individuate the essence of the recipient, but it is individuated by itself as you have learned. And then the author's answer is refuted: because you allowed the individuation of hyle by accidents inhering in it, so let that be allowed in the essence; because here there is no individuation of the recipient by what inheres in it, but rather the individuation of its parts by what inheres in itself. So reflect, for this station is among the subtleties.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical exchange on the cause of determination (al-ta'ayyun). It begins by presenting an objection: if determination were caused by the essence, it would limit the essence to one individual; if by a recipient, then either the recipient's determination is by its essence (again limitation) or by another recipient (infinite regress). A respondent (some virtuous one) offers an answer: the recipient's determination is caused by successive accidents (preparednesses) that are not simultaneous, and such a regress is permissible. The author retorts that this answer is not beneficial because it concedes that the recipient's determination is by accidents inhering in it. Since they already allowed this for the recipient, why not allow the same for the essence? The author then provides a detailed counter by distinguishing two types of individuation: individual (al-tashakhkhus al-fardi) and specific (al-tashakhkhus al-takhassusi). For individual individuation, the cause is the essence itself, and it is confined to one individual. For specific individuation (e.g., within elemental bodies or celestial orbs), the cause is accidents that attach to the recipient, either purely from the agent or through a chain of preparatory accidents. Importantly, these accidents do not individuate the essence of the recipient; the recipient is individuated by itself. The author concludes that the initial response is untenable because it treats the individuation of the recipient as by inhering accidents, whereas in reality it is the individuation of its parts. The passage ends with a call for deep reflection.

Key Terms
الاستعدادات المتعاقبة
التسلسل
الجواب
لا يجدي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author say the successive accident response is not beneficial?
A) Because the regress is still infinite
B) Because it concedes determination by inhering accidents
C) Because the preparednesses are not real
D) Because the objection is invalid

Key Takeaway
The successive accident response fails because it still relies on accidents inhering in the recipient, which themselves require determination.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The opponent thought a regress of successive preparednesses was a sufficient explanation. When you make excuses for your own shortcomings, do you ever settle for a chain of justifications that, upon honest examination, still leave you accountable? What would it take to accept that your faults are not just a series of accidents but require a deeper reckoning?
?
The author says the answer 'is not beneficial' because it still relies on inherent accidents. Are there areas in your life where you rely on a series of good deeds or spiritual states to earn Allah's pleasure, forgetting that even those deeds need to be accepted and determined by Him? How does this lesson challenge your reliance on your own efforts?
?
This argument forces you to trace every determination back to a cause. Have you ever truly considered that every aspect of your existence—your personality, your circumstances, your very being—is fully dependent on Allah's determination? Does that thought lead you to humility, or do you still find yourself thinking some things are self-determined?

Individual vs. Specific Individuation: The Resolution
Detailed distinction between individual and specific individuation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between individual and specific individuation and how it resolves the dilemma.

Core Idea
Individual individuation is by essence; specific individuation is by accidents, but those accidents do not individuate the essence itself.

In this detailed answer, the author distinguishes two types of individuation: individual (al-tashakhkhus al-fardi) and specific (al-tashakhkhus al-takhassusi). For individual individuation, the cause is the essence itself. For specific individuation, it is due to accidents attached to the recipient, either from the agent alone or through preparatory accidents. Importantly, these accidents do not individuate the recipient's essence; the recipient is individuated by itself.

Guided Path
1
Understand the distinction
Read the two types of individuation: individual (limited to one person) and specific (occurs within kinds like elements and planets).
2
Identify the cause for each
For individual: essence. For specific: accidents from the agent or preparatory accidents.
Note that the recipient itself is already individuated by its essence.
3
Reflect on the refutation
The author concludes that the opponent's response is refuted because they conflated the individuation of the recipient with the individuation of its parts.
The passage ends with a call for deep reflection.

Source Text

Determination and Its Necessary Concomitant
Objection and refutation on determination's ontological status.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the claim that determination is non-existential because it means negation of another is flawed, and how distinguishing between a thing and its necessary concomitant refutes it.

Core Idea
A thing is not defined by what necessarily accompanies it.

In kalam, the nature of determination (al-ta'yin) is debated. Some argue it is non-existential because its meaning is simply 'not other'. But this confuses the thing itself with a necessary consequence. In this passage, the refutation clarifies the logical distinction between a subject and its concomitant.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the first part of the passage where the objector defines ta'yin as 'it is not other' and concludes it is non-existential.
Notice that the objector takes the definition as the essence.
2
Grasp the refutation
Read the response that distinguishes between ta'yin and its lazim, and note why the conclusion does not follow.
The refutation points out a logical fallacy.
3
Apply the distinction
Reflect on why this logical move is important in kalam reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد يقال في إثبات كون التعين عدمياً: (التعين معناه أنه ليس غيره، وهو سلب لا وجود له في الخارج، ومنع بأن هذا السلب الذي ذكرتموه ليس هو التعين بل هو (لازم) له وليس يلزم من كون اللازم عدمياً كون الملزوم كذلك.
And it has been said in proving that determination is non-existential: "Determination means that it is not other than itself, which is a negation that has no existence in the external world." It is refuted by saying that this negation you mentioned is not determination but a necessary concomitant of it, and from the concomitant being non-existential it does not necessitate the object being non-existential.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage is an objection and answer pair. The objector claims that determination (al-ta'yin) is non-existential (adami) because its meaning is simply 'it is not other than itself', which is a pure negation (salb) with no external existence. The answer (the refutation) responds by distinguishing between determination itself and its necessary concomitant (lazim). The negation of being other is not determination; it is merely something that necessarily accompanies determination. Even if that concomitant is non-existential, it does not imply that the object it accompanies (malzum) is also non-existential. This refutes the argument by showing a logical fallacy: what is true of the concomitant is not automatically true of the subject.

Key Terms
تعين
عدم
سلب
لازم
ملزوم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If something is defined by a negation, then the thing itself must be non-existential.
Correction: A negation can be a necessary concomitant without affecting the ontological status of the subject.

Checkpoint
How does the refutation respond to the claim that determination is non-existential because it means 'not other'?
A) By denying that determination means 'not other'.
B) By asserting that 'not other' is actually existential.
C) By distinguishing between determination and its necessary concomitant.
D) By arguing that all negations are existential.

Key Takeaway
Determination is not defined by the negation of other; it is defined by its own essence, and the negation is only a necessary accompaniment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a time when you judged a person's character based on a single action or trait that you assumed defined them. How might you have confused a necessary concomitant with their essence? What would it look like to separate the two in your heart?
?
Consider your own sense of identity: do you define yourself by what you are not (e.g., 'I am not a hypocrite, not a sinner') rather than who you are in your core? How does this lesson challenge you to ground your identity in a positive reality, especially in relation to your Creator?
?
The objector in this passage made a logical slip that could have led to a false belief about reality. Where in your life have you allowed a quick inference—based on appearances or feelings—to define what is true? What would change if you paused to examine whether you were confusing the concomitant with the thing itself?

Objection on Modalities of Propositions and the Answer
Objection and answer on the nature of the examples, with a note on terminology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the concepts of wujub, imkan, and imtina' differ from the modalities of propositions (jahat al-qadaya), and why the author defined derivatives instead of sources.

Core Idea
The three judgments are more specific than modalities of propositions.

In this passage, an objector argues that the examples used to demonstrate the self-evidence of the three concepts are actually about modalities of propositions (jahat al-qadaya). The answer clarifies that while related, they are not identical: the concepts here are the modalities and matters for specific propositions (those with existence as predicate). This distinction is crucial for understanding the unique nature of these rational judgments. The commentary also addresses why the author defined the derived terms (wajib, mumkin, mumtani') rather than the verbal nouns (wujub, imkan, imtina').

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer carefully
First read the objection: it concedes self-evidence but claims the examples pertain to modalities of propositions. Then read the answer, which refines this claim.
Notice that the objector acknowledges the examples show self-evidence, but raises a technical distinction.
2
Identify the key distinction
The answer states that the concepts here are 'more specific' (أخص). Understand why: they are modalities and matters for specific propositions (with existence as predicate), not modalities in an absolute sense.
The difference lies in the predicates, not in the concept of the modalities themselves.
3
Understand the note on definitions
The commentator notes it would have been better to define the sources (verbal nouns) rather than the derivatives. Reflect on why the author might have chosen derivatives.
The author did not find explicit definitions of the sources in earlier works, so he used derivatives by analogy.
4
Connect to the broader lesson
Consider how this objection and answer reinforce the self-evidence of the three rational judgments: they are distinct from mere modal logic and grounded in necessary knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ألا ترى أن كل عاقل يعلم إلخ) أورد عليه بعد تسليم إفادة بديهية الكنه أن المذكور في هذه الأمثلة جهات القضايا، وسيجيء أن ما نحن فيه غير الجهات والجواب : أن الذي سيجيء هو أنها ليست عين جهات القضايا مطلقاً، بل أخص منها لأنها جهات ومواد لقضايا مخصوصة، كما حققه الشارح فالاختلاف بحسب اختلاف المحمولات لا اختلاف نفس مفهوم هذه الجهات، فبداهتها بداهتها . بحسب قوله : ( ومن رام تعريفها إلخ) كان الأنسب أن يذكر تعريفات المصادر كما يدل عليه عنوان المرصد بمبادئ الاشتقاق وكأن المصنف لم يجد تصريح تعريفات المصادر في كلام القوم، وإنما وجد تعريفات المشتقات فأوردها ليعلم الحال بالمقايسة.
His statement: 'Do you not see that every rational person knows etc.' An objection is raised against it, after conceding that it indicates the self-evidence of the essence, that what is mentioned in these examples are the modalities of propositions, and it will come later that what we are dealing with is other than modalities. The answer: What will come later is that they are not exactly the modalities of propositions absolutely, but more specific than them, because they are modalities and matters for specific propositions, as the commentator (al-Sharih) has verified. So the difference is according to the difference of predicates, not a difference in the very concept of these modalities; thus their self-evidence is the same. According to his statement: (And whoever seeks to define them, etc.), it would have been more appropriate to mention the definitions of the sources (masadir) as indicated by the title of the observatory from the principles of derivation. It seems that the author (al-Musannif) did not find explicit definitions of the sources in the statements of the scholars, but found definitions of the derivatives and thus cited them so that the situation could be known by analogy.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage contains an objection and answer about the examples used to demonstrate the self-evidence of the concepts. The objector grants that the examples show self-evidence but argues that the examples are actually modalities of propositions (jahat al-qadaya), whereas the subject of this discussion is different from those modalities. The answer clarifies that the future discussion will show that the concepts here are not exactly the modalities of propositions in an absolute sense, but more specific: they are the modalities and matters (mawadd) of specific propositions (i.e., with existence as the predicate). The difference lies in the subjects and predicates, not in the very concept of these modalities. Therefore, the self-evidence remains. The commentary then adds a note on the subsequent statement: it would have been more appropriate for the author to define the sources (masadir), i.e., the verbal nouns (wujub, imkan, imtina'), rather than the derived adjectives (wajib, mumkin, mumtani'). But since the author did not find explicit definitions of the sources in the works of earlier scholars, he provided the definitions of the derivatives so that one could infer the source definitions by analogy.

Key Terms
جهات القضايا
مواد
مصادر
مشتقات
بديهية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the concepts of necessity, contingency, and impossibility are the same as the modalities of propositions (e.g., necessity, possibility, impossibility in logic).
Correction: The answer clarifies that they are more specific: they are modalities and matters for propositions that have existence as their predicate, not modalities of propositions in general.

Checkpoint
How does the answer differentiate the concepts under discussion from the modalities of propositions?
A) They are completely different and unrelated.
B) They are more specific, being modalities and matters for specific propositions (with existence as the predicate).
C) They are more general and include all modalities.
D) They are the same but studied from a different perspective.

Key Takeaway
The three rational judgments are more specific than logical modalities because they are tied to existence as a predicate, yet their self-evidence remains unaffected.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When someone raises an objection to something you know is self-evident, like the difference between necessary and contingent, do you instinctively doubt yourself or do you examine the objection carefully? How can you train yourself to distinguish between genuine refinements and mere confusion?
?
The author used derivatives to teach the sources by analogy. Are there foundational concepts in your faith that you have only understood superficially, through secondary sources, without going back to the original proofs? What step can you take today to deepen your understanding of one such concept?
?
You know that nothing can be both necessary and contingent at the same time. Yet in your daily life, do you act as if you are self-sufficient at times? Where are you relying on yourself rather than on the Necessary Being? Write down one area you will consciously surrender today.
